                                            Prompts
                    
                    CRM Database Health Audit - Roadblock Report

                    
                        May 7, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



A Claude prompt that reads your CRM export and produces a one-page report on where an agent is stuck in their pipeline — plus the exact leads they should be calling today. No more staring at a database wondering who to call first. This surfaces the broken metrics (dormancy rate, missed follow-ups, dialer activity), identifies the hottest leads, and writes personalized scripts based on each lead’s actual history.



Agents get decision fatigue from overwhelming databases. Team leaders coach on vibes instead of data. This cuts through both problems with a performance scorecard and action plan that takes 5 minutes to run.



How to Use It




Log into your CRM (Sierra Interactive, Follow Up Boss, kvCORE, etc.).



Pull a full CSV export of the agent’s leads. Include every column your CRM gives you — status, source, last activity, history, visits, properties viewed, tags, notes, dialer activity, all of it. Don’t clean or trim anything.



Open a fresh Claude Cowork chat (one agent per chat).



Drag the CSV file into the chat.



Paste this prompt:





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are my real estate operations analyst. I just uploaded a CSV. It is a full lead export from Sierra Interactive for one of my agents. I have not cleaned or filtered it. Read every row. Cross-reference activity, history, visits, tags, status, and notes on your own.

Produce an Agent Roadblock Report. Use plain English, short sentences, hyphens instead of em-dashes, and a confident, no-fluff tone. Pull every number, name, date, and address straight from the CSV - do not invent anything. If a field is missing, mark it as Unknown rather than skipping it.

The report should be organized into three parts. You can adjust formatting (tables, bullets, paragraphs) to whatever reads cleanest, but make sure all of the following information is captured and clearly presented.

PART 1 - PERFORMANCE SCORECARD
A snapshot of the agent's activity inside Sierra. Include the metrics that are useful for spotting dormancy, missed follow-up, and overall pipeline health. At minimum cover: total database size, dormancy rate (leads with no activity in 90+ days), cold or lost active leads, year-to-date closed transactions and volume, recent session activity, last login, new leads in the last several weeks, leads not yet viewed, time to first email, time to first call, dialer activity, outbound call/text/email counts in the last several weeks, and tasks sitting with no action. Flag each metric as OK, Warning, or Critical based on whether it is healthy, slipping, or genuinely broken. Use your judgment on thresholds based on what looks normal vs. neglected in the data.

PART 2 - HOTTEST LEADS RIGHT NOW
The top handful of leads (5 is a good default) most likely to convert in the near term. For each one, capture name, status, days since last touch, and source. Pick based on a combination of recent engagement signals (visits, properties viewed, replies, lead score, recent activity) and viable status. Rank them in priority order.

PART 3 - PERSONALIZED FOLLOW-UP SCRIPTS
For each of the leads listed in Part 2, give the agent everything they need to make the call. Capture:
Lead name, type (buyer, seller, nurture), and source.
- Phone, email, and location.
- Price band, visit count, and properties viewed.
- Key Intel: a short paragraph pulling specific facts from the CSV - what they clicked, what the agent has already done, dates of last touches, referral source, lead score, anything that explains why this lead is hot or stuck. Use real dates and real properties from the data.
- A recommended script or approach the agent can read off their phone. Reference the last specific interaction. Sound human, not corporate. If the lead has been called multiple times with no callback, pivot to text or email and write the actual message to send.

ASK ME FIRST
Before producing the report, ask:
1. Agent's first and last name.
2. Their role (listing, buyer, dual).
3. Any context I want factoredin (new agent, slump, just back from leave, personal stuff, etc.).

Then read the CSV and produce the report.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






Answer the clarifying questions about the agent.



Claude reads the entire export and produces your report.




Using This with a Different CRM: This prompt is built for Sierra Interactive, but works with any CRM. Just swap “Sierra Interactive” for your platform name and adjust the metrics in Part 1 to match what your system exports. The structure (scorecard, hottest leads, scripts) works the same way.



Tips: Run one agent per chat for clean results. Don’t pre-filter the data — let Claude spot the patterns. Use the performance flags (OK/Warning/Critical) to prioritize coaching conversations. The personalized scripts reference real interactions from the CRM, so they sound natural instead of generic.



Attribution: The Wolfe Team, Jupiter Florida (Erica Wolfe & Alexandra Simon)

                                            Bots
                    
                    Automated BOFU Blogger — Cowork Agent

                    
                        April 20, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



This is a ground-up revision of the Automated BOFU Blogger — rebuilt for Claude Cowork. If you set up the original version with Zapier, Google Sheets, Apps Script, and API keys for OpenAI and Perplexity, that system still works. But this isn’t just the same workflow on a different platform. The research mechanism is fundamentally different, the writing quality is higher, and the entire multi-tool stack has been replaced by a single desktop agent.



What changed — and why it matters: The original BOFU Blogger asked Perplexity for 5 topic ideas in a single API call. That was the entire research step. One prompt, one response, five suggestions. This version replaces that with the same research engine that powers the BOFU Video Engine — it generates 230+ localized search queries tailored to your market and runs them across Google, YouTube, Reddit, Zillow, Realtor.com, Redfin, BiggerPockets, City-Data, Nextdoor, and NerdWallet. It deep-dives into Reddit threads and YouTube comments to extract real questions from real buyers and sellers. Then it scores every discovered topic on five dimensions — inquiry type, decision-stage intent, source confirmation, emotional urgency, and local relevance — before selecting the strongest one to write about. That’s a categorically different level of research.




No Zapier subscription. No OpenAI API key. No Perplexity API key. No Google Sheet. No Apps Script. No RSS feed. No XML export. Everything runs inside Claude — one tool, one subscription.




The BOFU Blogger is a Cowork agent that researches bottom-of-funnel topics in your market, picks the strongest one, checks it against your existing blog, writes a complete SEO/AEO-optimized post, and delivers it — on a schedule, without you lifting a finger.



Here’s what it does on every run:




Refreshes your blog library by scanning your live site — so it always knows what you’ve already published before it does anything else



Generates 230+ localized search queries tailored to your city, neighborhoods, audience, and your state/province’s specific real estate process terminology



Searches 9+ platforms — Google People Also Ask, YouTube, Reddit, Zillow, Realtor.com, Redfin, BiggerPockets, City-Data, Nextdoor, NerdWallet — pulling real questions from real buyers and sellers. The focus is on two types of questions: process questions (“how much are closing costs,” “what happens after the inspection,” “should I sell before buying”) and property questions (“new construction in [neighborhood],” “what does flood zone X mean,” “what’s being built near [development]”). These are the questions people ask when they’re approaching a decision — not casually browsing.



Deep-dives into Reddit threads and YouTube comments to find the exact questions, frustrations, and concerns people express when they’re approaching a real estate decision or navigating one



Scans for current local news — new construction, zoning changes, employer relocations, development activity in your market



Scores every discovered topic on five dimensions — inquiry type, decision-stage intent, how many platforms confirmed it, emotional urgency, and local relevance — then ranks the top 7–10



Checks for duplicates against your existing blog and prior runs — if the top pick overlaps with something you recently published, it logs a recommendation to refresh that existing post (with specific suggestions), skips writing a competing piece, and moves to the next-best topic instead



Writes a complete blog post — SEO title, meta description, an AI snippet summary at the top designed to be pulled by Google AI Overview and other AI search engines, 1,200–1,800 word body, FAQ section, JSON-LD schema markup, internal links to your existing content, CTAs, and author attribution



Delivers it as an HTML file, a Markdown file, and optionally as a Google Doc, a draft on your blog via API connector, or a draft via Chrome — your choice



Notifies you when it’s done — via iMessage, Slack, Zapier, or a file in the folder




You review. You publish. The system handles everything else.




This isn’t a prompt you paste into ChatGPT. It’s a desktop agent — it plans the work, executes every step, saves finished files to your computer, and notifies you when it’s done. You describe it once. It runs on a schedule.





Why bottom-of-funnel? Neil Patel’s research shows AI-driven traffic converts 10–23× better than traditional organic search — but only when the content targets decision-stage queries. Top-of-funnel and middle-of-funnel content gets read by AI and summarized for the consumer. Bottom-of-funnel content gets cited — and the consumer clicks through. That click is your lead.




Fair Housing guardrails are baked in. The system is instructed to avoid topics that reference neighborhood demographics, school quality rankings, or any language that could function as steering. You should still review every post before publishing — AI guardrails reduce risk, but they don’t replace your professional judgment.



Already have the BOFU Video Engine? This uses the same query generator, scorer, and market config — you’ll skip half the setup.







How to Use It



Setup takes about 15–20 minutes. You’ll download the files, run an intake conversation, install your skills, and paste a prompt into Cowork.



You’ll need: the Claude Desktop app (Mac or Windows, any paid plan), a blog or website, and about 10 minutes to answer some questions about your market.







Step 1: Download the Zip File



Download the zip file below and unzip it. Inside you’ll find the system prompt and three skill files that power the engine.



BOFU Blogger DownloadDownload



Contains four files: Claude.md (system prompt), bofu-query-generator (skill), bofu-scorer (skill), and aim-bofu-blog-writer (skill template — personalized during intake). If you already have the BOFU Video Engine installed, you already have the query generator and scorer — overwriting them is harmless.







Step 2: Run the Intake Prompt



Open a regular Claude chat — not Cowork. Before you paste anything, attach one file from the zip: the aim-bofu-blog-writer/SKILL.md template. This is the only file you attach — Claude will personalize it for you during the conversation.



Then copy and paste the intake prompt below into the chat:












	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# BOFU Blogger — Intake Prompt

You are setting up a personalized BOFU Blogger for a real estate agent. The member has downloaded a zip file from the AiM library containing:
- **Claude.md** — the system prompt (goes in their Cowork task folder)
- **bofu-query-generator** skill (goes in their skill library)
- **bofu-scorer** skill (goes in their skill library)
- **aim-bofu-blog-writer** skill template (you will personalize this based on their answers)

**One template file should be attached to this conversation:** `aim-bofu-blog-writer-template.md`. This is the skill you will personalize. The other skills are installed as-is — no personalization needed.

Your job is to:
1. Interview the member to collect their details
2. Personalize the aim-bofu-blog-writer skill from the attached template
3. Generate a complete market-config.md file
4. Generate a Cowork kickoff prompt as copyable text
5. Walk them through setup step by step

If the template file is not attached, tell the member: "I need one file attached to this conversation to get started: `aim-bofu-blog-writer-template.md`. This is the blog-writing skill template I'll personalize for you. You'll find it in the zip file you downloaded. Please attach it and we'll begin."

---

## How This Conversation Works

Ask the questions below in groups. Wait for the member's answers before moving to the next group. Be conversational and brief — don't over-explain. If something needs clarification, keep it to one sentence.

---

## Group 1: Your Market

Ask:
- What country do you work in? (Default to US if not specified — but don't assume.)
- What city and state/province do you work in?
- What's the larger metro area? (e.g., if they say "Franklin, TN" → "Nashville metro")
- What county or region?
- What are 3–5 specific neighborhoods or submar

                                            Bots
                    
                    Cowork Avatar Agent

                    
                        April 9, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



TheCowork Avatar Agent is a Claude Cowork task that takes your BOFU Video Engine results and turns them into finished videos — scripts written in your voice, produced through your HeyGen avatar, and delivered to your computer.



You drop in your BOFU output file, tell the agent which topics to produce, and it handles the rest. It writes the script (short-form or long-form), checks that any data or numbers in the script are accurate, sends it to HeyGen, and brings back the finished video.



The system uses two script-writing skills:




Reel Script Writer — 30–60 second scripts for Instagram Reels, YouTube Shorts, and TikTok. One clean paragraph, teleprompter-ready.



YouTube Script Writer — 5–8 minute scripts for YouTube. Structured with a hook, speaker intro, 2–3 key points, and a CTA — all in natural spoken paragraphs.




Both skills get personalized to your voice, your market, and your brand during setup. The scripts sound like you — not like AI.



A built-in Data Integrity Gate works to prevent the agent from writing scripts with fabricated numbers. If a topic requires market data, closing costs, or other specific figures, the Claude agent searches for verified data first. If it can’t confirm the numbers, it pauses and asks you before writing — so you never end up with a video full of made-up statistics.




Note: The Reel Script Writer in this system is the same skill included in the Claude Skills Agent Starter Pack (from the March 2026 Ai Rookies lecture). If you’ve already installed and personalized that skill, you don’t need to reinstall it — the intake prompt will let you know if your existing version is up to date.








How to Use It



Setup takes about 10–15 minutes. You’ll download a zip file, connect HeyGen, run a setup chat that personalizes everything to your voice, and install the results. A HeyGen account is required for the video production steps — but the script-writing portion works on its own if you’d rather record yourself on camera.







Step 1: Download the Zip File



Download the zip file below and unzip it. Inside you’ll find three shell files that the intake prompt will personalize for you.




Download Cowork Avatar Agent (ZIP)




Contains three shell files: Claude.md (system prompt), Reel Script Writer (skill), and YouTube Script Writer (skill). The intake prompt below will personalize all three.







Step 2: Connect the HeyGen Connector



Before Claude can send scripts to HeyGen, you need to add the HeyGen connector to your Claude app. Here’s how:




Open Claude and click Customize in the left sidebar



Click Connectors



Click the + icon



Select Add Custom Connector



Name it HeyGen



For the remote MCP server URL, enter: https://mcp.heygen.com/mcp/v1



Save the connector




You only need to do this once. If you don’t have a HeyGen account, you can skip this step — the system will still write your scripts, you just won’t get the automated video production.







Step 3: Run the Intake Prompt



Copy the intake prompt below and paste it into a regular Claude chat (not Cowork — just a normal conversation). Attach all three shell files from the zip to the same message.



Claude will ask you four groups of questions:




Who you are — name, title, brokerage, market area



Your voice — how you talk on camera, words you use or avoid, and optionally 2–3 writing samples for voice matching



Your video preferences — which formats you create (YouTube, Reels, Shorts, TikTok), your preferred long-form length, and your default CTA



Your HeyGen setup — avatar, voice, and background settings




When you’re done, Claude generates three personalized files:




Personalized Reel Script Writer — add this to your Claude Cowork skill library



Personalized YouTube Script Writer — add this to your Claude Cowork skill library



Personalized Claude.md — put this in whatever folder on your computer you want to use for this task




To add skills to your library: open Claude, click Customize in the left sidebar, click Skills, click the + button, select Upload a new skill, and drag and drop each file.



Here’s the intake prompt — copy and paste it into Claude (and attach the three shell files):












	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			


# Cowork Avatar Agent — Intake PromptYou are setting up a personalized Cowork Avatar Agent for a real estate agent. The member has already downloaded three shell files from the AiM library:– **Claude.md** — the orchestrator (goes in their Claude Cowork task folder)– **Reel Script Writer** skill (goes in their Claude Cowork skill library)– **YouTube Script Writer** skill (goes in their Claude Cowork skill library)Your job is to ask the right questions, then generate personalized versions of all three files — tailored to this person’s voice, market, brand, and HeyGen setup.Be conversational. Don’t overwhelm them. Ask one group of questions at a time, confirm, then move to the next group.—## Group 1: Who You AreAsk:– What is your full name (as it should appear in your videos)?– What is your title or role? (e.g., REALTOR®, Listing Agent, Broker Associate)– What is your brokerage name?– What city, state/province, and market area do you work in?—## Group 2: Your VoiceAsk:– Describe how you talk on camera in 3–5 words. (Examples: “confident, conversational, sharp” or “warm, friendly, approachable” or “direct, no-nonsense, data-driven”)– Are there any words or phrases you always use — or always avoid? (Examples: always say “reach out,” never say “nestled,” always sign off a certain way)– Do you have 2–3 examples of scripts, captions, or writing that sound like you? If so, paste or upload them. This is optional but dramatically improves voice matching.Note: If the member provides writing samples, analyze their voice patterns — sentence length, phrasing habits, vocabulary choices, rhythm, how they open and close — and weave those patterns into the voice sections of both script skills.—## Group 3: Your Video PreferencesAsk:– What video formats do you create? (YouTube long-form, Instagram Reels, YouTube Shorts, TikTok — pick all that apply)– For long-form videos, what’s your ideal length? (Default is about 6 minutes / ~750 words. Some people prefer shorter at 4–5 minutes, others go 8–10.)– When someone watches your video and wants to take the next step, what do you want them to do? (Schedule a consultation, DM you, visit your website, call/text you, comment a keyword — pick your default)—## Group 4: Your HeyGen SetupAsk:– Do you have a HeyGen account? (This system requires one for video production.)– What is your HeyGen avatar name or ID? (If they don’t know, tell them to open HeyGen, go to Avatars, and find the one they want to use.)– What voice do you use in HeyGen? (Their cloned voice, a stock voice, or they’re not sure?)– Do you use a specific background in your HeyGen videos, or the default?Note: If the member doesn’t have HeyGen set up yet, let them know the script-writing portion of this system works without it — they can write scripts and record themselves on camera instead. The HeyGen integration is optional but requires an account and avatar to be configured.—## After All Groups Are Complete — DeliveryGenerate all three personalized files and present them one at a time. Wait for the member to confirm each one before moving to the next.### File 1: Personalized Reel Script WriterTake the Reel Script Writer shell and personalize it:– Replace voice/tone descriptions with the member’s specific voice descriptors from Group 2– If writing samples were provided, embed analyzed voice patterns into the voice and delivery section– Integrate the member’s default CTA style from Group 3– Add the member’s name and market to examples where applicable**Important:** If the member already has the Reel Script Writer installed from the Claude Skills Agent Starter Pack, tell them: “This is the same Reel Script Writer from the Starter Pack, personalized to match the voice settings you just gave me. If your existing one already matches your voice, you can keep using that one instead — you don’t need to replace it unless you want to update it.”Present the personalized skill and tell the member

                                            Bots
                    
                    BOFU Video Engine – Claude Cowork Agent

                    
                        April 8, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



The BOFU Video Engine is a Claude Cowork agent that finds the exact questions buyers and sellers are asking in your market — and turns them into video ideas that generate inbound leads.



This isn’t a keyword tool. It doesn’t spit out search volume numbers or generic topic suggestions. It mines Google, YouTube, Reddit, Zillow, Realtor.com, Redfin, BiggerPockets, City-Data, Nextdoor, and NerdWallet for real questions from real people who are close to making a decision — the kind of questions that, if you answer them on camera, position you as the agent who gets it.



The engine focuses on two types of questions above all:




Process questions — “how much are closing costs,” “what happens after the inspection,” “should I sell before buying”



Property questions — “new construction in [neighborhood],” “what does flood zone X mean,” “what’s being built near [development]”




These are the questions people ask when they’re in a transaction or about to be — not when they’re casually browsing. That’s what makes them bottom-of-funnel.



Every search is localized to your city, your neighborhoods, your state/province’s specific process terminology. Every output includes a video title, a hook, a CTA suggestion matched to your preferred lead-capture method, and a source signal showing where the question appeared. The engine also scans for current local news and development activity on every run — new subdivisions, employer relocations, zoning changes — so your content stays current automatically.



Fair Housing guardrails are baked in. The engine should never suggest topics that reference neighborhood demographics, school quality rankings, or any language that functions as steering. It’s designed to keep you compliant without you having to think about it.







How to Use It



Setup takes about 10 minutes. You’ll download a zip file, install two skills, run a quick setup chat, and you’re ready to go.







Step 1: Download the Zip File



Download the zip file below and unzip it. Inside you’ll find the system prompt and two skill files that power the engine.




Download BOFU Video Engine (ZIP)




Contains three files: Claude.md (system prompt), bofu-query-generator (skill), and bofu-scorer (skill). Setup instructions below.







Step 2: Place the Claude.md File



Take the Claude.md file from the zip and put it in whatever folder on your computer you want to use for this task. This is the folder you’ll point Claude Cowork to later.







Step 3: Install the Two Skills



The two skill files need to be added to your Claude skill library. Here’s how:




Open Claude and click Customize in the left sidebar



Click Skills



Click the + button



Select Upload a new skill



Drag and drop the bofu-query-generator SKILL.md file and save



Repeat for the bofu-scorer SKILL.md file




That’s it — the skills are installed. You only need to do this once.







Step 4: Run the Intake Prompt



Copy the intake prompt below and paste it into a regular Claude chat (not Cowork — just a normal conversation). Claude will ask you four groups of questions about your market, your audience, your local process, and your content preferences — including which video formats you create (YouTube long-form, Shorts, Instagram Reels, TikTok) so the engine tailors its search and output to match.



When you’re done, Claude gives you two things:




market-config.md — your personalized market details. Download this file and put it inside a references/ folder within the same folder where your Claude.md file is.



Your kickoff prompt — copy this and save it somewhere handy. This is what you’ll paste into Claude Cowork every time you run the engine.




Your folder should now look like this:



your-folder/
├── Claude.md
└── references/
    └── market-config.md



Here’s the intake prompt — copy and paste it into Claude:












	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			


# BOFU Video Engine — Intake PromptYou are setting up a personalized BOFU Video Engine for a real estate agent. The member has already downloaded three files from the AiM library:– **Claude.md** — the system prompt (goes in their Claude Cowork task folder)– **bofu-query-generator** skill (goes in their Claude Cowork skill library)– **bofu-scorer** skill (goes in their Claude Cowork skill library)Your job is to ask the right questions, then generate two personalized files:1. A completed **market-config.md** — the member’s localized market details2. A **kickoff prompt** — what the member pastes into Claude Cowork to start a runBe conversational. Don’t overwhelm them. Ask one group of questions at a time, confirm, then move to the next group.—## Group 1: Your MarketAsk:– What country do you work in? (Default to US if not specified — but don’t assume.)– What city and state/province do you work in?– What’s the larger metro area? (e.g., if they say “Franklin, TN” → “Nashville metro”)– What county or region?– What are 3–5 specific neighborhoods or submarkets you focus on? (The ones you’d want to be known for.)– Is anything happening locally right now that buyers or sellers are talking about? New construction developments, school changes, zoning issues, major employers moving in, road projects, anything?—## Group 2: Your AudienceAsk:– Do you primarily work with buyers, sellers, or both?– What property types do you focus on? (Single family, condos, townhomes, new construction, luxury, investment, land — pick all that apply.)– What’s your typical price range? (Give me a low end and a high end.)—## Group 3: Your Local ProcessAsk:– In your state/province, who handles the closing — a title company, an attorney, an escrow company, or something else?– Are there any state/provincial or local transfer taxes when selling a home? If so, what are they called locally?– What’s the standard seller disclosure form called in your area?– Are there any other jurisdiction-specific process terms or steps that are unique to how real estate works where you are?Note: If the member doesn’t know these answers, look them up based on their state/province. Most agents know the basics — they may just not know the formal terminology.—## Group 4: Your ContentAsk:– Where are you creating content? YouTube, Instagram Reels, TikTok, or a combination?If they say Instagram or TikTok:– Do you use ManyChat for comment-to-DM automations?Then ask:– When someone watches your video and wants to take the next step, what do you want them to do? Pick all that apply:  – DM you for a specific resource (if so, what resource? e.g., “seller net sheet,” “buyer guide,” “home search portal”)  – Schedule a consultation or call  – Visit your website  – Follow / like / subscribe  – Comment a keyword to trigger a DM  – Call or text you directly  – Something else?—## After All Groups Are Complete — Two-Stage DeliveryDeliver the personalized files in two separate responses. Wait for the member to confirm they’ve completed each step before moving to the next one.### Stage 1: Market ConfigGenerate the **market-config.md** file filled in with all of the member’s answers from Groups 1–4.Use this structure:“`# BOFU Video Engine — Market Configuration## Location– **Country:** [answer]– **State / Province:** [answer]– **County / Region:** [answer]– **City:** [answer]– **Metro Area:** [answer]– **Key Neighborhoods:** [answer]– **Local Subreddits:** [research and suggest relevant local subreddits based on their city/metro]– **Local Hot Topics:** [answer]## Audience– **Primary Audience:** [answer]– **Property Types:** [answer]– **Price Range:** [answer]## Jurisdiction-Specific Process Terms– **Closing Entity:** [answer]– **Common Contingencies:** [answer or default: Inspection, appraisal, financing, sale of home]– **Transfer Tax Term:** [answer]– **Disclosure Requirements:** [answer]– **Jurisdiction-Specific Terms:** [answer]## Content Preferences– **Primary Platform:** [answer]– **ManyChat Active:** [answer — only if platform includes Instagram or TikTok]– **Preferred CTA Types:** [answer]– **Lead Magnets Available:** [answer or “None specified”]“`Tell the member:“Here’s your personalized market config file. Download it.This file goes inside a `references/` fol

                                            Bots
                    
                    Talking Head Video Editor AI Agent

                    
                        April 8, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



Turn a raw talking head recording into a polished, captioned video — without manually scrubbing through takes, hunting for filler words, or hand-placing captions.



This system turns Claude Cowork into your video editor. Here’s what’s happening under the hood: Claude connects to Descript — a video editing app that lets you edit video by editing text — and talks directly to Descript’s built-in AI editor called Underlord. Underlord is a chatbot inside Descript that has full editing permissions — it can cut, rearrange, add captions, reframe, and export your video. What this system does is put Claude in charge of that conversation. Two AI bots, chatting edits back and forth, while you stay in the loop on the decisions that matter.



You paste a Descript project link into Cowork, answer a few quick questions, and Claude handles the rest:




Rough-cuts the video — finds the best takes, removes the bad ones



Verifies every line against your script so nothing important gets cut



Cleans up filler words and dead air



Adds branded captions with active word highlighting



Applies zoom cuts and intro/outro fades



Reframes for vertical or horizontal



Exports an MP4 to your Downloads folder




It gets you 85–90% of the way to a finished edit. Not perfect — you still review the framing, eyeball the captions, and make final tweaks in Descript. But it compresses what used to be 30–60 minutes of manual editing into a few minutes of AI-assisted work. Claude asks you to verify visuals before exporting, but the tedious part — finding best takes, removing bad ones, syncing captions — is automated.



This is built for talking head videos — one speaker, one camera, scripted content recorded off a teleprompter. It could work for multi-speaker recordings like interviews too, but it’s optimized for the solo talking head workflow.



If you’ve used the Video Rough-Cut Editor Prompt, you already know the concept — paste a prompt into Underlord, get a rough cut back. This workspace takes it further. Instead of stopping at the rough cut, Claude runs the entire pipeline: rough cut, script verification, cleanup, captions, zoom cuts, reframe, and export. And instead of you driving the conversation with Underlord, Claude handles that for you.




Tip: For the best results, open Descript’s settings and set Underlord’s model to Claude Opus 4.6. This gives Underlord the strongest reasoning for complex editing decisions like selecting the best take from multiple options.








What You’ll Need




Claude Pro or Team plan with the Claude desktop app — Cowork is a mode inside the desktop app that lets Claude work on files and folders on your computer. It only runs onthe desktop app (not the website or mobile app) because it needs access to your local machine. You’ll point it at a folder, and Claude can read and work with anything inside it.



Descript account with AI credits — any paid plan works (Hobbyist, Creator, or Business). The free plan includes Underlord access too, but AI credits are limited. Each edit uses roughly 11–14 credits, so check your plan’s monthly allowance and plan accordingly.








How to Use It



Setup takes about 10 minutes. After that, every edit starts with a single link.







Step 1: Connect Descript to Claude



This step connects Claude to Descript so the two can talk to each other. You only need to do this once.




Open the Claude desktop app.



In the left sidebar, click Customize.



Click Connectors.



Click the + button to add a connector. Descript isn’t in the directory yet, so choose Add Custom Connector.



For the name, type Descript. For the Remote MCP Server URL, paste: https://api.descript.com/v2/mcp



Click Add, then click Connect. You’ll be prompted to sign into Descript and click “Allow” to give Claude permission to edit on your behalf.




Once connected, you should see Descript listed under your connectors. That’s it — Claude can now send editing instructions to Descript’s Underlord.







Step 2: Install the Two Skills



Skills are instruction files that teach Claude how to do specific jobs. This system uses two of them — one that contains the editing pipeline and one that teaches Claude how to talk to Underlord. They’re bundled together in a single download.




Download Skills (ZIP)




Contains two files: talking-head-editor and underlord-capabilities. Install each one separately — instructions below.



Unzip the download. You’ll see two markdown files. Install each one:




Open the Claude desktop app.



In the left sidebar, click Customize.



Click Skills.



Click the + button, then choose Create a Skill.



Click Upload a Skill, then drag and drop the markdown file.



Click Save.




Do this for both files. Once saved, these skills are permanent — they’ll be there every time you use Claude.







Step 3: Generate Your Personal Settings File



The connector tells Claude how to reach Descript. The skills tell Claude what to do. This step tells Claude who you are — your brand colors, fonts, and editing preferences so every video comes out looking like yours.



You’re going to generate a file called CLAUDE.md. Think of it like a settings file — Claude reads it at the start of every editing session to know your brand kit, your default recording style, your pacing preference, and your preferred output format. You create it once, and it applies to every video you edit.



Copy the intake prompt below and paste it into a new Claude chat (not Cowork — just a regular chat). Claude will ask you five quick questions, then generate your personalized CLAUDE.md file. The whole thing takes about two minutes.














	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

I need you to help me set up a Cowork workspace for automated talking head video editing. You’re going to ask me a few quick questions, then generate a personalized CLAUDE.md file I’ll put in my workspace.Here’s the template with placeholders. Your job is to ask me the questions below, then output the completed file with my answers filled in.TEMPLATE:# Talking Head Video Editor — Cowork WorkspaceYou are a talking head video editor. This workspace edits talking head videos in Descript using the Underlord AI agent via the Descript MCP connector.—## TriggerWhen the user provides a Descript project link (e.g., https://web.descript.com/…), start the talking head editing workflow using the talking-head-editor skill.Before starting the edit, ask these quick questions (skip any the user already answered):1. “Was this recorded {{DEFAULT_RECORDING_STYLE}}? Or did you do it differently this time?”2. “Do you have the script you were reading? Pasting it here helps me verify the edit doesn’t accidentally cut real content.”3. “Horizontal (16:9), vertical (9:16), or both?” (Skip if the user’s default covers it and they didn’t say otherwise.)Then run the full pipeline from the talking-head-editor skill.If the user comes back with another video in the same session, repeat the questions above. All brand preferences carry over automatically.—## Brand Kit### Colors| Name | Hex | Usage ||——|—–|——-|| Primary | {{PRIMARY_COLOR}} | Active word highlight in captions, accent elements || Secondary | {{SECONDARY_COLOR}} | Caption background, secondary accents || Tertiary | {{TERTIARY_COLOR}} | Call-to-action emphasis (optional) || Text Dark | {{TEXT_DARK_COLOR}} | Dark text, dark backgrounds || Text Light | {{TEXT_LIGHT_COLOR}} | Light text, caption text on dark backgrounds |### Fonts| Font | Usage ||——|——-|| {{FONT_PRIMARY}} | Headings, captions, on-screen text || {{FONT_SECONDARY}} | Body text, secondary text, fallback |### Caption Style– Font: {{FONT_PRIMARY}} Bold– Text color: {{TEXT_LIGHT_COLOR}}– Active word highlight: {{PRIMARY_COLOR}}– Background: Semi-transparent {{TEXT_DARK_COLOR}} at 80% opacity, rounded corners– Position: Bottom center for horizontal; lower third for vertical (roughly 70% from top — above the IG/YT Shorts/TikTok UI zone but low enough to look natural)– Animation: Word-by-word highlight (active word changes color as spoken)—## Editing Preferences– Default recording style: {{DEFAULT_RECORDING_STYLE}}– Dead air threshold: {{DEAD_AIR_THRESHOLD}

                                            Bots
                    
                    15 Custom GPTs and Gems Every Real Estate Agent Should Build

                    
                        April 1, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



A complete playbook for turning your 15 most repetitive marketing tasks into Custom GPTs (ChatGPT) and Gems (Gemini) that run on repeat. Each one produces a specific, finished asset — not brainstorming, not ideas, but deliverables you’d otherwise spend hours creating from scratch.



Every recurring marketing task you do can become a Custom GPT or Gem that performs that task to your exact spec, every single time. Set it up once. It remembers how you want it done — your brand, your voice, your formatting preferences, your compliance requirements. No more re-explaining yourself in every chat.



Custom GPTsGemsPlatformChatGPTGeminiRequiresChatGPT Plus ($20/mo) or higherFree Google account (Gemini Advanced recommended)Image generationImage 1.5Nano Banana 2Video generationSora – coming soonVeo 3Search/Deep researchModerateStrongHow to buildWrite instructions + upload files → save as Custom GPTWrite instructions + upload files → save as Gemini Gem



Which one should you use? Depends on the task. Some features are platform-exclusive — image generation works differently on each, Gemini has Veo for video and stronger web search. Each entry below notes which platform works best. When both work equally well, pick whichever you’re more comfortable with.



New to building these? These AiM resources will get you started:




How to Create a ChatGPT Custom GPT — step-by-step setup from scratch



Custom GPTs vs. Projects — which format fits which task



GPTs for Everyday Marketing — the Ai Rookie lecture that covers what custom GPTs are and why they matter for your marketing








Quick Reference



Use this table to find the GPT or Gem you need and see which platforms support it. Scroll down for full details, system instructions, and linked resources.







#GPT / GemChatGPTGeminiOther1Email Newsletters✅—Claude (recommended for HTML)2Blog Posts✅ (recommended)✅Claude3Social Captions✅✅Claude4Carousel Design✅ (image 1.5)✅ (Nano Banana 2)—5Thumbnails & Covers—✅ (Nano Banana 2)—6Branded Stats Graphics—✅ (Nano Banana 2)—7Property Flyers✅ (image 1.5)✅ (Nano Banana 2)—8Listing Remarks✅ (recommended)✅Claude9Photo Captions✅ (required)——10Listing Motion—✅ (Veo 3 only)—11Video Scripts✅ (recommended)✅Claude12Ad Creative (Meta)✅✅Claude12Ad Creative (Google)✅✅Claude13Market Analysis✅ (recommended)—Claude14Area Research✅✅Perplexity, Grok15Property Intel✅✅Perplexity, Grok + NotebookLM












1. Email Newsletter Generator



Writes your weekly or monthly email campaigns start to finish — layout, copy, subject lines, and platform-ready code or text you can paste directly into your email provider. Works on ChatGPT or Gemini.




Note: Claude is the strongest option for coding HTML emails — but since this guide focuses on Custom GPTs and Gemini Gems specifically, the resources below are built for those platforms. If you use Claude, the same system instructions work in a Claude Project or Skill.




AiM resources cover this one completely. Pick the one that fits your email style:




HTML/CSS Email Newsletter Generator — Fully designed, branded HTML newsletters with your colors, fonts, images, and buttons. Adapts to your email platform (Mailchimp, Follow Up Boss, Flodesk, etc.).



Plain-Text Email Newsletter Generator — Conversational, no-design-needed newsletters. Handles merge tags, spam filter avoidance, and platform formatting.



HTML Market Update Email Newsletter — Market update emails specifically. Upload MLS data, get a designed HTML email with charts and data narrative.



Personalized Market Update Email Built from MLS Data — Builds a personalized market update email from your MLS export. More text-forward than the HTML version above.



Listing Announcement Email Blast — A one-off branded HTML email for a new listing announcement (not a recurring newsletter — a single campaign).




Each resource page includes complete system instructions you can copy and paste into a Custom GPT, Gem, or Claude Project.








2. Blog Post Writer



Turns any topic, transcript, or keyword data into a publish-ready blog post — SEO-optimized, locally relevant, and written in your voice. Best on ChatGPT (recommended for web research capability) or Claude.



AiM resources cover this one completely:




Custom GPT That Writes Your Blogs — The primary tool. Handles five blog types (local area, market insights, buyer/seller advice, listing spotlights, repurposed video), includes compliance guardrails, and walks you through every decision. Available as a pre-built GPT you can launch instantly or system instructions you can customize.



Automated BOFU Blogger — System Setup — The full setup guide for building an automated bottom-of-funnel blog system. This connects your keyword data to an AI writing pipeline that produces hyper-local, search-optimized blog posts on repeat.



Blog Posts from Seller Search Trends — Two-prompt system: generates 50 localized blog titles from keyword data, then expands any title into a full post.









3. Social Caption Writer



Writes post copy matched to any platform — Instagram, Facebook, LinkedIn, or X. Adjusts length, tone, hashtag strategy, and formatting for each one. Works on ChatGPT or Gemini.



This one is new. No existing AiM resource covers a general-purpose social caption GPT, so here are the system instructions to build one. Upload 5–10 of your best past captions or transcripts to the GPT’s Knowledge section — that’s how it learns your voice.














	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## PurposeYou write **platform-optimized social media captions** for a real estate professional. Every caption is on-brand, engagement-driven, and ready to paste. You adapt length, tone, structure, and formatting to the specific platform and post format.—## Behavior Overview### TriggerWhen the user says something like:– “Write a caption for [topic]”– “Post this on Instagram”– “I need social copy for [listing / stat / event]”– “Caption for all platforms”Begin the caption workflow. If no platform is specified, ask which one(s) they want before writing.### Voice MatchingIf writing samples have been uploaded to the Knowledge section, **analyze them and match the user’s unique voice, tone, and diction as closely as possible.** All captions must reflect this style consistently. If no samples are uploaded, write in a conversational, confident tone — professional but not corporate. The user’s explicit style requests always take priority over uploaded samples.—## Intake FlowAsk the user for the following in one message:> To write your caption, I need a few quick details. Reply with whatever you’ve got:>> – Topic or content idea (listing, market stat, event, tip, behind-the-scenes, etc.)> – Platform(s): Instagram, Facebook, LinkedIn, X, or “all”> – Tone preference (optional): educational, conversational, bold, luxury, casual> – Call to action (optional): comment, DM, link in bio, share, save> – Any hashtags, keywords, or phrases to include> – What’s the visual? (photo, carousel, Reel, text graphic — helps me match the copy to the format)If some details are missing, proceed with what is provided — just acknowledge anything that’s unclear or skipped.**CRITICAL — If the user provides all the info upfront in a single message, do NOT ask them to repeat it.** Acknowledge what they gave you and go straight to writing.—## Writing the Opening LineThe opening line is the most important line in every caption on every platform. It’s what shows before the truncation (“…more” on Instagram, “see more” on LinkedIn). Bad opens = nobody reads the rest. Get this wrong and nothing else matters.**Strong opens:**– Lead with a benefit or insight, not a setup (“Email outperforms every social platform you’re on” not “I wanted to share something about email”)– State something bold or contrarian (“Strategy beats spend” not “Strategy can sometimes be important”)– Ask a real question that makes them think (“What would it look like if you never wrote a listing description from scratch again?” not “Have you ever thought about using AI?”)– Reference something timely — a tool update, market shift, or behavioral insight**Weak opens to avoid:**

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Video Rough-Cut Editor Prompt

                    
                        March 25, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


A paste-ready prompt that turns Descript’s Underlord into your rough cut editor. Drop it in before you start editing, and the AI will scan your raw talking head footage — find the best takes, cut the bad ones, remove filler words, strip dead air, and even follow your verbal directions if you gave any during recording — as in, you said something like: “Use that last take.” It’s the first 80-90% of your edit, done in seconds.




This prompt is built for a specific recording style: scripted talking head videos where you repeat lines to get the best delivery. Whether you’re reading off a teleprompter, working from bullet points, or freestyling with retakes — if your raw footage has multiple attempts at the same lines, this is for you.




Video builds authority faster than any other content format. When someone watches you break down a market trend, walk through a listing strategy, or explain what buyers and sellers need to know right now — you become the expert they trust. That’s true whether it’s a 60-second Reel, a YouTube Short, or a 10-minute deep dive. The agents who post consistently are the ones who stay top-of-mind.



Here’s the problem: most agents know they should be posting more video. They have the ideas. They can record just fine. But the editing kills them. Not the creative part — the tedious part. Scrubbing through 15 minutes of raw footage to find the three good takes. Cutting the six bad ones. Trimming the dead air. Removing the “ums.” That rough cut phase is where videos go to die on a hard drive.



This prompt hands that entire job to Descript’s built-in AI editor: Underlord. You still do the creative polish — transitions, animations, music. But the grunt work of assembling the rough cut from raw footage? That’s handled.



If you’ve used Gling.ai (covered in the AI Video Editing Shortcuts lecture), you already know the concept — AI that finds and removes bad takes. This prompt does something similar, but inside Descript where you’re already editing, and it can follow your verbal directions mid-recording, which Gling can’t.







How to Use It



Record your video. Repeat lines as many times as you need until you’re happy with the delivery. Don’t worry about mistakes — the AI will sort it out.



Go to descript.com and log in (or open the Descript desktop app). A free account works for this.



Create a new project. In the left sidebar, click Projects, then New Project → Video Project.



Upload your raw footage. Drop your video file into the project. Descript will automatically transcribe it — this is what Underlord reads to make its editing decisions.



After the transcription is autogenerated, open Underlord. Look for the button in the lower-right corner of the screen. It opens a chatbot. You’ll see a model selector — it defaults to Auto, but you can choose a specific model. We recommend Claude Opus 4.6 for the most accurate results with this prompt. 



Copy the prompt below. Before you paste it, read the two recording style options inside the prompt and delete the one that doesn’t match how you recorded.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are a talking head video editor. Your job is to create a clean rough cut from this raw footage. The speaker recorded a scripted video and repeated lines multiple times to get the best delivery. Your job is to keep only the best take of each line and remove everything else.

RECORDING STYLE:
>>> IMPORTANT: Delete one of the two options below before pasting this prompt. Keep the one that matches how the video was recorded. <<<

OPTION A — LINE BY LINE: The speaker read one line at a time off a teleprompter, repeated it until they were happy, then moved to the next line. Duplicate takes of the same idea will be clustered together in the timeline.

OPTION B — FULL SCRIPT PASSES: The speaker read the entire script from top to bottom multiple times. Duplicate takes of the same idea will be spread across the timeline — the first attempt of each line will appear early, and later attempts will appear later in the footage.

DIRECTOR CUES — HIGHEST PRIORITY:
The speaker sometimes talks to the editor mid-recording. These are commands, not content. Look for phrases like: "let me do that again," "one more time," "scratch that," "use that one," "go with that take," "that was good," "that's the one," "take two," "from the top," "all right, that one's done," or any moment where the speaker is clearly addressing the editor rather than the audience. When you find a director cue:
- If it's a REDO signal ("let me do that again"), cut the bad take AND the cue itself. Keep the next attempt.
- If it's a KEEP signal ("use that one," "that was good"), keep the take they're referring to. Cut the others.
- If it's a CUT signal ("editor cut this," "don't use that"), remove what they're pointing to.
- The audience should never hear any director cue in the final edit.

DUPLICATE TAKES — WHEN NO DIRECTOR CUE EXISTS:
When the speaker says the same idea multiple times and gives no verbal instruction about which to keep:
- Keep the take with the fewest filler words
- Keep the take that completes the full thought (incomplete takes lose)
- Keep the take with the cleanest, most concise phrasing
- If it's a coin flip, keep the LAST take

REPEATED LINES WITHIN A SINGLE TAKE:
Sometimes the speaker repeats a line within the same continuous take — they say "not because it's hard" twice in a row without stopping. When this happens, keep ONLY the first clean instance of the line and cut where the repetition begins. Do NOT remove the entire take — surgically cut the repeated portion.

FILLER WORDS:
Remove all "um," "uh," "like" (when used as filler, not comparison), "you know," "I mean," "so yeah," and false starts where a sentence begins and is immediately abandoned.

DEAD AIR:
Remove all silence gaps longer than 1 second between lines.

NOT PART OF THE SCRIPT:
Any moment where the speaker breaks character — laughing at themselves, sighing, reacting to a mistake, talking under their breath, commenting on their own performance, or addressing someone off-camera — is NOT content. Cut these moments along with the bad takes they accompany. If it sounds like the speaker stepped out of "presenter mode," it's not part of the video.

CRITICAL RULES:- Never remove a line that is only said once. If the speaker makes a point only one time, it stays even if the delivery is imperfect.
- Every distinct idea in the video must be represented in the final cut. Do not drop entire topics.
- When cutting a repeated line within a take, make the cut mid-block — do not delete the entire block.
- Close all gaps so the kept sections play back to back smoothly.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






Paste the prompt into Underlord and send. It will scan your transcript and start making cuts across the timeline. Give it a minute to work.



Review and refine in the chat. This is the most important step. The first pass gets you about 85–90% of the way. After Underlord finishes, stay in the chat and ask: “Did you remove any lines that were only said once? Walk me through what you kept and what you cut.” If it dropped something it shouldn’t have, just tell it — “You removed the line about CapCut, put that back” or “That take at 0:45 was the good one, keep that instead.” You’re in a conversation. Work through it until the rough cut feels right.



Make your polish pass. Once the rough cut is clean, add transitions, captions, punch-ins, music, and color. That’s the creative work — and it goes fast when the rough cut is already done. (Btw, Underlord can help with some of these tasks too!)




If you’re new to Descript, watch AI Video Editing Shortcuts first — it walks through the tool and how to get set up.

                                            Guides
                    
                    Build a Client Resource Library with NotebookLM

                    
                        March 23, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                

Give Your Clients an AI Assistant Trained on Your Expertise



In February 2026, Zillow partnered with Google to launch a featured notebook in NotebookLM — a “Buying Your First Home” guide that buyers can chat with, listen to, and explore on their own. (Try it here.) If Zillow thinks this is worth building for their audience, imagine what it could do for yours — except your version isn’t generic. It’s built from your market knowledge, your process, and your expertise.



Your clients have questions. Lots of them. And most of those questions aren’t urgent — they’re the kind of thing people Google at 10 PM on a Tuesday. What if you could text them a link to an interactive, AI-powered resource — built from your expertise — that they could chat with, listen to, quiz themselves on, and explore whenever they wanted?



That’s what NotebookLM does. You feed it your sources — articles, documents, transcripts, your own notes — and it becomes an AI assistant that only knows what you told it. 



No hallucinations. No wandering off-topic. Everything it generates is grounded in the sources you gave it. And when you share a notebook with a client, they don’t just get a static document. They get the whole thing — they can ask it questions in chat, generate audio overviews to listen to on their commute, compile reports, generate explainer videos, and more. All they need is a free Google account (which most people already have).



This guide walks you through five notebooks you can build and share with clients today:




Architectural Styles & Home Elevations — so buyers know what they’re looking for before you start touring.



Pre-Listing Prep & Curb Appeal — so sellers know what to fix, paint, and stage before the photographer shows up.



What to Expect During Escrow — so first-time buyers stop calling you at 9 PM with questions.



Neighborhood Comparisons — so relocation clients can research areas on their own schedule.



Your Listing, Interactive — so buyers and showing agents arrive already engaged with your property.




Before You Start



What you’ll need:




A free Google account (NotebookLM is free at notebooklm.google.com)



Access to an AI tool with deep research or long-form output — Gemini, Perplexity, ChatGPT, Grok, or Claude all work



For Notebook #3: an AI tool with voice mode (Gemini recommended — it has a 1 million token context window, so long voice conversations won’t hit any limits)



15–20 minutes per notebook




How NotebookLM works (the 2-minute version):




Go to notebooklm.google.com and sign in with your Google account.



Click New Notebook.



Add sources — you can paste text, upload PDFs, add Google Docs, drop in website URLs, or link YouTube videos.



Once your sources are loaded, the notebook becomes an interactive AI resource. It can generate audio overviews (podcast-style—meaning, listen on the go), FAQs, study guides, mind maps, timelines, briefing docs, quizzes, slideshows, explainer videos, and more — all grounded in your sources.



Hit Share, set access to “Anyone with a link,” and send that link to your client. They open it with their Google account and get full access to chat with the notebook, generate outputs, and explore everything you built — on their own time, at their own pace.Note: They’re view-only, so they can’t change your sources or mess anything up. They can only interact with what you’ve built.




You’re not sending them a PDF. You’re giving them a personal research assistant trained on your expertise. The rest of this guide is about building great sources for five specific use cases. Each notebook below is its own section — expand the one you want to build and follow the steps.







Notebook #1: Help Buyers Identify What They Want



Architectural Styles & Home Elevations — for buyers who don’t yet have the vocabulary to describe the home they’re looking for.



You’re giving them a self-guided education on home styles — Colonial, Craftsman, Mid-Century Modern, Ranch, Tudor, Contemporary, and everything in between. They browse it, figure out what they’re drawn to, and come to your first showing with clarity instead of “I’ll know it when I see it.”



Step 1: Generate your source document.Open Gemini (gemini.google.com), Perplexity (perplexity.ai), or your preferred AI research tool. Before you paste the prompt below, make sure you select the Deep Research option in the message box — this tells the AI to do a thorough, multi-source research pass rather than a quick answer.



Fill in the placeholder first, then paste the prompt and run it:




[YOUR CITY/REGION] — Your market area. Be specific. “Nashville, Tennessee” or “Greater Orlando” works better than just a state name.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Create a comprehensive guide to residential architectural styles commonly found in [YOUR CITY/REGION]. For each style, include:

- The style name and any common regional variations or nicknames
- A physical description of the exterior: roof shape, facade materials, window styles, door placement, porch or entryway features, and overall proportions
- The era when this style was most popular and any historical context
- Interior layout characteristics buyers can expect (open vs. compartmentalized floor plans, ceiling heights, typical room flow)
- Common updates or renovations homeowners make to modernize the style
- Price range context for [YOUR CITY/REGION] — where these homes typically fall relative to the broader market

Styles to cover (include all that are relevant to [YOUR CITY/REGION] and skip any that aren't common locally):
Colonial, Cape Cod, Ranch, Split-Level, Craftsman/Bungalow, Tudor, Victorian, Queen Anne, Mid-Century Modern, Contemporary/Modern, Mediterranean/Spanish Revival, French Country, Farmhouse (traditional and modern), Townhouse/Rowhome, A-Frame, Log Home, Cottage, Georgian, Federal, Prairie, Art Deco, Coastal/Beach, Southwest/Adobe, Plantation

Write this for a homebuyer audience — no jargon, no academic language. The tone should be friendly and informative, like a knowledgeable friend explaining what to look for. Use vivid descriptions that help someone picture the home from the street.

Format the guide so each style is its own clearly labeled section. End with a "How to Use This Guide" section that encourages the buyer to screenshot or bookmark the styles they're most drawn to and share them with their agent.

Include a brief contact section at the end with [YOUR NAME], [YOUR BROKERAGE], and [YOUR PHONE/EMAIL] so anyone exploring the guide knows who built it and how to reach you.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	









Step 2: Review the output and add it to NotebookLM.Read through the research output before you paste it in. Does it cover the styles that are common in your market? Does anything look off or missing? Edit as needed — this is your source of truth, so make sure you’re happy with it.



Once it looks good, open your notebook in NotebookLM and click Add Source → Pasted Text. Drop the full output in and give it a clear name like “Architectural Styles Guide.”



Step 3 (Optional): Add a second source.If your MLS lets you save filtered searches by architectural style, export a PDF of sample listings for 3–4 popular styles in your market. Upload those PDFs as additional sources. This adds real, local listing examples to the notebook — but the research output alone is enough to get started.



Step 4: Share the notebook.Generate an audio overview or FAQ to seed the notebook with something your client can explore right away — then hit Share → “Anyone with a link” and text them the link. They can chat with it, generate their own study guides, listen to audio overviews, and dig deeper into any style that catches their eye.



Make it yours. This notebook gets stronger with more sources. What else would help your buyers? A PDF from a local architecture walking tour? A blog post you’ve written about popular home styles in your market? A YouTube video of you walking through different neighborhoods and pointing out the styles? Think about what you already have — or what you could create — and add it in. The notebook works with whate

                                            Guides
                    
                    Claude Cowork: YouTube to Blog Agent

                    
                        March 17, 2026                    
                
            
        

        
            
                
What This Is



You’re about to set up an AI agent that turns your YouTube videos into blog posts — automatically, every day, while you’re doing something else entirely.



By the end of this guide, you’ll have a system that checks your channel for new videos, writes SEO-optimized blog posts from the transcripts, saves them to your computer, and messages you when they’re ready to review. You describe it once. It runs every day.



You’ll need four things: the Claude Desktop app (Mac or Windows, any paid plan), the Claude in Chrome extension, a YouTube channel, and a blog.



You’re already sharing videos. That content has real value. But right now, the only people finding it are the ones watching on YouTube. A blog post takes that same video and puts it somewhere else (that Google indexes), AI models cite, and potential clients discover when they search for exactly what you’re talking about. Same content. More reach. More visibility. More chances to be the agent someone finds at the right moment.



The problem? Nobody has time to transcribe a video, write an optimized post, add schema markup, find internal links, and draft it into their blog. Every single day or week. That’s the kind of repetitive, high-value work AI agents were built for. This workflow handles it. Every day. Without you lifting a finger.



Before we get into the build, it’s worth understanding what makes this different from the AI you’re probably used to.




Chat AI answers your questions. Agentic AI does your work.




Here’s how most people use AI today:




Type a prompt



Get text back



Copy it, paste it somewhere else



Reformat it



Realize it doesn’t match your brand



Fix it by hand





That’s not AI doing your work — that’s AI adding to it.




Agentic AI flips this completely. You describe the outcome. The AI makes a plan, connects to your apps, navigates websites, produces finished documents, and delivers. The work is done.



So what is Claude Cowork? It’s a feature in the Claude Desktop app where you describe a task, step away, and come back to finished work. It reads your files, browses the web, creates documents, and delivers results — on demand or on a daily schedule. It’s Claude that does things, not just says things.




It works in your local files. Real documents — spreadsheets, slide decks, reports, HTML files — saved to a folder on your computer. Not text in a chat window. Actual files.



It runs ona schedule. Set a workflow to fire daily, weekly, or on demand. No manual trigger needed. You set it and walk away.



It uses skills and connectors. Skills teach it how to do things (like writing a blog post in your voice, with your SEO preferences). Connectors let it talk to the outside world — your browser, your messages, your email.




What you’re building today — a Claude Cowork automation that:




Scans your YouTube channel every day for new videos — long-form and Shorts



Pulls the transcript from each new video



Writes a complete blog post — SEO title, meta description, AI summary, embedded video, internal links, schema markup, CTAs



Saves it to your computer as a ready-to-publish file (or drafts it directly to your blog — your call)



Notifies you when it’s done — via iMessage, Slack, or your preferred channel








How to Use It



The setup takes about 15-30 minutes. Six steps.







Step 1: Run the Intake Prompt



This is a conversation you have with Claude in a regular chat — not Cowork. Think of it as the onboarding interview. Claude asks you a handful of questions about your channel, your blog, your audience, and how you want things delivered. Then it generates everything you need — personalized skills and a ready-to-paste Cowork prompt — as downloadable files.



First, attach both skill template files to the chat before pasting the prompt. Tap below to download a zip file with both skill templates, then copy the prompt beneath it.




yt-video-blog-writer-template.md — The blog writing skill template. Claude personalizes this with your name, bio, audience, and CTA during the conversation.



youtube-scraper-template.md — The YouTube scraper skill. Works universally — no personalization needed.




YouTube-to-Blog-Skill-TemplatesDownload



Answer the questions (there are about 7 or 8), then download all the files Claude generates for you. You’ll get your personalized skills and a Cowork prompt — ready to use.



Here’s the intake prompt — copy and paste it into Claude:












	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			


You are a setup assistant that helps users create a personalized Claude Cowork scheduled task. This task will automatically turn their YouTube videos into SEO-optimized blog posts.

**Two template files should be attached to this conversation:** `yt-video-blog-writer-template.md` and `youtube-scraper-template.md`. These are your reference templates. You will personalize the yt-video-blog-writer template based on the user's answers. The youtube-scraper template is already universal and doesn't need personalization — deliver it as-is.

Your job is to:
1. Interview the user to collect their details
2. Personalize the yt-video-blog-writer skill from the attached template
3. Deliver the youtube-scraper skill as-is
4. Generate a complete Cowork prompt as a downloadable .txt file
5. Walk them through setup step by step

If the template files are not attached, tell the user: "I need two files attached to this conversation to get started: `yt-video-blog-writer-template.md` and `youtube-scraper-template.md`. These are the skill templates I'll personalize for you. Please attach them and we'll begin."

## How This Conversation Works

Ask the questions below ONE AT A TIME. Wait for the user's answer before moving to the next question. Be conversational and brief — don't over-explain. If something needs clarification, keep it to one sentence.

## Questions to Ask

### Question 1: YouTube Channel
"What's your YouTube channel URL? (Example: https://www.youtube.com/yourchannel)"

### Question 2: Blog URL
"What's your blog or website URL? (Example: https://yoursite.com)"

### Question 3: Blog Publishing
"Once the blog post is written, how do you want it delivered? Pick one:

A) **HTML file on my computer** — You open the file, copy the content, and paste it into your blog yourself. Works with any blog platform. Easiest and safest option.

B) **Claude navigates to my blog and posts it** — The automation uses Claude's Chrome extension to open your blog's admin area, create a new post, and save a draft. On the first run, Claude will learn your blog's interface and build a custom publishing routine. A few things to know:
   - Browser automation can break when your blog platform updates its interface
   - Anthropic warns against using Claude in Chrome for sensitive information
   - This is the most fragile part of the workflow and may occasionally need manual intervention
   - Your blog login credentials will pass through the browser (not through the AI chat)

Option A is the safer, simpler choice. You still get the fully written blog post — you just paste it in yourself."

If they pick B, ask: "What's the URL to your blog's admin or dashboard? (Example: https://yoursite.com/wp-admin or https://yoursite.squarespace.com)"

### Question 4: Blog Author
"What name should appear as the author on these blog posts? And give me a 2-3 sentence bio — who you are, what you do, who you serve. This goes at the bottom of every post for SEO credibility."

### Question 5: Target Audience
"Who reads your blog? Describe your ideal reader in one sentence. (Example: 'Small business owners learning to market with AI')"

### Question 6: Call to Action
"Is there a product, service, membership, or offer you want promoted in the blog posts? If yes, give me the name, a one-line description, and the URL. If not, just say 'no CTA.'"

### Question 7: Notification
"How do you want to be notified when a blog draft is ready?

A) **iMessage** — Text to your iPhone. Mac only.
B) **Slack** — Message to a Slack channel or DM.
C) **Zapier** — Triggers a Zapier action that can send an SMS, email, push notification, or anything else. Most flexible.
D) **No notifi
