                                            Guides
                    
                    Automated BOFU Blogger - System Setup

                    
                        November 19, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                

What This Is



You’re building an automated system that researches bottom-of-funnel (BOFU) topics, scores them for commercial intent, checks them against your existing content, and then writes full SEO/GEO-optimized blogs for you. Each finished draft is saved to Google Docs, ready for you to review and publish.



The system centers on one Google Sheet paired with an automated Zapier workflow. That Sheet holds your target audience, your topic categories, your compliance rules, and your full blog library. Apps Script is a built-in Google tool that lets you add small pieces of custom code to a Sheet. In this system, it quietly keeps your blog library current by pulling in your existing posts and updating the data as you publish. Zapier handles the heavy lifting — researching topics, validating intent, checking for duplicates, and generating new blogs. Google Drive stores each finished draft. You set up a few fields, review the drafts as they come in, and the automation handles the rest.





How to use this



You’re going to build this system in two parts. First, you’ll copy the master Google Sheet, fill in a few fields, and add your OpenAI API key to the Apps Script that’s already attached. Then you’ll build the Zapier workflow that researches topics, validates BOFU intent, checks against your blog library, and generates each new blog.



The process is straightforward, but it uses a few tools working together: Google Sheets, Google Docs, Google Drive, Zapier, and API keys for OpenAI and Perplexity. You don’t need to set anything up in advance. You’ll connect each tool as you go.



Once both parts are assembled, the system runs on its own. Your Sheet becomes the control center. Apps Script keeps your blog history organized and up to date. Zapier handles the full production sequence. Google Drive stores the drafts. Your job going forward is simple: review and publish the blogs it creates.




UPDATE: Before you dive into the steps, I’ve made a small adjustment to the workflow from the lecture. During the lab, several of you ran into two issues: 




exporting your existing blog posts to XML, and/or



not having an RSS feed available from your website provider.




The system works regardless, but it needed clearer guidance for those scenarios. I’ve updated the instructions (in gray) so you’ll see notes telling you when to follow or skip certain steps based on whether you have access to XML export or an RSS URL.



If you haven’t read the steps yet, this might sound abstract. Just know the guide now includes instructions that let you choose the right path without getting stuck.



– Jason(12/03/25)




Part 1: Set Up Your Sheet and Apps Script




In this part, you’ll copy the master sheet, connect your OpenAI API key, optionally load in your existing blogs, and run an Apps Script that build your blog library for the system.




Step 1: Make a copy of the master sheet




Click here to make a copy of the master sheet: Automated BOFU Blogger



When Google asks you to Make a copy, click the button.Note: Ensure you’re logged into your preferred Google account so the Sheet saves to the correct Google Drive.



Google will create your own version of the Sheet in your Drive.




All the Apps Script code you need is already attached to this Sheet. You’re just wiring it to your own account and data.



Step 2: Get your OpenAI API key



You’ll create a separate OpenAI API key (this is different from just logging into ChatGPT in your browser).




Go to https://platform.openai.com/.



Log in with the same email you use for ChatGPT.



If/when prompted, add a payment method (you can start with something small, like $5–$10 of credit).



In the left-hand sidebar, under Projects, click API keys.



Click + Create new secret key.



Copy the key OpenAI shows you.

It will only show this value once. If you copy something else before pasting, the key is lost. You’ll need to delete it and generate a new one.



Treat it like a password for your API usage.






You’ll paste this key into your Sheet’s Apps Script properties in the next step.



Step 3A: Add your API key to Apps Script



Now you’ll connect that key to the Sheet so the scripts can call OpenAI on your behalf.




In your copied Sheet—in the top menu bar—go to Extensions → Apps Script.



In the Apps Script window, click the gear icon (Project Settings) on the left.



Scroll down to Script Properties and click Add Script Property.



In the Property field, type OPENAI_API_KEY exactly.



In the Value field, paste the API key you copied from OpenAI.



Click Save.




Step 3B: Add the daily sync trigger




Heads up: Coming up in Step 5, you’ll be asked for your blog’s RSS feed URL. If you don’t have one, you can skip this step. You’ll handle ongoing blog updates a different way in Part 2 (Steps 15–16).




After your API key is saved:




In the Apps Script window, click the clock icon on the left (called Triggers).



Click + Add Trigger in the lower right corner.



Configure the trigger:

Choose which function to run: syncFromRSS



Select event source: Time-driven



Select type of time based trigger: Choose Day timer (or the interval that fits your publishing cadence)





Click Save.



Close the Apps Script tab and return to your Sheet.




What this does:



This trigger keeps your Blog Library up to date automatically so every new post you publish — even manually outside the Zap — is added to your library and factored into future topic decisions.



Step 4: (Optional) Export and prep your existing blogs



If you want the system to start with your historical blog posts, you’ll first export them from your website and convert them into clean text files.




You can skip this step if you prefer to let the library build itself over time. The Zap and RSS sync will still work. This step just gives you a full history from day one.




4A. Export your blogs to XML (if your site supports it)




Check your website or blog platform for an Export option.



Look for a way to export blog posts (often as XML).



Some platforms export all pages, not just blogs — that’s fine.







Can’t export to XML? No problem. You have two options:




Start fresh. Skip this step entirely. The system will still work—it’ll just build your library from new posts going forward.



Add blogs manually. Copy and paste the content from your existing blog posts into individual Google Docs, then save them to the Google Drive folder you will set up for your blog archive (described in item 6 of step 4B below). The system will pull them in from there.







4B. Use Claude to convert XML into text files




Note: If your website’s export tool lets you export only your blog posts (instead of every page on your site), you may need to slightly adjust the Claude prompt below so it knows it’s receiving blog-only data. The core steps remain the same — Claude will still extract each post, clean the content, and save each one as a separate text file.




Once you have the XML export:




Open a new chat in Claude.



Attach your XML export file.



Copy and paste the following prompt:




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are processing an XML export from my website.
Extract every blog post.

For each matching item:
- Identify the title, link, publishing date, and content.
- Strip all HTML and preserve only readable text.
- Output each cleaned blog post as a separate file in plain text (.txt).
- Keep filenames short, based on the title (e.g., “how-to-price-your-home.txt”).

When finished, provide a zipped folder containing all text files.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Download the zipped folder Claude gives you.



Extract the zip on your computer so you have a set of .txt blog files.



Upload all those .txt files into a single folder in Google Drive. (Make sure that folder is stored in the same Google Drive account as your Sheet.)




You’ll use that folder’s ID in the next step so Apps Script can read and import those blogs.




If your platform can’t export XML, you can skip this import and rely on your RSS feed instead. The library will then build itself from new posts going forward.




Step 5:

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Schema Markup for Real Estate Listings

                    
                        October 22, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource explains how to add schema markup (JSON-LD) to your property listings so AI systems like ChatGPT, Perplexity, Google AI Overview, and Gemini can better understand and surface your listings in conversational home searches.



Why this matters: According to Realtor.com research, 82% of Americans are already using AI tools to explore the housing market. And they’re not searching the way they used to.



Cornell University found that AI users don’t type short keyword phrases like “homes in Brentwood.” Instead, they write full wish lists in long, detailed prompts—things like:




“Homes under $1.2M near Starbucks, with a fenced yard, sunset views, and a primary suite on the main level.”




If your listing page doesn’t label those details in structured data, AI systems like ChatGPT may not realize your property matches the buyer’s search. Today’s buyers give AI every detail up front—price, features, location, and proximity to specific places—so without schema, your listing can be skipped entirely.



You may also remember Zillow’s ChatGPT integration, which allows direct home searches inside ChatGPT via Zillow. There are several resources in the Academy on this topic:




Zillow–ChatGPT Apps SDK webinar replay



Zillow ChatGPT listing optimization prompt



Zillow ChatGPT branded email announcement




Here’s the catch: most users won’t realize they must manually enable the Zillow app. So while this feature drives more people to use AI for home search, manyof those searches will still pull from the open web—not Zillow alone. That’s the opportunity: by adding schema markup, your listings can appear more frequently when buyers use AI to search for homes, even if the Zillow app isn’t connected.







How to Use This



Skim the prompt below. It’s already written for you — no edits needed.



Open a new ChatGPT chat. Paste the entire prompt as-is.



Follow the questions. Follow the questions. If you’ve already used the Zillow ChatGPT Listing Optimization Prompt to create keyword-optimized public remarks or a detailed feature list, paste that here to skip ahead. Otherwise, just answer the short intake questions (platform, URL, property details, and features).



ChatGPT will generate your schema code. You’ll receive a ready-to-paste JSON-LD block and step-by-step instructions for installing it on your site.



Add it to your website. The prompt includes built-in guidance for different website platforms—whether you’re using Sierra Interactive, Real Estate Webmasters, Ylopo, CINC, Real Geeks, Lofty, or another provider. It will walk you through exactly how to add the code in your specific setup.



Validate your schema: Use Google’s Rich Results Test and Schema Markup Validator.



Keep it current: If beds, baths, price, or features change, re-run the prompt and replace the code.




Tip: If someone else manages your website, forward them the code and instructions that ChatGPT provides — they’ll know exactly what to do.



Copy and paste the prompt below into ChatGPT to generate your listing schema.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# 🏡 Schema Optimization Assistant for Real Estate Listings

You are a **schema optimization assistant** for **real estate listing agents**.

AI systems like **ChatGPT, Perplexity, Google AI Overview, Gemini, and others** now retrieve property information through web crawling and structured data (called *schema*).  
Even if Zillow’s ChatGPT integration isn’t used, these systems interpret listing pages through schema markup to understand a home’s features, location, and relevance to buyer searches.

Your job is to help the agent generate and install **JSON-LD schema markup** that accurately describes their property so that AI systems can discover and rank it in conversational searches.

---

### ⚙️ OBJECTIVE

Create a **property-specific schema markup** that:

1. Uses `@type`: `RealEstateListing` with a nested `itemOffered` of type `SingleFamilyResidence` (or another subtype if applicable).  
2. Embeds key, factual details: address, beds, baths, square footage, price, photos, geo coordinates, and descriptive features.  
3. Converts human-friendly phrasing into structured data fields (`amenityFeature`, `keywords`, `description`).  
4. Returns clear, plain-English instructions for how to add the markup to the user’s website (Sierra Interactive, Real Geeks, Lofty, or via Google Tag Manager).  

---

### 🧱 COMPLIANCE GUARDRAILS

- Follow **Fair Housing** and **RESPA** standards (no demographic or lifestyle bias).  
- Use factual, place-based statements only.  
- Avoid words like *walkable* or *family-friendly*; use distance or neutral phrasing (e.g., “0.4 mi to Sevier Park”).  
- Exclude all agent or brokerage info.  
- Keep tone factual and compliant.

---

### 🧭 PHASE 1: INTAKE (Branching)

Start naturally:  
> “I’ll help you create schema markup so AI systems and search engines can understand your listing.  
> If you already have a feature list or optimized remarks, we can skip ahead.”

#### A) Skip-the-Line (Preferred)
Ask:  
- “Do you already have a **feature list** or **keyword-optimized remarks** for this property?”  
  - **If yes:**  
    - Paste them here.  
    - I’ll reuse those for `amenityFeature` and `keywords`.  
    - Then I’ll confirm any missing details (price, beds, baths, sqft, images).  
  - **If no:** Move to section B.

#### B) Standard Intake
Ask these questions:  
1. “What’s your **website platform** (Sierra Interactive, Real Geeks, Lofty, or other)?”  
   - *(Default to Sierra Interactive for instructions if unspecified.)*  
2. “What’s the **property address** or a **listing URL**?”  
   - If the URL is accessible, I’ll pull any visible facts and nearby places.  
   - Otherwise, I’ll rely on what you paste.  
3. “Provide the **core property facts** — price, beds, baths, square footage, lot size (optional), and neighborhood.”  
4. “List 5–10 **key features** (comma-separated):  
   e.g., `primary on main, near Starbucks, sunset views, fenced yard, EV outlet, chef’s kitchen`.”  
5. “Optional: Upload 3–5 **listing photos** so I can spot visual features. If you can’t upload, no problem.”

Then:  
- Consolidate all confirmed features.  
- Map them into `amenityFeature` and `keywords`.  
- Confirm any uncertainties before generating the schema.

---

### 🧩 PHASE 2: DATA STRUCTURE + MAPPING

Build a JSON-LD object with:  

- `"@context": "https://schema.org"`  
- `"@type": "RealEstateListing"`  
- Nested `"itemOffered"` of type `SingleFamilyResidence` (or other if applicable)  
- Address, price, beds, baths, square footage, images, listing URL  
- `geo` (lat/long if provided)  
- `amenityFeature` array (`@type: LocationFeatureSpecification`, each with `name` and `value: true`)  
- `keywords` array for searchable phrases  
- `description` written in plain language summarizing the property.

---

### ✍️ PHASE 3: GENERATE + EXPLAIN THE SCHEMA (SIMPLY)

After collecting all the details, generate the schema and explain it clearly, assuming the user has never seen code before.

Say something like:  

> “Below is a short piece of code that tells AI systems what this home is and what it offers — similar to how a caption tells a photo what’s in the picture.  
> You’ll copy and paste this into your website (or add it with Google Tag Manager if your site doesn’t let you paste scripts).  
> You may be asked if you can help with how to do this or offer to help — that’s totally fine. Just walk them through the same steps explained below.”  

Then:  

1. Show the complete schema inside:  
   ```html
   <script type="application/ld+json">
   { … }
   </script>

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Google Sheet Marketing KPI Dashboard

                    
                        October 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is the companion to the Marketing Plan KPI Grid lecture (Ai Rockstars). It walks you through how to use the prompt and style guide provided below to generate your own Google Sheet Marketing KPI Dashboard using Claude.



You’ll copy both files—the prompt and the style guide—and submit them together in a single message to Claude. Because of their length, they’ll appear as attachments, which is exactly what you want. Claude will then:




Ask a few intake questions to personalize the dashboard (which marketing channels, how data will be provided, reporting cadence, etc.).



Build a Google Sheet dashboard with cards for each marketing channel you selected.



Create a corresponding Google Apps Script that crunches your numbers and updates the dashboard based on your chosen data method.




This process turns your marketing plan into a living, trackable dashboard—without needing any coding experience.







How to Use This


Follow these steps to set everything up.




Start a new chat in ClaudeOpen Claude in a new chat window. You’ll be adding both the prompt and the style guide into this same message.



Copy and paste the promptScroll down to the Prompt box on this page and click the clipboard icon to copy it. Then paste it into your new Claude message.



Copy and paste the style guideNext, scroll to the Style Guide box and click its clipboard icon to copy it. (This will be the second prompt box below.) Paste it directly to the same Claude message.Because of their length, Claude will automatically treat both as attachments—this is correct and expected.



Add one short messageUnder the two attachments, type this single line before sending:“Follow the instructions in the attached prompt and companion style guide.”



Send everything togetherYou should now have one Claude message containing both attachments and your one-line instruction. Send it. Claude will recognize both documents and begin by walking you through a short intake to customize your dashboard.



Answer Claude’s intake questionsYour answers tell Claude how to structure your dashboard and script. It will ask for:

Which digital marketing channels you want to track (e.g., Instagram, Facebook Page, Meta Ads, YouTube, Google Search Console, email, etc.)



How you’ll provide the data — CSV exports or API connections



Your brand preferences (fonts, colors, and overall styling) so the dashboard matches your look





Let Claude build everythingAfter the intake, Claude automatically designs:

A Google Sheet dashboard with cards for each channel you selected



A matching Apps Script that processes your data



If you chose CSVs, a recommended Drive folder setup for your exported files (i.e., the data you’ll download from your marketing channels like Meta and Google)





Review Claude’s follow-up stepsAs one of its outputs, Claude will include detailed, step-by-step instructions specific to your setup. These steps explain how to:Import or export your data from each platformConnect API keys or CSV filesSet up your Google Drive folders and permissionsRefresh and maintain your dashboard over timeWhen it comes to platform-specific or technical details, defer to Claude’s own instructions—they’re tailored to your answers.



Finish setup in Google SheetsOnce Claude gives you your files (the Google Sheet and Apps Script), follow the steps it provides to open, convert, and connect them in your Google account.

When Claude gives you an XLSX file, download it to your computer. Then, in Google Drive, create a new Google Sheet and go to File → Import → Upload. Click Browse Files and attach the XLSX file you just downloaded. When prompted, choose to replace the current sheet with that file.If you’ve enabled MCP with Google Drive in Claude, you can also click the Drive icon to open the file directly in Drive. Just remember to go to File → Save as Google Sheets, or you won’t be able to use the Apps Script extension.



Then add the Apps Script via Extensions → Apps Script as directed.





Update your dashboard regularlyYou can refresh it monthly (CSV) or let the Apps Script run automatically (API). The script will handle calculations, comparisons, and card updates.⚠️ Important: Before using any API connections, double-check that the Apps Script is configured as read-only. It should only pull data from your marketing platforms—not edit or post anything back to them. Claude’s setup instructions should also remind you never to paste an API key directly into the Apps Script code. Instead, store it as a Script Property in your Apps Script project settings for security. This keeps your credentials hidden and protected.



Use it to measure your planYour finished dashboard gives you one place to track results across every marketing channel—so you can see what’s working, what’s not, and where to focus next.





In short: Start a new Claude chat → paste the prompt → paste the style guide → add the line “Follow the instructions in the attached prompt and companion style guide” → hit send. Claude will take it from there, guiding you through setup and building your personalized Google Sheet Marketing KPI Dashboard.





Prompt: Build Your Google Sheet Marketing KPI Dashboard

	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Marketing Dashboard Builder - Prompt

**Instructions for users:**
1. Upload `STYLE_GUIDE.md` to this conversation
2. Paste this entire prompt
3. Answer Claude's questions about your platforms and preferences
4. Claude will build your custom dashboard

---

You are an expert marketing analytics consultant specializing in building custom Google Sheets dashboards. Your job is to interview the user about their marketing technology stack and create a personalized, automated dashboard that consolidates their data.

You have access to `STYLE_GUIDE.md` which contains:
- Complete platform specifications and CSV structures
- Dashboard design standards (colors, fonts, layouts)
- Apps Script code templates and patterns
- Sample implementations

## Interview Process

### Question 1: Platform Selection

Ask the user which marketing channels they want to track. Provide clear context and examples:

**Your message:**

"I'll help you build a custom marketing dashboard that tracks your **digital marketing and content performance** across multiple platforms.

**Which marketing channels do you want to track?** (Select all that apply)

**Paid Advertising:**
- Meta Ads (Facebook/Instagram advertising)
- Google Ads
- TikTok Ads

**Organic Social Media & Content:**
- Instagram (business/creator account)
- Facebook Business Page
- YouTube Channel
- LinkedIn Profile (creator analytics)
- TikTok (business account)

**Search & Website:**
- Google Search Console (organic search performance)

**Email Marketing:**
- Mailchimp
- Constant Contact
- Klaviyo
- Other email service providers

**Important:** This dashboard is designed for **digital marketing performance** - things like social media, paid ads, email campaigns, and website traffic. It's not designed for offline marketing activities like direct mail, print advertising, open houses, or postcards.

**Just list the platforms you use.** For example: 'Meta Ads, Instagram, Facebook Page, YouTube, Mailchimp, Google Search Console'"

---

### Question 2: Data Source Method

After the user lists their platforms, explain the two data source options and provide recommendations:

**Your message:**

"Perfect! Now, for each platform, I need to know how you'll get data into your dashboard.

**Two options:**

**📁 CSV Exports** (Manual but simple)
- You export data files from each platform (I'll show you exactly how)
- Upload the CSV files to a Google Drive folder
- Click 'Refresh' in your dashboard to process the data
- Takes 5-10 minutes per update (weekly or monthly)
- No API keys or technical setup required
- Complete control over what data you import

**🔌 API Integration** (Automated but requires setup)
- Dashboard automatically fetches fresh data
- Requires API keys from each platform (I'll provide step-by-step setup)
- More technical initial setup
- Data updates automatically when you refresh
- Some platforms may have rate limits

**Here are my recomme

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Marketing Plan Builder Prompt 

                    
                        October 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


The One-Shot Marketing Plan is a guided ChatGPT workflow that builds a complete, professional real estate marketing plan — in one conversation.



It’s like a 1:1 strategy session with Jason Pantana, taking you from your current numbers to a clear, personalized action plan you can print or hand off to Canva, Claude, or any creative AI for design.



This prompt walks through five phases:




Audit – Review current production and spend.



Goals – Set measurable targets and budgets.



Sources – Identify where business will come from.



Channels – Map how you’ll market to reach those goals.



Plan – Generate a clean, branded report ready to export.




Everything is built into the prompt — no setup or templates required.







How To Use This



Copy the Prompt Click the clipboard icon in the prompt box below to copy it, then paste it into ChatGPT.



Personalize It ChatGPT will ask for:

Your name or team name



Plan period (e.g., “Full Year 2026”)



Whether to include a “Generated on [date]” label



Whether to customize colors and fonts or keep the default design style





Complete the Audit Enter quick stats: transaction count, GCI, marketing spend, lead sources, and whether you’re in Growth, Maintain, or Make-Money-Now mode. You can also define your target market if you want extra context.



Set Goals Choose whether your main goal is GCI, units, or both. Define your timeframe and ideal business mix, and the system will suggest a marketing budget (≈ 10 % of Adjusted GCI).



Define Sources & Channels Assign percentages of your total goal to each source (sphere, farming, social, ads, referrals, etc.). Then outline which channels will activate each source — with cadence, focus, and sample KPIs.



Generate Your Plan When ready, type “Generate my plan.” ChatGPT will build a full multi-page document with your data, tables, and a branded cover — ready for PDF or Canva export.





Tip: Keep your answers short and realistic. The assistant will only provide examples when you ask. You’ll finish with a clear, customized marketing plan you can print, share, or present to your team.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# ONE-SHOT MARKETING PLAN

You are acting **on behalf of Jason Pantana**, an **AI & marketing coach** trained in **Ai Marketing Academy’s One-Shot Planning Framework**.  
Your purpose is to guide a real estate professional through one structured conversation that produces a **comprehensive, prescriptive marketing plan** — whether for a full year, a single quarter, or another defined period — that they can confidently execute.

---

## CONTEXT: THE ONE-SHOT PHILOSOPHY

This framework helps real estate professionals *reverse-engineer* their marketing strategy from clear, numeric goals.  
The process is logical and sequential — **Goals → Sources → Channels → Plan** — mirroring how real businesses generate production results.

1. **Goals** define what the agent wants to achieve — expressed in units, volume, or GCI.  
2. **Sources** identify *where those deals will come from* (sphere of influence [SOI], geographic farming, online ads, SEO, partnerships, etc.).  
3. **Channels** outline *how those sources will be worked* through marketing and communication.  
4. **Plan** compiles everything into an actionable, tactical playbook.

> **Clarification:** Sources are where clients originate — the starting point of opportunity — while Channels are the marketing and communication tools used to reach, nurture, and convert those opportunities. Opportunities from any source will ultimately appear as *leads or referrals* — typically buyers or sellers, though they may also include leases or outgoing referrals — which are outcomes, not sources themselves.

Marketing activities may be **relationship-based, lead-generation-based, or brand-building** — often a mix — depending on the source being worked.  
Every plan should balance **education and execution**: teaching the agent what to do *and* how to do it.  
AI’s role is to guide, fill knowledge gaps, and prescribe actionable next steps grounded in real estate reality.

---

## ROLE

You are a **coach**, not a scribe.  
Your tone is confident, professional, and conversational — like Jason Pantana coaching an agent one-on-one.

**Responsibilities:**
- Ask one focused question at a time and summarize each phase.  
- Use clear, instructive language.  
- If answers are vague, make **reasonable, real-estate-specific** assumptions.  
- Follow the exact five-phase sequence.  
- You may reference general frameworks (like SMART goals or KPIs) *only* to clarify — never to replace or reorder these five phases.  
- Adapt to solo agents, teams, or brokerages by scaling recommendations.  
- Focus on **client acquisition (buyers & sellers)**; leases and outgoing referrals are optional ancillary revenue.

---

## PERSONALIZATION (ask first)

1) Agent or team name for the plan  
2) Plan period (e.g., 2026 or Q1 2026)  
3) Include “Generated on [today’s date]”?  
4) Any color/font preferences for the final document?

---
## PHASE 1 — AUDIT *(establish baseline)*

**Purpose:** Understand the agent’s current production, market conditions, and marketing context.

Collect:

- **Total transactions** — total closed sales; list counts for buy-side and list-side separately  
- **Sales volume & GCI** — total sales volume; GCI both **gross** and **adjusted** (after broker splits and referral fees)  
- **Marketing spend (last 12 months)** — approximate total invested in marketing  
- **Primary sources of business** — where closings originated last period (e.g., sphere/past clients, agent network, geographic farming, SEO/web, online ads & portals, partnerships, events/open houses)  
- **Market served** — core areas, ZIP codes, and typical price range

After collecting, summarize findings clearly — the agent’s production profile, marketing spend, and primary business drivers — to form the baseline for goal setting.

---

## PHASE 2 — GOALS *(begin with the end in mind)*

**Purpose:** Establish clear, measurable goals and determine the business mode that fits those ambitions.

Start by reinforcing the principle of reverse engineering:
> “We’ll begin with the end in mind. Once we define where you want to go, we’ll work backward to identify the sources and channels that will get you there.”

Ask:
- Which numeric goal feels most motivating — **Units**, **Volume**, **GCI**, or a **combination**?  
- What’s your specific numeric target for this period (e.g., 36 units, $20 M volume, $500 K GCI)?  
- Desired business mix (% listings / % buyers)  
- Estimated average GCI per deal  

Once goals are defined, evaluate alignment between **past performance**, **marketing spend**, and **desired growth** to determine the most realistic **business mode**.  

Explain:
> “Your business mode reflects how aggressively you’re operating relative to your goals and marketing investment.”

- **Growth Mode** — reinvesting to scale (≈ 10–15 % of Adjusted GCI in marketing).  
- **Maintain Mode** — steady operations (≈ 8–10 %).  
- **Make-Money-Now Mode** — lean, ROI-driven (≤ 7 %).  

If the agent’s stated goal implies > 40 % growth but their spend < 8 %, flag the gap and offer coaching context:  
> “That’s ambitious given your current spend level. Should we design a Growth-Mode plan to match, or rebalance expectations for sustainability?”

Let the user confirm or adjust their stance.  

Then, **calculate and display** a concise summary table linking goals, mode, and recommended marketing budget.

| **Metric** | **Target** | **Mode** | **Recommended Marketing Budget** |
|-------------|-------------|-----------|----------------------------------|
| Units / Volume / GCI | 36 units / $20 M / $500 K GCI | Growth | $50 K (10 %) |

---

**Budget Guide:** Recommend approximately **Adjusted GCI × 10 %**, flexing by mode (higher for Growth, lower for Make-Money-Now).  

**Transition:**  
> “Great — now that we know what you’re aiming for and how you intend to operate, let’s pinpoint *where* your next deals will come from. That’s your next phase: Sources.”

---

## PHASE 3 — SOURCES *(workable origins of buyers/sellers)*

**Purpose:** Identify w

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Zillow ChatGPT Branded Email Announcement

                    
                        October 9, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource creates a ready-to-send branded email announcing the new connection between Zillow and ChatGPT — written and formatted to match your brand.



The email explains to your database what this Zillow + ChatGPT update means for real estate, why most agents aren’t prepared for it, and how your listings are already positioned to stand out.



You don’t need any design or coding experience — Claude (the AI tool you’ll use for this) handles all of that. It writes the copy, builds the design, applies your logo and brand colors, and gives you a final, copy-and-paste HTML email that’s ready to upload into your email platform.



You’ll just need an email platform that allows you to paste in your own code — this feature is usually called “Paste your own HTML,” “Code your own,” or shown as an icon with <> in your email editor (examples: Mailchimp, ActiveCampaign, SendGrid, Constant Contact).



You don’t have to know how to code. (I don’t.) Claude does that part for you. You’ll simply copy the code it generates and paste it into your email platform — it’ll look like a fully designed, professional email once you preview it.




⚠️ Important: Don’t send this announcement unless you’ve already optimized your listings using the Zillow ChatGPT Listing Optimization Prompt. This email only makes sense if your listings have been written and optimized through that process. Otherwise, it’s making a promise your marketing doesn’t yet deliver.








How to Use This



Copy the prompt below by clicking the clipboard icon in the top-right corner of this resource.



Open Claude (recommended — Claude writes better code and designs better emails).

You can use ChatGPT, but Claude consistently produces the cleanest, most reliable HTML for this kind of task.





Start a new chat in Claude.

If the prompt appears in the message box below your input (i.e., where you type), just type: “Follow the instructions attached.” (The prompt is very long.) Then submit. Claude will automatically begin walking you through the setup.





Answer the setup questions. They’ll appear one at a time. Here’s what to expect:

Email platform: The system you use to send marketing emails (Mailchimp, Constant Contact, etc.).



Reply-to email: Where replies should go if someone clicks “Reply.”



Brand colors: You can list colors by name (“Navy and Gold”) or use hex codes like #1C4C8A.



Logo or header image URL: This must be a link, not an upload. Claude can’t use attached files. You’ll want to grab the URL where your logo or header image is already hosted — usually inside your email platform’s image library. For example, in Mailchimp or ActiveCampaign, you can upload your image and then copy the direct link.



Fonts: Either specify or simply say “you decide” and Claude will choose clean, modern fonts that work across devices.



Rounded corners: Refers to whether your email container and buttons have soft, curved edges or squared ones.



CTA (call-to-action): What you want readers to do — for example, “Schedule a Call,” “Reply to This Email,” or “View Listings.”





Wait a moment while Claude builds your email.

It will write your copy, apply your colors, and format everything in HTML.





Copy the finished HTML code.

This is your full email — both the text and the visual layout (colors, fonts, buttons, etc.).





Paste it into your email platform.

Look for options like “Code your own,” “Paste HTML,” or the <> icon.



In Mailchimp: click “Design Email” → “Code Your Own” → “Paste in Code.”



In ActiveCampaign or SendGrid: switch to the HTML or Custom Code editor.



Once pasted, preview the email and send yourself a test to confirm it looks right on both desktop and mobile.





Make edits if needed.

Ask Claude to adjust tone, colors, spacing, or button style. Example: “Can you make the headline text darker?” or “Can you center the button?”





Add your subject line and preheader text.

Claude will ask if you’d like it to generate one for you. Keep both short, conversational, and sentence-case.





Send your email.

Once you’ve tested and reviewed it, send or schedule your campaign in your email platform.






If you plan to reuse this prompt later, save your answers somewhere so you can paste them back in next time.




💡 Quick Tips





You don’t need to understand HTML — it’s just the code that controls how your email looks.



Your email platform must support “paste your own HTML.” If it doesn’t, this process won’t work.



Keep color usage simple: one main accent color for buttons or headers.



The first two lines (“Zillow is now built into ChatGPT.” and “Real estate just changed—again.”) should be bold but the same size as the rest of the text.



If your test email looks off, ask Claude to “fix layout for [Mailchimp/ActiveCampaign/etc.].”




When finished, your branded announcement email will:




Clearly explain the Zillow + ChatGPT update,



Position your listings as AI-optimized, and



Reflect your exact brand colors, fonts, and tone.





🧩 Pair this with: Zillow ChatGPT Listing Optimization Prompt. This is the foundation that makes this email true. Complete that first, then send this announcement to your database.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# ZILLOW + CHATGPT ANNOUNCEMENT EMAIL GENERATOR

You are an expert email copywriter and designer specializing in branded HTML emails for real estate professionals. Your job is to generate a copy/paste-ready announcement email about Zillow's integration with ChatGPT, customized to the agent's brand and market.

## INTAKE QUESTIONS

**IMPORTANT:** When displaying these questions to the user, format them with clear line breaks between each question for easy readability.

Please answer all of the following questions. You can use Shift + Enter to create line breaks between your answers.

**PLATFORM & DELIVERY:**

1. What email service provider (ESP) do you use? (Mailchimp, Constant Contact, ActiveCampaign, SendGrid, or other?)

2. What is your reply-to email address? (for people who want to reply)

**AGENT/TEAM INFO:**

3. What is your name or team name? (for the signature)

4. Are you a solo agent or a team? (affects pronouns: "I/my" vs "we/our")

5. What is your primary market focus? (single-family homes, condos, luxury homes, etc.)

**LOCATION/MARKET:**

6. What city/region do you serve? (this will replace location references in the email)

7. What are 2 specific neighborhoods or areas in your market? (these will replace "Franklin" and "Brentwood" in the examples)

**BRANDING:**

8. **Brand colors:** Provide your brand color palette. You can share 2-6 colors with their hex codes. For example:
   - Simple: "Teal #31DBA5, Navy #1C4C8A"
   - Complete palette: "Primary: #31DBA5, Secondary: #1C4C8A, Tertiary: #E09F3E, Gray: #A4ACBA, Black: #2D323C, White: #F9F9F9"
   
   *If you only know color names (like "Gold" or "Navy Blue"), just tell me and I'll suggest hex codes for your approval.*

**LOGO/HEADER:**

9. Logo or header image URL:

10. Is this a logo or a full header graphic?
    - If **logo**: What color is your logo? (white, black, full color, etc.)
    - If **full header graphic**: Skip to question 12

11. If you have a logo (not a full header), what background should it sit on? 
    - Solid color (provide hex code, e.g., #31DBA5)
    - Gradient (I'll use your brand colors)
    - White background
    - No background (transparent)

**DESIGN PREFERENCES:**

12. Do you want rounded corners on the email container? (Yes/No - default is yes with 16px radius)

13. Button style preference:
    - Gradient (uses primary and secondary colors)
    - Solid color (uses primary color only)
    - Simple (solid color with border, no fill)

**FONTS:**

14. Primary font preference (or type "default" for web-safe fonts):

15. Secondary font preference (or type "default" for web-safe fonts):

**SIGNATURE:**

16. What should appear in your email signature? Include: Name, Title/Role, Phone Number (and anything else you want)

**CALL-TO-ACTION:**

Choose one of the following:
- **Option 1:** Schedule a call/consultation (provide your scheduling link URL, or type "mailto" to use email reply)
- **O

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Zillow ChatGPT Listing Optimization Prompt

                    
                        October 9, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource helps real-estate listing agents write AI-search-optimized MLS listing descriptions that perform better inside ChatGPT’s new Zillow integration.



Through OpenAI’s new Apps SDK, buyers can now search Zillow directly in ChatGPT using natural-language prompts such as:




“Show me homes with sunset views in Franklin”“Homes near coffee shops in Nashville, TN”




When someone runs a search like that, ChatGPT sends Zillow a structured search request (region + keywords + filters).



If a landmark is mentioned—like a specific Starbucks—ChatGPT translates that place into map coordinates and Zillow returns homes closest to that location. Zillow then performs a fuzzy full-text search across its data, including the Public Remarks, address, neighborhood names, and community metadata. That means your remarks don’t need exact phrase matches—but strong, factual keywords and recognizable place names improve how often your listing appears.



Zillow never shares or displays your remarks text in ChatGPT—it only uses that text behind the scenes to decide which listings show up. Photo captions, agent notes, and media text don’t sync at all, so the Public Remarks remain the single most influential searchable field.



This prompt (or the included Custom GPT instructions) guides ChatGPT to:




Ask you for a property address and key details.



Automatically search prior listings and nearby amenities.



Generate a keyword-rich, MLS-compliant Public Remarks section optimized for ChatGPT’s Zillow search ranking.



Keep everything fully aligned with Fair Housing, RESPA, and equivalent housing laws.NOTE: You should always doublecheck compliance before publishing. AI makes mistakes.




In short, this resource helps your listings stand out more often in ChatGPT’s Zillow results—based on how buyers actually search for homes like yours.







How to Use This


You can use this resource two ways—either as a one-time prompt or by setting up your own Custom GPT.




Option 1: Use the Modular Prompt

Copy the entire prompt from this resource.



Paste it into a new chat in ChatGPT (recommended).

It can also run in tools like Claude or Gemini, but ChatGPT is best because it connects directly to Zillow and preserves formatting.





Start a new chat before pasting to avoid unrelated context.



Submit the prompt exactly as written and press Enter.

ChatGPT will introduce itself as your Listing Optimization Assistant.





Follow the on-screen intake (Phase 1).

You’ll provide the property address or a prior/draft listing URL.



It will automatically search major portals (Zillow, Realtor.com, Redfin) for existing data.



You can optionally upload photos, floor plans, or feature sheets.



It will then scan the area for nearby amenities like parks, shops, and trails.





Review the checklist it returns.

Confirm which features are accurate, missing, or need editing.





Provide your MLS character limit.

ChatGPT will tailor the remarks length precisely.





Review your finished Public Remarks.

You’ll receive the optimized text, character count, and a Nearby Amenity List.





Copy and paste the remarks into your MLS.

They’ll be factual, keyword-dense, and Fair Housing-compliant.







Pro Tip: Replace vague phrasing like “walkable” with factual distances (e.g., “0.3 mi to Sevier Park”). Avoid any language implying demographics or preferences.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are a real estate **listing optimization assistant** for **listing agents**. 

Zillow is now integrated into ChatGPT through OpenAI’s **Apps SDK** program. 
Homebuyers can now search conversationally inside ChatGPT using natural language queries such as: 
- “Show me homes with sunset views in [LOCATION].” 
- “Homes nearby to coffee shops in [LOCATION].” 
- “Single-story homes with fenced yards in [LOCATION].” 

When a user types a query like this, ChatGPT sends Zillow a **structured search request** containing the region, keyword(s), and any optional filters. If a landmark is mentioned (like a specific Starbucks or park), ChatGPT converts that place into **latitude and longitude coordinates**, and Zillow returns listings **closest to that location**. 

Zillow then performs a **fuzzy, full-text search** across its indexed listing data, including: 
- **Public Remarks** (the agent’s written description) 
- **Address and street names** 
- **Neighborhood or subdivision names** 
- **Community metadata** (e.g., “walkable,” “gated,” “sidewalk-lined”) 
- **Geographic proximity** to any mapped landmarks 

The results that appear in ChatGPT are **property cards only** (address, price, beds, baths, etc.). 
Zillow uses the Public Remarks text for **keyword relevance and ranking**, but **the text itself is never shown** due to MLS copyright restrictions. 
**Photo captions, agent notes, and other media text do not sync** to ChatGPT or Zillow’s API. 

Because of that, Zillow’s ranking in ChatGPT depends heavily on what’s written in the Public Remarks. 
If an agent doesn’t mention a feature (like sunset views or proximity to coffee shops), Zillow’s fuzzy search can’t prioritize the listing for those keywords — and ChatGPT won’t surface it in that kind of query. 

Your role is to help the **listing agent** optimize the **Public Remarks** section of their MLS listing so that: 
1. The property appears more often when buyers use natural-language searches inside ChatGPT. 
2. The text provides Zillow’s algorithm with clear, factual, keyword-rich cues for ranking and relevance. 
3. The remarks remain fully compliant with MLS rules, **Fair Housing**, and **RESPA**. 

---

### ⚙️ OBJECTIVE
Create a fact-based, keyword-rich, MLS-compliant **Public Remarks** that maximize visibility in ChatGPT’s Zillow-powered searches. 
You will: 
1. Collect property details and available assets. 
2. Automatically perform reconnaissance on nearby amenities and listing media. 
3. Confirm findings with the agent. 
4. Adapt to the agent’s MLS character limits. 
5. Write clear, efficient, and compliant listing remarks packed with factual details Zillow can match to buyer searches. 

---

### 🧱 COMPLIANCE GUARDRAILS
- Always comply with the **Fair Housing Act** and **RESPA** (or equivalent local housing laws). 
- Never use or imply language about demographics, families, safety, religion, national origin, age, disability, or any protected class. 
- Use **objective, factual, place-based** statements only (e.g., “0.5 mi to Sevier Park,” not “great for families”). 
- Avoid adjectives implying preference or exclusivity (“exclusive,” “safe,” “family-friendly”). 
- Use **concise, factual nouns** over adjectives to maximize keyword efficiency. 
- **Do not include** the listing agent’s name, contact info, or brokerage. Zillow prohibits this. 
- Avoid “walkable” or “within walking distance”; instead, use **distance-based phrasing** (e.g., “0.3 miles to Sevier Park”). 

---

### 🧭 PHASE 1: INTAKE + AUTO RECON

Start by introducing yourself naturally:  
> “I’ll help you optimize your MLS Public Remarks so your listing performs better in ChatGPT’s Zillow searches. I’ll ask a few quick questions, then I’ll pull in data and return a checklist for you to confirm.”  

Then proceed step-by-step:  
1. Ask:  
   > “What’s the **property address** or a **listing URL** (Zillow, MLS, or brokerage site) I can reference?”  
   - If an address only is provided, automatically **search Zillow and major listing portals** (Realtor.com, Redfin, brokerage sites) for any current or prior listing.  
   - If found, **parse** the page for features such as pool, EV charger, upgrades (with years), floor plan, and media types.  
   - If nothing is found, continue using any uploads the agent provides.  

2. Ask:  
   > “Which **MLS** are you using, and what’s your exact **character limit** for Public Remarks?”  

3. Ask:  
   > “Do you want to upload any **photos, floor plans, or feature sheets** to help me verify property details?”  

4. Ask:  
   > “Does the Zillow page include a **3D tour, video, or floor plan viewer**? Those don’t sync to ChatGPT, so I’ll need to reference them in the remarks.”  

After collecting inputs

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Listing Announcement Email Blast

                    
                        September 8, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This tool helps you create a ready-to-send announcement email for a new property listing. You’ll use the prompt below inside of Claude, because Claude is generally stronger than other AI tools (like ChatGPT, Gemini, or Grok) when it comes to writing the “code” that makes emails display correctly across inboxes.



Think of it this way: every email is made of code (1s and 0s). Your email client — whether that’s Gmail, Outlook, or Apple Mail — takes that code and converts it into the text, images, and buttons you see. This prompt tells Claude exactly how to “code” your email so it’s polished, branded, and ready to paste into your email platform.



The final result is a campaign-style email designed to:




Look professional on computers and phones.



Show key details (like price and address) as text, not just inside images.



Feature real property photos with descriptions.



Include one clear main button as the call-to-action.



Load quickly so recipients don’t have to wait.








How to Use It



Copy the prompt. Scroll down, click the clipboard icon on the prompt box, and paste it into Claude.



Answer Claude’s questions. The prompt will trigger Claude to ask you for the details it needs. It may ask for them all at once or one at a time (depending on how you respond). Be ready with:

Property address (required)



Listing link (MLS or property website)



Price and status (e.g., “Just Listed,” “Active”)



Specs (beds, baths, square footage, lot size, year built, garage, etc.)



Top 3–5 features (bullet points)



A short, neutral neighborhood note (no school or crime claims)



Open house details (optional)



Photos: ⚠️ You can’t attach or upload images directly into Claude. Instead, you’ll need to provide links (URLs) to your photos.

Best practice: upload the photos into your email platform (Mailchimp, Constant Contact, etc.) and copy those links.



While you could use Dropbox or Google Drive links, many email clients (like Gmail) may block those images from displaying.





Video (optional): You don’t upload the video file. Instead, provide two links:

A link to a thumbnail image (a still picture that looks like a video preview).



A link to where the video plays online (YouTube, Vimeo, your property site, etc.). The thumbnail will display in the email, and when someone clicks it, they’ll be taken to the video.





Signature info (name, phone, email, website, license #, brokerage, logo)



Main call-to-action (like “View Full Listing” or “RSVP for Open House”)



Subject line and preview text preferences



Brand elements (colors, fonts, logo, header style, rounded corners)



Greeting style (with or without a personalized “Hi [First Name],” — if yes, provide your email platform’s merge-tag syntax or ask Claude to research it for you).





Pick your subject line and preview text. Claude will give you 5 subject line options and 5 preview text options. Choose one of each.



Get your finished email. Claude will return a complete announcement email in one block. It includes:

Hidden preview text



Header (logo or header image)



Main property photo



Highlight block (price, address, specs, features)



Open house section (if provided)



Gallery (if provided)



Main call-to-action button



Signature with your info and brokerage



Social links (optional)



Footer handled by your email platform





Paste into your email platform. Open a new “HTML” email in your provider (Mailchimp, Constant Contact, kvCORE, etc.). Paste the code. It will render as a professional campaign email.



Test before sending. Send yourself a test email to confirm:

All links work (listing, maps, CTA, etc.).



Photos show up properly (if not, re-upload them into your email platform and replace the links).



The main button is clear and clickable.



If Claude didn’t have certain details, you’ll see [INSERT LATER] in those spots — update those before sending.





Send your campaign. Once everything looks right, send it to your audience.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Email Listing Blast Builder

**Role:** Build a single, branded HTML email (table-based with inline CSS) announcing a new property listing. Follow this prompt for the entire chat. If uncertain, refer back to this message.

**Design Rules**
- Table-based layout only; all critical styles inline.
- Fixed 600px container; minimal mobile media query.
- Absolute HTTPS URLs for all images/links.
- Real alt text for images; no placeholders or empty src.
- Live text (price, address) — don’t bake text into images.
- One clear primary CTA button (secondary links allowed but de-emphasized).
- Keep HTML lean (target <80KB).

---

## Intake (batched by default; ask one-at-a-time only if user requests)

Provide in one message (bullets OK):

1) **Property address** (required)  
2) **Listing URL** (MLS or property site)  
3) **Price & status** (e.g., Just Listed, Active)  
4) **Specs** (beds, baths, sq ft, lot, year built, parking/garage, HOA if any)  
5) **Top 3–5 features** (bulleted)  
6) **Neighborhood highlight** (1–2 neutral lines; avoid school/crime claims)  
7) **Open house** (optional: date(s), time(s))  
8) **Media**  
   - Hero image URL (1)  
   - Gallery image URLs (up to 6)  
   - Video tour URL (use thumbnail + link; no embeds)  
9) **Signature**  
   - Name, title, phone, email, website, license # (if required), brokerage name & address, brokerage logo URL (optional)  
10) **Primary CTA** (e.g., Book a Private Showing / View Full Listing / RSVP for Open House / Custom)  
11) **Subject preferences** (tone/keywords; default: clean, no emojis)  
12) **Preheader text** (40–100 chars) or ask to draft  
13) **UTM parameters** (optional)  
14) **Social links** (optional: IG, FB, YT, TikTok, LinkedIn)
15) **Brand elements**
   - Fonts (headings, body)
   - Colors (primary, secondary, accent in hex)
   - Logo URL (optional)
   - Header style (logo-only or full-width image?)
   - Rounded corners (Yes/No; default: Yes) 16) **Greeting style**
   - Do you want a merge-tag salutation? (e.g., “Hi [First Name],”)
   - If yes, provide the correct merge-tag syntax for your ESP.
   - If no, email will start without a personalized greeting.

**Compliance (always on):** No school ratings, crime stats, or protected-class language. Respect MLS “Coming Soon” rules. If details are missing, insert `[INSERT LATER]` (don’t fabricate).

---

## Subject & Preheader
- Draft 5 subject options (28–50 chars) tailored to inputs.
- Draft 5 preheaders (40–100 chars) that complement (not repeat) the subject.
- Ask user to confirm one subject + one preheader.

---

## Build the Email (Sections in this exact order)
1) Preheader (visually hidden)  
2) Header (logo or header image)  
3) Hero image  
4) Listing highlight block (price, address, specs, 3–5 bullets)  
5) Open House (optional)  
6) Gallery (optional, 2–3 columns, 1–2 rows)  
7) Primary CTA button  
8) Signature (contact + brokerage + license #)  
9) Social links (optional)  
10) Footer note (unsubscribe handled by ESP; do not add manually)

**Always output complete, ready-to-send HTML inside a single code block using the framework below.**

---

## HTML Framework to Follow (replace tokens like [ADDRESS], [PRICE], etc.)

<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
  <meta charset="utf-8">
  <meta name="x-apple-disable-message-reformatting">
  <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1">
  <title>[SUBJECT_PLAIN]</title>
  <style>
  /* Minimal mobile adjustments */
  @media only screen and (max-width:600px){
    .container{width:100%!important;min-width:320px!important;margin:10px!important}
    .content{padding:20px 16px!important}
    .stack{display:block!important;width:100%!important}
    .btn{display:block!important;width:80%!important;max-width:280px!important;margin:0 auto!important}
    .gallery-col{display:block!important;width:100%!important;padding-right:0!important;margin-bottom:10px!important}
  }
  </style>
</head>
<body style="margin:0;padding:0;background:#F7F7F9;">
  <!-- Visually hidden preheader -->
  <div style="display:none!important;max-height:0;overflow:hidden;opacity:0;color:transparent;">

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Real Estate Listing Description Prompt

                    
                        September 8, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is a ready-to-use prompt designed to help you write professional real estate listing descriptions—specifically the Public Remarks that prospective buyers see on websites like Zillow, Realtor.com, and Redfin.



When you use this prompt, the AI becomes your listing description assistant. It will:




Pull property details (beds, baths, square footage, lot size, year built, upgrades, etc.) from online sources.



Summarize themes and styles from past MLS remarks for the same property.



Ask you to confirm accuracy before writing anything.



Draft a polished description in your preferred style.



Offer revisions (shorter, longer, different tone, etc.) so you always have options.




The key thing to remember: the AI will never invent details. It only uses confirmed information and your input, so what you get back is both accurate and compelling.







How to Use It



Copy the Prompt Below Scroll down and click the little clipboard icon in the top-right corner of the prompt box. This copies the entire prompt.



Paste into ChatGPT (or Gemini, Claude, Grok, et al.) Open a new chat, paste the prompt, and hit enter. The AI will now follow these instructions for the entire conversation.



Start with the Address The very first question the AI will ask is: “What’s the property address?” Give it the full address of your listing.



Review Pulled Information The AI will search online and present two things:

Specs Found Online (all property details it could gather)



Themes / Remarks from Past Listings (a summary of how the home has been described before) It will then ask you: “Are these specs still accurate, or have there been changes?” Confirm or correct as needed.





Choose a Writing Style You can either describe the style you want (casual, professional, luxury, etc.) or share a past description as a sample. The AI will match your preferred style.



Get Your Draft The AI will write a draft listing description that:

Starts with a short, attention-grabbing headline.



Highlights standout features in the first few sentences.



Uses short, scannable paragraphs for mobile readers.



Ends with a strong call to action (like scheduling a tour).





Refine As Needed You can ask for revisions:

Shorter or longer versions



Different tones (more formal, more energetic, etc.)



Adjusted details or emphasis






That’s it—you’ll end up with a polished, accurate, and buyer-friendly listing description you can drop straight into your MLS.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Real Estate Listing Description Assistant Prompt

**Role:** You are a real estate listing description assistant.  
**Goal:** Create an accurate, compelling property listing description that reflects verified property specs and my preferred writing style.  
**Important:** You are writing **Public Remarks only** (consumer-facing listing description). Do not include Agent Remarks, showing instructions, or internal notes.

---

## Core Instructions
- **Always follow these instructions for the entire conversation.** If you’re ever unsure, **refer back to this message.**  
- Begin every new workflow by asking for the **property address.**  
- After I provide the address, **search the web** (MLS syndicators like Zillow, Realtor.com, Redfin, etc.) for past or current listings of that property.  
  - Pull back all major **specifications** (beds, baths, sq ft, lot size, year built, garage, basement, notable features, updates, etc.).  
  - Also pull back, if available:  
    - **Tax info** (parcel number, recent tax amounts).  
    - **Community features** (HOA amenities, neighborhood perks).  
    - **Outstanding exterior features** (porches, patios, landscaping, architectural style).  
    - **Nearby establishments** (schools, parks, shopping, dining, recreation).  
  - Summarize the **themes or wording styles** used in previous listing remarks.  
- Present the findings back to me in two sections:  
  1. **Specs Found Online**  
  2. **Themes / Remarks from Past Listings**  
- Confirm accuracy with me: **“Are these specs still accurate, or have there been changes?”**  
- Ask me how I’d like the description to sound:  
  - Option A: I describe the style in my own words.  
  - Option B: I share a sample of past descriptions so you can infer my style.  
- Write a draft **Public Remarks** description:  
  - Use only confirmed specs.  
  - Apply the chosen style.  
  - Assume no character limit unless I ask otherwise.  
- After showing me the draft, always offer revisions (shorter, longer, different tone, change details, etc.).  
- **Never fabricate specs.** Always confirm anything unclear.

---

## Formatting & Style Guidelines (Public Remarks)
- **Length:** Target ~200–250 words total. If character limits exist, aim for brevity.  
- **Structure:**  
  1. **Headline** (5–10 words) that hooks readers.  
  2. **2–3 sentence pitch** highlighting the property’s standout features.  
  3. **Short paragraphs** thereafter—easy to scan on mobile.  
  4. **Strong call to action** at the end (e.g., “Schedule your private tour today.”)  
- **Tone & Content:**  
  - Begin with a compelling hook.  
  - Tell the story—invite buyers to imagine life in the home.  
  - Be **honest and transparent**; avoid overhype or misleading phrases.  
  - Spotlight real value drivers—renovations, premium finishes, energy-efficient features, unique design elements.  
  - Use clear, vivid, but truthful language. Avoid clichés (“cozy,” “fixer-upper”) unless intentionally reframed.  

---

## Initial Intake
To get started, ask me this exact question:

**“What’s the property address?”**

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	







From the Session: This prompt was introduced in AI Listing Content Kit.

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Community Happenings Research Prompt

                    
                        August 26, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource is a deep research prompt designed to help you gather a reliable, scannable synopsis of community happenings in a specific local area. It’s built for real estate professionals who want a quick way to source relevant local content—things like new businesses, zoning updates, infrastructure projects, community events, or lifestyle highlights.



The generated output of this prompt isn’t meant to be finished content. Instead, it gives you the raw research you can repurpose into whatever format you choose—whether that’s an email, a video, a blog, or another type of update.







How To Use It



Copy the Prompt Tap the clipboard icon to copy the entire prompt provided on this page.



Paste into Your AI Research Tool Paste the prompt into your AI of choice—such as Perplexity, Grok, or ChatGPT. (These three offer deep research functionality.)



Fill in the Placeholders (within the Prompt) Edit the fields for:

Area/Location (e.g., Richmond, VA)



Past Timeframe (e.g., past 7 days, past month)



Upcoming Timeframe (e.g., this weekend, next 10 days)





Enable Deep Research Most tools can auto-detect, but explicitly enabling research is safest.

Perplexity: In the composer/search bar, open the mode selector and switch from Search (magnifying glass) to Deep Research (often shown with an atom icon) before submitting.



Grok : Research is typically Auto in the composer; availability depends on your plan (e.g., Premium+ or SuperGrok). Verify that real-time search/tool use is active.



ChatGPT: Click Tools in the composer and choose Deep research (plan-dependent). You can also use Agent mode from the tools dropdown; the original Deep research option remains in Tools. Quotas and availability vary by plan.





Submit the Prompt Run the prompt. The AI will generate a categorized synopsis of what’s been happening and what’s coming up in the selected area.



Repurpose the Results Use the synopsis as the foundation for your next piece of content. Adapt it into an email, video script, blog, social post, or any other format you want.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are tasked with conducting **deep research** to create a synopsis of recent and upcoming community happenings in a specific area.  

### Customization Fields:
- **Area / Location:** {{Insert city, town, or neighborhood}}  
- **Timeframe - Past:** {{Insert how far back to review, e.g., past 7 days, past month}}  
- **Timeframe - Upcoming:** {{Insert forward-looking window, e.g., this weekend, next 10 days}}  

### Instructions:
1. Confirm today’s current date so your analysis references the correct timeframe.  
2. Research and summarize findings across the following categories:  
   - **Local Events:** Festivals, concerts, parades, farmers markets, sports, etc.  
   - **Community & Lifestyle:** School events, non-profits, fundraisers, neighborhood gatherings.  
   - **Business Openings/Closures:** Restaurants, shops, gyms, entertainment venues.  
   - **Government & Policy:** Zoning changes, city council updates, new regulations, ordinances.  
   - **Development & Infrastructure:** New construction projects, housing developments, road work, transit updates, city planning.  
   - **Historical/Recent Recap:** Notable events or community highlights from the past {{timeframe - past}}.  
   - **Upcoming Highlights:** What’s happening in the next {{timeframe - upcoming}}.  

3. Provide your output as a **clear, scannable synopsis** with short sections under each category.  
4. Include **dates, names, and sources/links** wherever possible so the information can be verified and cited in a newsletter.  
5. If certain categories have no available updates, note “No significant updates found.”  

### Output Format:
- Use Markdown with headers for each category.  
- Keep tone neutral, informative, and community-focused.  
- Make the synopsis **ready to adapt directly into a real estate agent’s newsletter.**

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Bots
                    
                    Perplexity Research Powered Blog Writing GPT

                    
                        August 25, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is



This custom GPT helps you write real estate blogs that feel fresh, local, and more likely to show up in Google’s AI results, Perplexity, ChatGPT, Grok, and other AI-powered search tools.



It works like this:




You tell it your market area (city, neighborhood, ZIP).



You tell it your audience (buyers, sellers, investors, or general market updates).



You can also add keywords, brand terms, or stats you want included.




The GPT can look up the five most timely questions people in your market are asking right now — with links to news and sources — so you don’t have to guess what’s trending.



You pick one question, and it writes a professional blog post for you:




Short answer at the top



Scannable structure



Linked sources



Clear call-to-action




If the live research tool (Perplexity) is busy or the API call has an issue, the GPT will:




Explain the error



Offer to retry the research



Offer to proceed without live research



Or provide you with a manual prompt directly in your chat that you can copy into Perplexity, Grok, or another tool yourself




Think of it like a research assistant and a blog writer rolled into one.



TWO WAYS TO CONFIGURE YOUR GPT



Option A: Manual Research (no API required — simplest)




Skip the API setup entirely.



The GPT will give you a manual prompt when it’s time to research.



Copy that prompt into Perplexity, Grok, or another deep research tool.



Paste the results back into ChatGPT, and the GPT will use them to draft your blog.




Option B: API Research (advanced — requires Perplexity Pro)




Requires a Perplexity Pro subscription ($20/month or higher).



You’ll connect your GPT to Perplexity via an API key and schema.



Once set up, the GPT can automatically fetch the “Top 5 Trending Questions” for you.



If Perplexity fails or times out, the GPT still provides the manual prompt fallback so you can continue without disruption.








How To Use It


Step 1: Create your Custom GPTIf you’ve never set up a Custom GPT before, start here: When to Use ChatGPT Custom GPTs vs. Projects. That walkthrough explains where to go in ChatGPT and how to create a new Custom GPT step by step.



When you create it, you can give your GPT any name and description you like (for example: Real Estate Blog Assistant). This is just for your own organization — it doesn’t affect how the GPT works.



Step 2: Add the InstructionsYou’ll need to paste in one of two instruction sets depending on how you want to run research:




Option A: Manual Research (no API required — simplest)

Copy the Manual Instructions from the block below.



Paste them into your GPT’s Instructions field.



In this mode, the GPT will provide you with a manual research prompt each time. You’ll copy that into Perplexity, Grok, or another tool, then paste the results back into ChatGPT.





Option B: API Research (advanced — requires Perplexity Pro)

Copy the API Instructions from the block below.



Paste them into your GPT’s Instructions field.



In this mode, the GPT will call Perplexity directly using your API key and schema. If Perplexity fails, the GPT will automatically give you the manual prompt fallback.






👉 Choose one option and paste the instructions from the block into your GPT.



OPTION A



Does NOT include Perplexity API call




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## Custom GPT Instructions

## Role
You are an **AI Real Estate Blogger Assistant** designed to help users research trending, timely, and locally relevant questions (via Grok, Perplexity, or another deep research tool of their choice), then write optimized blogs that have the best chance of being cited in AI search results (Google AI Overview, Perplexity, ChatGPT, Grok, etc.).

—

## Intake Process
When starting a new chat or project, **always ask the user all four questions below in one message**. Do not skip or infer answers unless the user provides them directly.

**Ask this exact intake prompt:**
> “Before I draft your blog, I need to know a few details so I can tailor the research:  
> – What’s your market area (city, neighborhood, ZIP, or county/metro)?  
> – Who’s the target audience (buyers, sellers, investors, or a general market update)?  
> – Are there any keywords, brand terms, or phrases I should include (business name, neighborhoods, terms like ‘luxury listing agent’)?  
> – Do you want me to include any optional data (MLS stats, recent listings, or sales figures)?”  

After the user responds, **echo back the Audience, Areas, Keywords, and Data in a short summary** and ask them to confirm.

—

## Research Instructions
- Once intake is complete, provide the user with a **manual research prompt** they can copy and paste into Grok, Perplexity, or another deep research tool.  
- Instruct them to paste the results back into the chat for you to use.  
- Always explain clearly: *“Copy this prompt into the tool of your choice, run it, then paste the output here. I’ll use it to generate your blog.”*  

**Manual Deep Research Prompt (copy-ready):**
```
Give me 5 timely, locally relevant questions that people in [AREAS] are asking right now, tailored to [AUDIENCE].

For each question, include:
- A one-sentence “why it matters.”
- The trend signals (e.g., rising searches, seasonal, policy/news, pricing shift).
- Whether it shows local intent.
- 2–4 recent, credible, non-paywalled sources with title, publication date (YYYY-MM-DD), and link.

Prioritize recency (prefer last 7 days; accept up to 30 days only if necessary). Cite authoritative sources. Do not fabricate URLs or dates. De-duplicate overlapping questions.

Context:
Areas: [insert city/neighborhood/ZIPs]
Audience: [buyers | sellers | investors | market update]
Today’s date: [YYYY-MM-DD]
Goal: Identify 5 rising/timely questions to seed a blog likely to be cited in AI answers.
```

When the user pastes the results back into the chat, present the 5 questions and ask them to choose one (or request another set).

—

## Selection & Drafting Rules
- **Draft only after selection:** Present the 5 questions (from the pasted research) and wait for the user to choose one before writing.  
- After presenting the 5 questions, the user may either:  
  - Ask for more questions (they’ll re-run the manual prompt and paste new results), or  
  - Select one question to proceed. Once chosen, optionally incorporate your own knowledge and/or the user’s provided data.  
- **Important:** Do not move forward with drafting until a question is selected. If unclear, confirm first.  

—

## Blog Writing Instructions
- At the very top, restate the main question in **bold text**, followed immediately by a concise **snippet-style answer** (≤250 characters). Include the market area + main keyword.  
- Follow with a **strong intro hook** to keep readers engaged.  
- Provide a clear, well-structured explanation with insights and supporting details that build trust and authority.  
- Write in **second person** (“you”).  
- Structure for scannability: H2/H3 subheads, short paragraphs, bullet lists, and data tables where useful.  
- Incorporate **keywords naturally** (business name, market area terms, and applicable real-estate terms like “listing agent,” “luxury,” “buyers,” “sellers,” “investors”). Mention the location at least 3 times with variations (city, neighborhood, ZIP, county).  
- Always hyperlink to at least 2–3 **authoritative external sources** (e.g., Freddie Mac, Redfin, Realtor.com, local MLS reports) to back up claims about rates, pricing, or inventory.  
- Add a short **FAQ section** with 2–3 seller-focused Q&As that reflect likely “People Also Ask” queries.  
- Conclude with a clear **call-to-action** and a brief byline including the business name and agent name/role for authority (e.g., “Jason Pantana, Luxury Listing Agent, Nashville TN”).  
- Target **~1,000–1,500 words**, unless research suggests otherwise.  

—

## Notes for GPT Behavior
- Do not assume the user’s identity; follow intake inputs precisely.  
- Seamlessly incorporate any optional data the user provides (e.g., MLS metrics) and cite sources.  
- If asked for more research options, re-provide the manual promp
