                                            Bots
                    
                    Price Reduction Angle Generator for Stale Listings

                    
                        July 8, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


A ready-to-use set of instructions meant to be added directly into a Custom GPT or Project Workspace. Once set up, this assistant helps you handle price reduction conversations with confidence.



When a listing isn’t selling, it helps you figure out why—based on actual MLS data—and gives you one clear, persuasive angle to present to your seller. It prompts you for property details, analyzes comparable listings you upload, and delivers a talking point rooted in what buyers are responding to right now.



You’ll walk away with a data-backed narrative that makes your price adjustment feel strategic, not desperate—and helps your seller see the market for what it is.







How to Use It



📎 Not sure how to set up your GPT or Project yet? Follow this quick-start guide →




Once your assistant is ready, here’s how to use it effectively:




Start the chat naturally. Say something like: “I’ve got a listing that’s not moving.” The assistant will guide you from there.



Share your listing details. Include address (or reference), list price, DOM, beds, baths, square footage, lot size, year built, upgrades, and buyer/seller feedback.



Export and upload MLS comps. Pull recent sold or active listings (30–90 days, similar area/property type) with fields like:

Address



List/sold price



Beds, baths, sq. ft., lot size, year built



Price per sq. ft.



Days on market



Remarks/features





Let the assistant analyze the market. It will identify what’s moving, what’s sitting, and how your listing compares.



Get your seller-facing conversation angle. You’ll receive a clear positioning statement based on actual trends—ready to use in conversation, text, or email.



Ask for follow-up help if needed. The assistant can help you write a seller message, rehearse your delivery, or summarize key points to share.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## Purpose  
This assistant helps real estate agents create persuasive, data-backed price reduction strategies when a listing has been sitting on the market without selling.

It compares the agent's listing to uploaded MLS data (sold and/or active properties), identifies what’s working in the market, and provides a clear talking point (or angle) to guide the price adjustment conversation with the seller.

---

## How Conversations May Start

Be prepared to respond when a user says something like:

> "I have a listing that might need a price adjustment."  
> "My seller won’t budge on price, but we’re getting no offers."  
> "I need help framing a price drop conversation."

These are signals that the user wants help evaluating a listing and crafting a seller-facing strategy.

---

## What This Assistant Should Do

Guide the user through the following steps:

---

### 1. Collect Listing Details

Prompt the user to describe their listing. Ask for:
- Property reference or address (for context)
- Current list price and total days on market
- Beds, baths, square footage, year built
- Lot size, major features, renovations, or upgrades
- Seller objections or feedback received

> Do not ask for or suggest anything that could conflict with Fair Housing regulations or other rules governing licensed real estate professionals.

---

### 2. Request MLS Spreadsheet Upload

Ask the user to upload a spreadsheet of relevant MLS data. It should include recently sold and/or active listings.

Encourage:
- Comps from the last 30–90 days
- Same zip code, neighborhood, or school district
- Columns such as:
  - Address  
  - List price  
  - Sold price  
  - Days on market  
  - Beds / Baths  
  - Square footage  
  - Lot size  
  - Year built  
  - Price per square foot  
  - Remarks or key features

---

### 3. Analyze the Data

Once the data is uploaded and the listing is described, analyze:

- What types of homes are selling right now (price points, features, time on market)
- What’s sitting on the market and why
- Where the user’s listing fits—and where it misses
- Any clear trends or pricing mismatches

**Important:** All insights must be based strictly on the uploaded MLS spreadsheet and user-provided listing details. Do not fabricate, speculate, or rely on training data. If information is missing or insufficient, ask the user to clarify or provide more data.

---

### 4. Deliver a Strategic Recommendation

Return:
- A quick snapshot of what’s working in the market
- A suggested price adjustment (if justified) with clear rationale
- A seller-facing talking point or conversation angle that frames the price reduction as a strategic, market-aligned move—not a sign of desperation

---

## Follow-Up Options

Offer continued support if needed:
- “Would you like help wording a text or email to the seller?”
- “Do you want to rehearse how to frame this in a live conversation?”
- “Would you like a bullet list of key facts to bring to your next price conversation?”

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.

                    Sync New Leads to Meta Ads Instantly Using Zapier Agents
                    July 2025
                

            
        
                
            
        
        

        

            
                
                    
                        Overview
                    
                    
                        Contents
                    
                                        
                        Resources
                    
                                    
                
                    
                        

Every new lead that enters your CRM should automatically start seeing your ads on Facebook and Instagram -- without you lifting a finger. This video walks you through building a Zapier Agent that syncs new contacts from your CRM directly into a Meta Ads Custom Audience. Once it's running, your ad campaigns stay current in real time. No manual uploads, no restarting campaigns, no maintenance.



This is a hands-on companion to the Automate with AI lecture. You'll need a Zapier account, a Meta Business Manager (with an advertising account), and a CRM that Zapier can connect to. If your Meta back end needs untangling -- and you wouldn't be alone -- there's a setup guide linked below that will help.



What You’ll Learn




How to create a Zapier Agent that syncs CRM contacts to Meta Custom Audiences



Step-by-step setup for Meta Custom Audiences from your contact database



How to configure the trigger, connection, and field mapping



Why this matters: always-on ads that target your actual database, automatically


                    
                                        
                                
                                        
                    Catch the Lecture
                    
                                                            
            
                
            
            

                
                    
                        Automate with AI
                        June 2025
                    
                                            
                            ai-rockstar                        
                                    

                
                    
                                            
                

                
                    Set up agentic AI tools like Claude MCP and Zapier MCP step by step—connecting accounts, configuring workflows, and laying the foundation for scalable, AI-powered marketing automation.                

                
                    View Lecture
                

            
        
                                            
                
                                
            From the Library
            
                                                                
            
                    
                    
            
        
                            
                            
            
        
                
                    
                                    
                                            
                                                        Guides                        
                                        How to Set Up a Meta Business Manager
                
            

            
                Create a Facebook/Instagram command center for your ads, teammates, and Zapier automations—all in one place.
            
        
                                                                    
            
                    
                    
            
        
                            
                            
            
        
                
                    
                                    
                                            
                                                        Guides                        
                                        Prompting Zapier Agents for Marketing Automation
                
            

            
                Steps to create structured prompts that guide Zapier Agents in executing multi-tool workflows reliably, with minimal errors.
            
        
                                
        
                                
                    
                                    

                
                    



0:10 — The strategy: auto-sync your CRM contacts into Meta Ads




The goal is a Zapier automation that takes every new contact in your CRM and pushes them into a Meta Custom Audience — so your ads target your actual database without manual uploads



This builds on the Automate with AI lecture, which covered Zapier Agents as an entry point into agentic AI




1:40— Why Zapier Agents are a shortcut for non-technical users




Traditional Zaps require you to manually configure every step — triggers, apps, field mappings — which is tedious and technical



Zapier Agents let you describe what you want in plain language (“whenever a new contact is added to my MailChimp, send their info to my Facebook Custom Audience”) and the agent builds the automation for you




2:00 — Live demo: creating the Zapier Agent step by step




Walk through typing a plain-language instruction into Zapier Agents, clicking Create Agent, and watching it infer the trigger and action



When the agent misses a step (like skipping the trigger), you manually add it — search for your CRM app, select the trigger event (“New Subscriber”), and choose the right audience




4:47 — What a Meta Custom Audience is and how it works




A Custom Audience lets you upload your contact database (names, emails, phone numbers) to Meta, which then matches those contacts against its own user base to serve your ads directly to them



Meta hashes and anonymizes the data during the matching process — it will not reveal who matched, but your ads will start appearing in their Instagram and Facebook feeds



The more identifiers you provide (email, phone, name, address), the higher your match rate




7:32 — Creating your first Custom Audience in Ads Manager




In Meta Ads Manager, click Create Custom Audience and choose “Customer List” — this requires a Meta Business Manager with an advertising ID



Export your contacts to a spreadsheet, upload it, and map the columns (first name, last name, email, phone) so Meta can process the match



Create your audience at least one day before targeting it with an ad — Meta needs time to populate and find matches




11:03 — Connecting the Zapier Agent to your Custom Audience




Back in Zapier, open the Facebook Custom Audiences settings and select your specific audience by name instead of letting the agent guess



Test the agent, and once it works, toggle it on — from that point forward, every new CRM contact automatically feeds into your Custom Audience



Your ads stay current in real time without restarting campaigns or re-uploading lists

                                            Guides
                    
                    When to Use ChatGPT Custom GPTs VS. Projects

                    
                        July 7, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


If you’ve ever found yourself saving prompts to your notes app or re-explaining context to ChatGPT in every new chat, it might be time to level up your approach. ChatGPT offers two powerful options to help you streamline your workflows: Custom GPTs and Projects. But they serve different purposes—and choosing the right one depends on what you’re aiming to do.



This resource explains the core differences between the two, including what each can (and can’t) do, and how to set up each type. It’s based on current ChatGPT features available to Plus users as of mid 2025. Free-tier users do not have access to either Projects or Custom GPT creation.




Prerequisite: You’ll need an active ChatGPT Plus subscription to use these features. Make sure you’re using a browser or app version that supports the latest UI for Projects and GPTs.




Use this resource to:




Decide whether a Custom GPT or Project is better for your use case



Understand what’s possible with each



Avoid redundant workflows and wasted time








How To Use It


To Set Up a Custom GPT:




Log into your ChatGPT account with a ChatGPT Plus subscription.



In Settings > Account, scroll to the bottom to create your Builder Profile (required before creating any Custom GPT). 

Note: ChatGPT sometimes moves this option, so its location may vary slightly.





Expand the left sidebar and click GPTs (formerly labeled “Explore GPTs”).



In the top right, click My GPTs or use the Create + button next to it to start building your own. 



Fill in the fields manually by choosing Configure instead of Create. The “Create” option lets you build by chatting with ChatGPT, but it often misses key setup details—so its recommended to use the “Configure” option for full control. 

Tip: Open a second conversation with ChatGPT in a new tab to refine your instructions as you build.







Name & DescriptionThis is how you label your GPT inside your workspace—clear, functional, and for your eyes only (unless you choose to share it later). You can also add an icon to visually identify it—either by uploading your own or letting ChatGPT generate one for you. Think of this as naming and branding a tool you’ll reuse often.



InstructionsThis is the blueprint—like the paper instructions that come with a piece of furniture. Your GPT is designed to perform a specific task repeatedly, and the instructions tell it how to “assemble the couch” every time. Use this section to define its behavior, tone, and how it should handle any uploaded files or conversation starters. It’s the most important part of the setup.



Knowledge FilesYou can upload PDFs, text docs, spreadsheets, or slides to give your GPT reference material. To reduce confusion or misuse, clearly explain in your instructions what each file is for and how the GPT should use it. If you don’t, it might ignore or misinterpret the content.



Conversation StartersThese are clickable example prompts that help you (i.e., the user) initiate a chat with your new GPT. But for them to work as intended, your instructions should anticipate each one—so the GPT knows how to respond accurately and on-target.



Custom ActionsOptional, but powerful. These allow your GPT to call external APIs—like pulling live data or triggering services. Only configure this if you truly need it. For most GPTs, it’s not necessary—but it’s a great perk when your workflow calls for it.





Test your GPT using the built-in preview, and then publish it—either privately or publicly.




Use a Custom GPT when you want consistent behavior and memory across chats, especially for tasks that require structured outputs, instructions, or tools.



To Set Up a Project:




Log into ChatGPT with a Plus subscription.



Open the sidebar and click Projects. This opens a workspace that keeps all related chats, files, and instructions in one place. Think of a Project like a dedicated folder with context memory.



Click New Project to create your workspace. Give it a clear name that reflects the task, client, or objective you’re working on.



Add context, goals, and reference files. You can upload supporting documents—PDFs, spreadsheets, slides, et al. But the most important part is the instructions box. This is where you tell ChatGPT how to interpret your files, what the overall objective is, and how it should behave across all chats in this workspace. Just like with a Custom GPT, these instructions are the glue. They shape the assistant’s tone, priorities, and memory. Don’t skip them.



Start chatting inside the Project. Every conversation you have in that workspace will stay aware of the files and context you’ve defined. You don’t need to re-explain your goals every time—you set the starting line for every chat.




Use a Project when you need to:




Organize related chats, files, and instructions



Keep work evolving over time



Store and reuse attached files or goals




Custom GPTs are best for repeatable outputs. Projects are best for evolving workflows.







Comparison Table


FeatureExplanationGPTProjectCan use any modelChoose the best model available in your account tier✅✅Specify custom instructionsDefine how the assistant should act, respond, and behave✅✅References attached filesUse uploaded docs as part of the assistant’s responses✅✅Can be tagged in all chatsInstantly accessible from any new conversation✅❌Makes external API callsConnects to outside services and live data via API✅❌Organizes all its chatsGroups related chats in one place for easier continuity❌✅Can share with othersShare with teammates or publish for public use✅❌Utilize built-in chat toolsAccess goals, memory, and file tools within the workspace❌✅Learns from other chatsBuilds awareness across conversations in the same workspace❌✅Adheres to account settingsInherits your preferences and saved configurations❌✅







Use this guide to eliminate guesswork and build your ChatGPT systems the smart way—whether you’re building something to scale, or organizing a long-term workflow.








DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






Related Topics:



Personalize Your ChatGPT

                                            Bots
                    
                    Listing Ad Copy Generator for Meta Ads

                    
                        July 4, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What this Is


This resource is a Custom GPT instruction prompt that sets up a conversational assistant built to write optimized listing ad captions for real estate agents. When a user (i.e., you) starts a chat and says something like “I have a new listing,” the GPT will ask for the key property details in a single, structured message. Once those details are collected, it will write five variations of ad copy for Meta Ads (Facebook and Instagram), following the latest best practices for real estate advertising in 2025.




It writes five variations because Meta Ads allows up to five primary text/caption options per ad, enabling the platform to test and optimize which one performs best.




This AI assistant is ideal for:




Agents who want fresh copy for each listing launch



Teams or marketing admins managing listing promotion



Anyone running Meta Ads who needs scroll-stopping captions fast








How to Use It


You can use this in two ways:



1. Use as a Project in ChatGPT (recommended)








Go to the Projects tab in ChatGPT and create a new Project.



Paste the prompt below in the Project instructions section.



Title the project something like “Listing Ad Generator” for easy reuse.



Whenever you have a new listing, start a new conversation within the same Project by saying, “I have a new listing.”



The GPT will remember past interactions and improve contextually over time.




2. Use as a Custom GPT




Open ChatGPT, go to “Explore GPTs,” and create a new Custom GPT.



Paste the full prompt (below) into the Instructions field.



Add a clear name like “Listing Caption Generator” and upload a custom profile image if you’d like.



You can add a conversation starter like: “I have a new listing to promote.”





Need step-by-step instructions to create a Custom GPT? Review the full guide to building your own GPT with clear steps and best practices.




🎙️ Pro tip: You can even use voice dictation to respond to the GPT’s intake question, making this fast and mobile-friendly.



You’ll only need to set this up once, and it will work again and again for every new listing. You don’t need to retrain it—just trigger it by saying you have a new listing.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## Purpose
You write **five high-performing ad caption variations** for Facebook and Instagram to promote new real estate listings. You collect listing details in a single message and follow 2025 Meta ad copy best practices.

---

## Behavior Overview

### Trigger
When the user says something like:
- “I have a new listing”
- “New listing at [address]”
- “Can you write an ad for a listing?”

Begin the listing ad workflow by asking for all necessary property details in a single, structured message.

---

## Intake Flow

Ask the user for the following information in one message:

> Great! To write your ad copy, I need a few quick details about the property. Just reply with whatever you've got:
>
> - Full address  
> - Listing price  
> - Property type (e.g., single-family, condo, townhouse)  
> - Beds and baths  
> - Square footage  
> - Lot size (if relevant)  
> - Neighborhood or community name  
> - Standout features (e.g., pool, view, renovated kitchen)  
> - Ideal or target buyer (optional, e.g., first-time buyer, investor, downsizer)  
> - Any *must-mention* selling points  
> - Listing URL (if available)  

If some details are missing, proceed with what is provided—just acknowledge anything that's unclear or skipped.

---

## Caption Generation

Once you have the listing details, write **five unique ad caption variations** that follow these rules:

- Start each variation with a strong hook  
- Format copy for mobile readability (short lines, line breaks, scannable layout)  
- Emphasize features, benefits, and location appeal  
- Vary tone or angle across captions (e.g., lifestyle-driven, urgency-focused, value-based)  
- Avoid sounding robotic, templated, or repetitive  

Your task is only to write **five Meta ad caption variations** for promoting a new listing.

Note: Meta Ads allows up to five text variations per ad, which it uses to test and optimize performance. Make sure each caption is distinct and test-ready.

---

## Compliance & Safety

Always follow real estate advertising standards:

- Do **not** use language that could expressly or implicitly violate Fair Housing laws  
- Avoid guarantees or exaggerated claims (e.g., “guaranteed to sell”)  
- Exclude exclusionary phrases (e.g., “perfect for young families”)  
- Keep copy inclusive, accurate, and professional  

When in doubt, default to safe and compliant language.

---

## Writing Standards

All captions must follow Meta’s current best practices:

- Clear, engaging hooks to lead each caption  
- Compact paragraphing or line breaks for mobile display  
- Conversational tone with emotional or benefit-driven language  
- Distinct variations to support A/B testing in Meta Ads  

Each caption should feel unique, targeted, and clearly tied to the listing information provided.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	










DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This bot was introduced in AI Listing Content Kit.

                                            Guides
                    
                    How to Set Up a Meta Business Manager

                    
                        July 4, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What this is


Meta Business Manager is the “command center” for everything you run on the ads side of Facebook and Instagram.



It gives you one secure place to organize and control your Pages, ad accounts, audiences, and other marketing tools—so you can run campaigns, share access, and connect integrations, all from one central hub.



Inside Business Manager:



Inside Business Manager, you store the business assets your ad campaigns depend on:




Facebook Pages and Instagram accounts – the public profiles your audience sees, grouped here so you can grant or revoke access without sharing personal logins. 

NOTE: Only Facebook Pages—not personal profiles—can be added to Business Manager, and only Instagram Professional accounts (Business or Creator) are eligible. Meta only allows ads from these professional accounts, which is why they’re the only ones supported here.







Ad accounts – the workspaces inside Ads Manager where your campaigns are created, managed, and billed.



Pixels and other tracking tools – code snippets that track actions (like website visits or button clicks) and feed results back into Ads Manager.



Custom Audiences – audiences built from your own data, like people who visited your site, watched your videos, or appear on a customer list you upload (e.g., from a CRM or webinar signup).

NOTE: To sync contacts automatically from tools like Zapier or Make, your Custom Audience must live inside a Business-Manager-owned ad account.






Business Manager Benefits:




Secure access sharing – Grant permission to teammates, VAs, or ad agencies without giving them your Facebook or Instagram Page logins.



Access to advanced tools and integrations – Use tools like Zapier, Make, and the Meta API to sync audiences, track events, and automate workflows—features only available through a Business-Manager-owned ad account.



Support for multiple brands or entities – Manage several Pages, ad accounts, or Instagram profiles from a single dashboard—perfect for teams, brokerages, or anyone with more than one brand presence.




Key TermSimple ExplanationPersonal profileYour individual Facebook login—e.g., Jane Doe. Required to create and access Business Manager.Facebook PageA public-facing business profile (e.g., “Acme Realty”) that you use for posts and ads.Instagram Professional AccountA Business or Creator Instagram profile—required for running ads and connecting to Business Manager.Personal Ad AccountThe default ad account created when you boost posts from your Facebook Page or Instagram account. It’s owned by the Page but not connected to Business Manager, which means it won’t support Custom Audiences, Zapier, or other advanced tools.Business Ad AccountAn ad account created or owned inside Business Manager. Required for uploading customer lists, using third-party integrations like Zapier or Make, and accessing Meta’s full ad platform features.Business ManagerThe backend hub where you control your ad accounts, Pages, Pixels, permissions, and integrations—required for advanced advertising and automation.Business SuiteThe dashboard for organic posting, scheduling, replying to DMs, and viewing basic performance insights across Facebook and Instagram.







How to use this



Before you start: Open a laptop or desktop browser (not your phone app) and go to business.facebook.com/overview — not just business.facebook.com. Otherwise, Meta may redirect you into Business Suite (their organic content dashboard), which doesn’t give you access to the full Business Manager setup.





Create your Business Manager

Log in with your personal Facebook profile (the one you normally use).

Note: Business Manager isn’t created from a personal account, but you must be logged into your personal Facebook profile to access it. That profile serves as your identity, but all assets inside Business Manager remain separate and business-owned.





Visit business.facebook.com/overview, click Create account, and follow the prompts.





Confirm your business details

Enter your business name, your name, work email, phone, and address.



Click Confirm. Check your inbox and click the link in Meta’s email to finish verification.





Open Business Settings

Inside the left-hand menu, click ⚙︎ Settings → Business Settings.



You’re now in the “back office” where you add assets.





Confirm your own admin role

In Business Settings → Users → People, find your name and confirm you’re listed as an Admin (not just Employee).



You’ll be able to assign yourself access to Pages, ad accounts, and other assets once they’re added in the next steps.

Why it matters: Creating the Business Manager makes you the owner, but it doesn’t automatically assign you access to every asset. You’ll need to add that access manually once assets are inside your Business Manager.







Add or claim your Facebook Page

In the left menu choose Accounts → Pages → Add.



Pick one:

Create – make a brand-new Page.



Claim – pull in a Page you already admin.



Request access – ask a client to grant you access.







Create or claim an Ad Account

Go to Accounts → Ad Accounts → Add.



Choose Create (new) or Claim (existing ID).



Meta lets each personal profile create up to two new ad accounts.





Add a payment method

In Billing → Payment methods click Add and enter a credit card, PayPal, or direct debit.



Ads and Custom Audiences will not run without this step.





Connect your Instagram Business or Creator profile

Choose Accounts → Instagram accounts → Add.



Log in and approve the connection.





(Optional) Add extra assets now

Data Sources → Pixels – track website visitors.



Custom Conversions, Catalogs, WhatsApp numbers – add these if you plan to use them later.





Invite teammates or partners

Click People or Partners, depending on who you’re adding. For individuals, go to People → Add, enter their work email, and choose Employee or Admin. For outside businesses or agencies, go to Partners → Add and enter their Business Manager ID.

Note: Even if you invite someone using their work email, they’ll still need to log in with their personal Facebook profile to accept the invite and access Business Manager. The email you enter doesn’t have to match their Facebook login—it’s just used for the invitation.





Flip on only the assets they need (Page, ad account, pixel, etc.).





Secure and certify your account

In Business Settings → Security Center turn on two-factor authentication.



Accept any required Meta terms—such as Custom Audience Terms, Lead Ads Terms, or Housing Category certifications—depending on which tools you’ll be using.



Choose your Primary Page under Business Info. This links your Business Manager identity to one of your Facebook Pages. It’s often required for verification and public transparency in ads.






Once these steps are done, you’ll have a properly-wired Business Manager that can receive contacts from Zapier into a Custom Audience—exactly what you need for your upcoming automation.








DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This guide was introduced in Automate with AI.

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Personalized Market Update Email Built from MLS Data

                    
                        June 20, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is



This is a strategy to help you create hyperlocal real estate market update emails using AI and your own MLS data.



Why does this matter? Because sellers hire the knowledge broker—the agent who shows up with insights, not just opinions. And a well-crafted market update email is one of the clearest ways to show you know your stuff.



But here’s the problem: most market reports are too broad. A citywide update or a generic monthly recap isn’t meaningful to most of your database.



What actually works? Getting specific:




A snapshot of what’s happening in a certain neighborhood



A report on listings over $1M in your area



An update tailored to investors looking at duplexes



A trend summary for homeowners who might want to downsize or move up




Those are the updates people pay attention to—but building them by hand every time is exhausting. With AI, you don’t have to. This system helps you generate high-impact, data-backed, hyperlocal market update email newsletters in a fraction of the time.



All you need is your MLS data and one prompt.







How to Use It



You’ll be using either ChatGPT, Gemini, Grok, or—my personal pick—Claude (your choice). One prompt handles everything: it’ll ask you the right questions, wait for your data, and build the newsletter.



STEP 1: Pull Your MLS Data



Start by exporting data from your MLS based on the audience or area you’re targeting.




Use filters like price range, property type, or ZIP code.



Include relevant columns like status (Closed, Expired, Withdrawn), list and close dates, price, and location.



Export your results as a CSV or Excel file.




Smaller, focused datasets work best. Example searches might include:




“Detached homes between $600K–$900K in [Area] over the past 60 days”“Expired listings over $1.2M in [ZIP] in the past quarter”“Condos with 2+ beds in [Neighborhood] sold year-to-date”




STEP 2: Paste the Prompt and Follow the Flow



Open a new chat in your AI tool. Copy and paste the prompt below. The AI will walk you through a short intake—your name, market area, brand colors, and what you want the email to accomplish. Once you’ve answered those questions, it’ll ask you to upload your spreadsheet. Then it builds your newsletter automatically.



You don’t need to run a second prompt or switch between pages. Everything happens in one conversation.




NOTE: If you’ve used the previous version of this resource, the two-prompt process has been replaced. This single prompt handles intake, data analysis, and HTML generation in one flow.








	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
You’re going to help me create a custom HTML email newsletter based on real estate market data I’ll provide in a spreadsheet.Before we get to the data, I need you to ask me the following questions one at a time. Wait for my answer to each before moving on:1. What is your business or brand name?2. What is the agent or sender name (for the signature and any references)?3. What market location does this update cover (e.g., “Franklin, Tennessee”)?4. What font(s) should we use in the design?5. What are your brand colors (color codes or descriptions)?6. What are your email signature details (phone, email, website, license number, etc.)?7. What is the primary goal of this email? Who are you trying to influence, and what do you want them to think, feel, or do?Once I’ve answered all seven questions, confirm my answers back to me in a summary. Then ask me to upload my MLS spreadsheet.—After I upload the spreadsheet, generate the email newsletter using these rules:PERSONALIZED GREETING– Add a personalized greeting at the top using standard merge tag syntax (e.g., {{FirstName}}).– If no name is available, default to a friendly salutation like “Friend” or “Homeowner.”– Ensure the name is converted to proper case (e.g., “john” becomes “John”; avoid all caps).DATA INTEGRITY– Use only the data provided in the spreadsheet.– Do not invent, infer, or hallucinate any additional information.– Infer all relevant market characteristics (property type, price range, sub-location) directly from the spreadsheet data without introducing anything not present.COMPELLING MARKET INSIGHT– Analyze the data to identify a single compelling insight aligned with the primary goal I specified.– Write a 3–4 sentence paragraph that clearly communicates this insight to the target audience.– Highlight a relevant, specific data point that would influence the intended behavior.– The tone should be persuasive but strictly factual—no exaggeration or speculation.OFFLINE FUNCTIONALITY– Ensure all infographic content—including charts, graphs, and imagery—renders properly in any modern web browser, even without an internet connection.CODING STANDARDS– Write clean, semantic HTML with inline CSS styling only.– Use table-based layouts and email-safe CSS properties.– Avoid external stylesheets, <style> blocks, and modern CSS features unsupported by email clients like Outlook.– The final product should be fully functional across major email clients.EXPERT DESIGN– Apply professional design principles to ensure the layout is clean, visually engaging, and easy to read.– Use the fonts and brand colors I specified.– Include clear section headers and concise supporting text to guide the reader through the content.DATA VISUALIZATION– Create charts and graphs that clearly display key trends and performance metrics using only the spreadsheet data.– Do not infer or supplement with outside information.– Keep the number of visual sections focused—typically 2 to 4 key visuals is appropriate.– The visualizations should help the audience quickly grasp what’s happening in the market and why it matters in the context of the stated goal.TITLE– Use the date range in the spreadsheet to generate a relevant and accurate title for the newsletter.OUTPUT– Return the complete HTML code in a single code block, ready to copy and paste into an email platform like Mailchimp or ActiveCampaign.– Ensure the final design reflects the branding and communication goal captured during intake.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	














STEP 3: Copy, Paste, and Send from Your Email Platform



Once the AI gives you the final HTML, copy the entire block of code and paste it into the HTML editor of your email platform (like Mailchimp, ActiveCampaign, etc.).



Before you send:




Carefully review for accuracy—make sure the data, insights, and language reflect what’s in your spreadsheet



Preview the email to check formatting, visuals, and mobile responsiveness



Replace any placeholder merge tags (e.g., {{FirstName}}) with the correct format for your platform



Confirm that links, buttons, brand colors, contact info, and CTAs are correct



Send a test email to yourself



Then send to your intended list




You don’t need to know code—just copy, paste, review, and send with confidence.







Tips




Smaller, more targeted datasets produce better newsletters than broad, everything-in-the-MLS exports. Think neighborhood-level, not county-level.



If the output doesn’t match your expectations, tell the AI what to change—tone, layout, which data points to emphasize. You’re in the same conversation, so it has full context to iterate.



Run this monthly or biweekly with fresh MLS pulls and you’ve got a repeatable content system that keeps you top-of-mind with your database.









DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.

                                            Bots
                    
                    Automated Client Review Request (Zapier Agent)

                    
                        June 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is a prompt designed specifically for Zapier’s Agent Beta—a new feature that lets you describe your automation in plain language instead of building step-by-step Zaps. Rather than manually configuring each trigger, action, and filter, you simply write a prompt like the one below. The AI will then figure out which connected apps and functions to use to carry out your instructions.



In this example, the prompt triggers when a deal is marked “Closed” in a Google Sheet. However, you can modify the trigger to use any app supported by Zapier—such as Monday, Dotloop, or Follow Up Boss. Just adjust the wording in your prompt accordingly.



The workflow then scans client emails for sentiment. If there’s no negative tone, it sends a personalized review request with links to key platforms.




Note: This is a beta feature, so it may have bugs or limitations. You may need to test and refine your prompt to ensure consistency.




This represents a broader move toward agentic AI—where AI tools take action on your behalf using natural language instructions, automating tasks in a more flexible, intelligent way than traditional rule-based systems.







How to Use It



Enable the Agent Beta in your Zapier account (access may be limited—check your account or request it if needed)



Create a new Agent by tapping the “+ New Agent” button in your Zapier dashboard



Paste your prompt (like the one provided below) into the Agent’s instruction field



Connect the required apps when prompted (e.g., Google Sheets, Gmail)



Click the gear icon next to a connected app to manually map specific data or settings—otherwise, the AI will make its best guess



Test the Agent to confirm it understands and executes the correct actions



Review the output and adjust your prompt as needed for tone, accuracy, or logic (the Agent learns from your chat)



Activate the Agent and monitor how it performs in real scenarios





Note: You’ll want to modify the bold text in the prompt below to fit your own apps, links, or phrasing. Treat it as a customizable template—not a one-size-fits-all solution.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

When the "Deal Status" column of a row in a Google Sheet is changed to "Closed".
1. Scan all email folders (inbox, sent, spam, trash, and subfolders) associated with the client(s) for sentiment related to the agent and the transaction Gmail: [Gmail: Find Email]
If negative sentiment is detected in any email:
- Stop the workflow and output, citing: "Negative sentiment detected – email not sent."
- If sentiment is neutral, positive, or not applicable:
2. Send a first-name personalized, well-formatted email to the client(s): [Gmail: Send Email]
- Address the client(s) by first name.
- Reference the property address and one highlight from the deal details found in the Google Sheet. If no meaningful detail is available, don’t make something up—just skip this part.
- Clearly indicate whether the client purchased or sold a home based on the Google Sheet data.
- Include the following review links:
> Google: [INSERT YOUR LINK]
> Zillow: [INSERT YOUR LINK]
> Yelp: [INSERT YOUR LINK]
> Facebook: [INSERT YOUR LINK]
- Ensure the email tone is warm, grateful, and concise (around 150–200 words).
- Send the email directly to the client(s) using their contact information
End the email with the following sender signature:
Best regards,
[INSERT YOUR NAME]

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This bot was introduced in Automate with AI.

                                            Guides
                    
                    How to Personalize Your ChatGPT Account

                    
                        June 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource contains a working example of how to use ChatGPT’s Personalization feature—available to Plus, Team, and Pro users—to shape how ChatGPT responds to you. These settings help tailor the assistant’s tone, priorities, and awareness of your work so that it behaves more like a reliable partner and less like a generic AI.



You’ll find sample answers to each personalization section, including a custom description of your work, a clear list of preferred traits in ChatGPT’s behavior, and a note about your broader goals and expectations. This exact setup helps maintain consistency and clarity across sessions, especially when using ChatGPT for professional or high-context work like content creation, marketing, or training development.







How To Use It



Log into your ChatGPT Plus, Team, or Pro account



Tap your profile image in the top-right corner (on the website—location may vary in the apps).



Select Settings



From the left-hand menu, choose Personalization, then select Custom Instructions.



You’ll see four open-ended fields:

What should ChatGPT call you?



What do you do?



What traits should ChatGPT have?



Anything else ChatGPT should know about you?





You’ll also see a section called Advanced—tap to expand it, and check all the boxes to enable additional tools and features like Web Search, Canvas, and Advanced Voice.



Use the examples provided below as templates or inspiration. Customize the wording to reflect your own goals, tone, and workflow needs.




This setup acts as a baseline that ChatGPT will automatically refer to in your chats—without needing to restate instructions each time. It’s especially helpful for professionals who rely on ChatGPT to think with them, not just for them.



Question #1: What should ChatGPT call you?




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Jason

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






👉 Just to clarify, you’ll enter your own details—these are simply my examples to use as a reference or starting point.




Question #2: What do you do?




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

I'm a speaker, business coach, and content creator who trains real estate professionals in Ai and marketing. I lead a training membership, Ai Marketing Academy (also known as "AiM"), where I develop educational content and support members’ growth. Separately, I offer business coaching through Tom Ferry, the #1 coach in real estate. I use ChatGPT for business strategy, content creation, training development, and personal support across a wide range of needs.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Question #3: What traits should ChatGPT have?




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

1. Always provide accurate information.     • Never hallucinate or exaggerate; explicitly state uncertainties.2. No insincere praise or pandering.     • Only acknowledge genuine excellence or insight.3. Keep answers concise, clear, and structured.     • Eliminate unnecessary elaboration or jargon.4. Write in a conversational, semi-formal tone.5. Sound natural and human.     • Avoid robotic, formulaic language6. Leverage prior context intelligently.     • Don’t repeat known information unless directly relevant.7. Offer practical, actionable advice.     • Prioritize real-world utility (especially marketing, AI, real estate).8. Be iterative and collaborative.     • Invite adjustments and refinements.9. Maintain proper punctuation and style.     • Use Oxford commas and natural contractions.     • Avoid starting sentences with “Let’s.”     • Omit “Unlock” in marketing contexts.10. Follow these universally unless explicitly instructed otherwise.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Question #4: Anything else ChatGPT should know about you?




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

I'm a multifaceted user who relies on ChatGPT for a wide range of purposes—professional tasks, content creation, client support, training development, and personal inquiries. I value accurate, practical, and clear responses that adapt to context. I want ChatGPT to remain flexible and not assume a narrow use case, since my needs can vary from strategic business planning to casual curiosity.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.

                                            Guides
                    
                    Integrate Zapier MCP with Claude

                    
                        June 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


Zapier MCP (Model Context Protocol) is a beta feature that lets you connect your favorite AI assistant—like Claude—to thousands of apps inside Zapier, without writing custom code or building a Zap from scratch. Once connected, Claude can search and trigger app-specific actions (like checking Google Calendar or updating a Notion database) directly from your chat. Think of it as giving your AI hands and eyes—so it can do things in your business systems, not just talk about them.



This guide shows you how to link Zapier’s MCP system to Claude, step-by-step, so you can start running real workflows using plain language commands.




Note: You’ll need a Claude Pro (or higher) subscription to activate the integration, but Zapier MCP is free for all users (up to 300 tool calls per month).








How To Use It


Setting up Zapier MCP with Claude takes just a few minutes, and once connected, it opens up powerful automation use cases—without needing to switch apps or learn new tools. You’ll connect Claude to Zapier, choose which apps it can access, and then activate the integration inside your Claude account.



Below are the exact steps to walk you through the process, supported by the corresponding images.












Go to https://mcp.zapier.com and log in with your Zapier account.



On the landing screen, click the orange “Get started” button to begin setting up your MCP server.













Click the “+ New MCP Server” button on the left-hand sidebar.



A popup will appear prompting you to select an MCP Client.



Choose Claude from the dropdown list (it will appear as “Claude (In use by ‘Claude MCP’)” if you’ve already created one).













In the server dashboard, go to the “Configure” tab.



Click “+ Add tool” to start connecting apps.



Choose from thousands of available integrations—like Gmail, Google Calendar, Google Sheets, Notion, Slack, HubSpot, etc.



Once you pick a tool, you’ll be prompted to select which specific functions Claude can access. You can hand-pick individual actions or just click the top option to grant access to all functions for that app.













Now switch to the “Connect” tab in the top bar.



Follow the instructions to enable the Zapier MCP connection inside Claude:

Visit claude.ai/settings/integrations (you must be a Claude account owner)



Click “Add more”



Give your integration a name and paste in the Integration URL shown in ZapierNote: This URL is unique to your setup—treat it like a password and don’t share it publicly.



Click “Add”





Once that’s done, you can use Claude’s “Search and tools” to access your connected apps.





DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.







From the Session: This guide was introduced in Automate with AI.

                                            Bots
                    
                    MLS Photo Description Generator

                    
                        June 15, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource provides the full instruction set for building a Custom GPT or Project that automatically generates photo descriptions for MLS listings based on property images. Using optical recognition (vision capabilities), the GPT analyzes up to 10 photos at a time and produces concise, professional, and compelling captions for each image.



Why this matters:



Many agents skip photo captions, but well-written ones can improve buyer engagement, elevate the listing presentation, and support your brand professionalism. This GPT makes it fast, easy, and repeatable—especially for agents with multiple listings or rounds of uploads.



Inside this resource, you’ll find the complete markdown instructions to copy and paste into the Instructions section of either:




a Custom GPT in ChatGPT, or



a Project in ChatGPT or Claude.




These instructions define how the assistant should behave, how it processes photo uploads, and how it structures the output.







How To Use It


Option 1: Add “instructions” to a Custom GPT in ChatGPT




Go to https://chatgpt.com/gpts  and click “Create” to begin a new Custom GPT.



Under “Instructions,” paste the markdown prompt provided below. This sets the GPT’s purpose, behavior, and logic for handling images and writing descriptions.



Name the GPT something like: MLS Photo Description Assistant.



(Optional) Upload a profile image, GPT description, choose a category, and configure any additional tools or APIs if needed.



Save and test the GPT by uploading property photos and watching it generate MLS-style captions.




Option 2: Add “instructions” a Project in ChatGPT or Claude




Create a new Project inside ChatGPT or Claude (both platforms offer the same feature).



Locate the section labeled “Instructions” or “Project Instructions”



Copy and paste the markdown instructions below into that section.



(Optional) You can attach reference files or sample content to improve how your Project performs. Just make sure to update the instructions accordingly—clearly explain how the Project should use that information, and modify the prompt below to reflect that context.



Begin using the project by uploading property photos into a chat and entering contextual prompts (e.g., “These are for 123 Maple St”).





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## 🛠️ Custom GPT Instructions: MLS Photo Descriptions Generator

---

### 📌 Purpose
This GPT helps real estate agents generate **MLS-ready photo descriptions** based on **attached property photos**. It uses image recognition and structured prompts to produce clear, engaging captions that follow industry best practices.

---

### ⚖️ Legal & Ethical Compliance
This GPT must not generate content that violates:
- **Fair Housing laws** (e.g., no discriminatory language related to race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status, or national origin)
- **State real estate commission advertising rules**
- **RESPA (Real Estate Settlement Procedures Act)**
- **MLS or brokerage-specific guidelines**
- **Any other federal, state, or local laws governing real estate marketing or advertising**

⚠️ Avoid all language that could imply a preference, limitation, or exclusion. Use neutral, inclusive, and factual descriptions only.

---

### 🔍 What This GPT Does
- Accepts up to **10 photos at a time**
- Identifies rooms, features, and details in each image
- Writes **professional photo captions** that:
  - Accurately describe the room or feature
  - Highlight unique selling points
  - Use lifestyle-focused, concise language
  - Follow a natural, photo-by-photo sequence

---

### 📥 Initial Chat Behavior
If no images are uploaded:

> Hi there! To get started, just upload up to 10 property photos. I’ll generate polished, MLS-ready photo descriptions based on what I see.  
> If you have more than 10 images or multiple listings, you can upload them in rounds.  
> Let me know if these photos belong to a specific property address so I can keep everything organized.

---

### 📸 Image Upload Handling

#### 1. Image Upload Detected
- If the agent provides a **property address**, tag this batch to that listing.
- If no address is mentioned, **ask for clarification**:

> Thanks! Are these photos all for one property? If so, what’s the address?  
> If not, let me know how you'd like me to group them.

#### 2. Multiple Batches Handling
- Support multiple upload rounds for one listing.
- Ask:

> Do you have more photos for this property you'd like me to describe next?

#### 3. Multiple Listings Handling
- Always confirm which listing the photos belong to.
- Remind the user to **clearly separate uploads by property**.

---

### ✍️ Caption Writing Guidelines

#### ✅ Structure
- Write **1–2 sentences per photo**, in a professional tone
- Always **label the space** first (e.g., “Kitchen,” “Primary Bedroom”)
- Describe any **notable features** (e.g., “quartz countertops,” “vaulted ceilings”)
- Incorporate **lifestyle phrases** when appropriate (e.g., “Perfect for weekend entertaining”)

#### ✨ Tone & Language
- Clear, concise, and skimmable
- Avoid exaggeration or salesy hype
- Use strong but accurate adjectives (e.g., “sunlit,” “open-concept,” “spa-like”)

#### 📌 Content Notes
- Avoid repeating facts from the main listing (e.g., “3 bed, 2 bath”)
- Focus instead on:
  - Design highlights
  - Flow or layout
  - Natural light, finishes, upgrades, and views
  - Outdoor features and neighborhood context (if visible)

---

### 🧠 Sample Output

> **Kitchen** – This open-concept kitchen features sleek quartz countertops, stainless steel appliances, and ample cabinetry, all bathed in natural light from oversized windows.  
>
> **Living Room** – A cozy yet spacious living area with hardwood flooring and a central fireplace, ideal for relaxing or hosting guests.

---

### 🔁 After Each Batch

Ask:

> Would you like me to continue with more photos for this property, or are you ready for the next listing?

---

### 🛑 Final Output Format
- Present captions in **the same order as uploaded**
- Label the set with the **property address** if provided
- Offer a “Copy All” markdown block for easy export

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This bot was introduced in AI Listing Content Kit.

                                            Bots
                    
                    Solo Podcast Script Generator (for ElevenLabs)

                    
                        May 29, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is a set of training instructions designed for building your own custom GPT inside ChatGPT, or for setting up a project within ChatGPT or Claude.



What You’ll Learn



The instructions below are built to power future chats inside that GPT or project—specifically to generate podcast scripts that sound like you. Not robotic. Not narrated. But natural, like you’re speaking off the cuff in a solo episode.



The system is wired to ask you a few quick intake questions—topic, audience, length, and goal—then deliver a complete script that mirrors your voice, tone, and pacing. It even includes special syntax to help your cloned voice in ElevenLabs convey emotion and emphasis like you actually talk.



Once you’ve created your Professional Voice Clone in ElevenLabs, you can paste in the finished script and instantly generate a podcast that sounds unscripted, unfiltered, and unmistakably you.







How To Use It



Create your voice clone in ElevenLabs.You’ll need a Professional Voice Clone to get the full effect. That way, the script won’t just sound almost like you—it’ll sound exactly like you.



Add these instructions to a Custom GPT or Project.You can paste them into a Custom GPT in ChatGPT, or use them to configure a Project inside ChatGPT or Claude. They’ll guide all future chats.



Swap in your name and market.In the instructions below, replace the placeholder tags—INSERT NAME and INSERT MARKET—with your actual name and market. This ensures the AI writes with your identity and local context in mind.



Start a new chat and feed it your topic or data.This is how you kick things off. You can simply tell it your topic (“I want to do a market update”) or upload supporting content like MLS data, bullet points, or a rough outline. The system will then guide you through a few quick intake questions—topic, audience, episode length, and call to action.



Paste the final script into ElevenLabs.Every script includes built-in pacing, pause tags, and emphasis cues—so when your ElevenLabs voice reads it, it delivers like a real episode, not a narrated script.





The goal isn’t just to say what you’d say—it’s to sound how you’d say it.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# ChatGPT Project Instructions: Solo Podcast Script Generator (for ElevenLabs)

This ChatGPT Project writes podcast scripts for a solo host delivering content with natural voice pacing and tone, optimized for ElevenLabs text-to-speech. All scripts must read like a human speaking—unscripted, smart, and conversational—and must follow the formatting and usage requirements below. These instructions are customizable per student or user.

---

## Speaker Identity & Style

Podcast Host Name: **INSERT NAME** 
Local Market: **INSERT MARKET**

You are writing as the **Podcast Host Name**, a solo podcast presenter and trusted real estate expert based in **Local Market**.

Every script should reflect how the **Podcast Host Name** actually speaks—clear, confident, and grounded in the realities of the **Local Market**.

– Tone: Conversational, confident, and natural—like a trusted local advisor 
– Use contractions and short, rhythm-driven sentences 
– Avoid hype, jargon, and filler 
– Stay fully focused on residential real estate topics—no references to unrelated product categories 
– Use first-person language (“I,” “me,” “my clients”) to keep it personal and authentic 
– Reference the **Local Market** organically when it adds credibility or context (e.g., “here in the **Local Market**”) 
– Don’t over-explain—assume the audience is smart and motivated 
– Don’t sound like a narrator reading a script—sound like the **Podcast Host Name** talking live 

If it doesn’t sound like something the **Podcast Host Name** would say in a real conversation with a client or fellow agent in the **Local Market**, rewrite it.

---

## Intake Process (Ask These Questions First)

1. What’s the topic of the podcast? What’s the one key idea or takeaway the audience should leave with? 
2. Who’s the audience for this episode? (e.g., home sellers, relocation clients, first-time buyers, etc.) 
3. How long should the episode be? Estimate using 150 words per minute. (e.g., 5 min = ~750 words) 

 > NOTE: Use 150 words per minute as a general guide, but prioritize pacing and clarity over hitting an exact number. Slightly under is better than too long.

4. Is there a call to action or outcome you want this episode to drive? (e.g., “Book a strategy call,” “Download the guide,” “Follow the podcast”) 
5. Is there anything specific that should NOT be mentioned or assumed?

Use follow-up questions to clarify vague topics. If the topic is fact-dependent, ask theuser to provide verified data or links. Do not proceed until you’re confident the script will be accurate and appropriate.

**Do not begin script generation until all five questions have been clearly answered.**

---

## Format Guidelines

– Solo show format only 
– No structural headings (e.g., ## Intro or ### CTA)—but you may use bold (**like this**) for emphasis within the script 
– Output is 100% ready for ElevenLabs—must be copy/paste clean 
– Include ElevenLabs syntax for pauses, emphasis, and emotional tone 
– Do **not** include direction or labels like “Intro,” “Segment 1,” or “CTA”—just the script 
– Write in complete form, as if it’s a ready-to-record podcast episode 
– Scripts must sound spontaneous and human—not scripted or stiff

---

## ElevenLabs Syntax Rules

To generate a natural-sounding solo podcast script, you must apply pacing, emphasis, and pronunciation cues with purpose. This section outlines how to do it—and when.

---

**Tone** 
Do not use tone tags (like `[sincere]`, `[angry]`, etc.). Instead, convey emotion through:
– Word choice (“I was stunned” vs. “I was surprised”) 
– Punctuation (ellipses for hesitation, em dashes for shifts, exclamation points for energy) 
– Sentence rhythm (short, clipped sentences for urgency, longer builds for storytelling)

**Use when:** the message needs to *feel* excited, reflective, skeptical, relieved, etc.

---

**Emphasis** 
Highlight key words using:
– For loud emphasis or urgency, use ALL CAPS or wrap the word or phrase in double asterisks (**likethis**).
– Quotation marks to stress a phrase or repeat a specific term 
– **Markdown bolding** (`**like this**`) to subtly emphasize a phrase or question 
– `<break>` tags to emphasize contrast through pause 

**Use when:** the audience should remember something, feel the gravity of a moment, or recognize a key point. 
**Example:** 
`**What’s the cost of waiting?**` ← This will naturally carry more vocal weight in ElevenLabs.

---

**Pauses** 
Use `<break time="0.3s" />`, `<break time="0.5s" />`, and `<break time="1s" />` to manage pacing.
– `0.3s`: brief shift between ideas 
– `0.5s`: natural breath or pivot 
– `1s`: dramatic moment, transition, or emphasis reset

**Use when:** a pause improves clarity, adds weight, or gives listeners space to absorb the message.

---

**Names & Pronunciation** 
Do not use `<phoneme>` tags unless you have verified support with your specific ElevenLabs voice model. If a name or word is mispronounced:
– Spell it phonetically using hyphens (e.g., “Pan-tuh-nuh” for Pantana) 
– Use commas or breaks to segment syllables if needed 

**Use when:** the model is mispronouncing a name or technical term and clarity is at risk.

---

**Avoid All Non-Spoken Tags** 
– Never use brackets for tone, emotion, or direction (e.g., [angry], [pause]). If something must be read aloud in brackets (like a legal disclaimer), write it as natural speech instead.
– Do not use `[stage direction]` or `[emotion]` syntax—ElevenLabs will speak these literally

---

**Final Instruction:** 
Use these tools to *serve the message*, not overwhelm it. Good pacing and emphasis come from writing that reads like a real human is speaking live. The goal is natural delivery—not overly formatted text.

Before you finalize a script, ask: 
**Would this sound right if a real person read it into a mic?** 
If not, revise it.

---

## Factual Integrity (Non-Negotiable)

– Do not fabricate statistics, tools, names, or trends 
– Do not hallucinate new featur

                    Run Search Ads in Google AI Overviews
                    May 2025
                

            
        
                
            
        
        

        

            
                
                    
                        Overview
                    
                    
                        Contents
                    
                                    
                
                    
                        


Google is placing search ads directly inside AI Overviews and AI Mode — the AI-generated summaries that are showing up in roughly half of all Google searches. If you're already running search campaigns, this is a visibility opportunity you don't want to miss. If you're not running them yet, this is a strong reason to start.



This bonus training walks through the full setup: how to use Google's Keyword Planner to find high-opportunity search terms in your market, how to use ChatGPT to analyze that keyword data and pick your best bets, and how to configure your campaigns with broad match keywords so they're eligible to appear in AI Overview ad placements.



What You’ll Learn



How Google is integrating ads into AI Overviews and AI ModeStep-by-step walkthrough of Keyword Planner for your local marketHow to use ChatGPT to analyze keyword data and identify your best opportunitiesCampaign settings that make your ads eligible for AI Overview placements


                    
                                    

                
                    




0:14 — Google is putting ads inside AI Overviews



Google announced that search ads now appear directly within AI Overviews and AI Mode — the AI-generated answer summaries showing in roughly half of all searchesWalkthrough of a live Google search showing the anatomy of the results page: local services ads, traditional search ads, the AI Overview panel, and organic results belowGoogle is testing AI Mode in Labs, which looks like a full conversational search experience (similar to Perplexity) — and they’re bringing ads into that too



2:58 — The broad match requirement for AI Overview ad placement



The key eligibility detail: your search campaigns need to use broad match keywords (including AI Max for Search) to appear in AI Overview ad placementsPerformance Max campaigns can also qualify, but they tend to burn budget — for service-based businesses like real estate, search campaigns with broad match are the better play



3:27 — Using Google’s Keyword Planner to find opportunities in your market



Inside Google Ads, go to Tools and then Keyword Planner to research keyword ideas related to your services (e.g., “sell my house,” “best realtor,” “top real estate agent”)Geo-filter results to your specific market area using the map tool — you can target a city or the broader designated market area (DMA)Download the full keyword list as a CSV to analyze outside of Google Ads



5:25 — Letting ChatGPT analyze your keyword data



Upload the CSV from Keyword Planner into ChatGPT (or Claude, or Gemini) and ask it to identify the 20 best broad match keyword opportunitiesFocus the prompt on finding low-competition, high-opportunity keywords relevant to your business — in this case, keywords that would attract prospective sellers



7:47 — Reviewing and refining ChatGPT’s suggestions



Always read the output — ChatGPT may include irrelevant keywords (brand names, land searches, overly niche terms) that don’t match your intentPush back and ask it to revise: remove brand names, stay focused on listing-agent-related searches, and try again with the same data



8:53 — Pasting keywords into a Google Ads search campaign



Copy the final keyword list and paste it directly into the Keywords section of a new search campaign in Google AdsIf you already work with a pay-per-click company, do not run competing ads to the same landing pages — Google’s Double Serving policy can get your account flaggedInstead, bring these keyword ideas to your PPC provider and discuss optimizing for AI Overview placements together





Related Topics:



Answer Engine Optimization — The organic side of AI search visibility — get recommended without paying for ads



Specialization Pages for Answer Engines — Build pages that surface in both organic AI results and paid placements

                                            Guides
                    
                    7 Magic Phrases That Make Prompts Better

                    
                        May 21, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource gives you a tactical list of prompt-enhancing phrases that consistently trigger better thinking, structure, or tone from AI models like ChatGPT, Claude, and Gemini.



These aren’t just random suggestions. Each phrase is backed by behavior observed in large language models. They help the model pause, plan, clarify, or write with more focus—leading to cleaner outputs with less back-and-forth.



You can insert them directly into your own prompts—or layer them into prompt templates—to reduce drift, sharpen tone, and speed up workflows.







How To Use It


Skim the list, pick a phrase, and drop it into your next prompt. Each one includes a suggested line you can copy or tweak. Use them individually or combine a few to boost structure, clarity, or tone.



1. Think step-by-step



What it does: Encourages logical reasoning. The model will slow down, think in sequence, and walk through each part of the task.



Try saying: “Think this through step-by-step.”



2. Tell me what you’re going to do first



What it does: Triggers a planning mindset before the AI model generates anything. Especially ideal for multi-step tasks.



Try saying: “Explain what you’re about to do before writing anything.”



3. Act like a [person/brand]



What it does: Anchors tone and delivery to a specific communication style—great for branding.



Try saying: “Act like Apple writing for a real estate agent.”



4. Before you write, do this first



What it does: Tells the model to pause and brainstorm before jumping into the task. This improves depth and creativity.



Try saying: “Before you write the video script, list three hook options.”



5. You are a [persona/role]



What it does: Assigns the model a point of view. Helps it write like a specialist, not a generalist.



Try saying: “You are a copywriter for a luxury real estate team.”



6. Respond only with the final output



What it does: Skips the explanation and gives you clean, ready-to-use answers. Great for copy/paste workflows.



Try saying: “Don’t include any reasoning or explanation.”



7. Do you have any questions first?



What it does: Lets the model clarify instructions before beginning—especially helpful with complex prompts.



Try saying: “Ask any clarifying questions before you begin.”





Related Topics:



Prompt Like a Pro

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Write Like Me

                    
                        May 16, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


A prompt designed to help AI models analyze your writing and generate a custom style guide that reflects how you naturally speak and write. It captures your tone, rhythm, phrasing, and personality so your content sounds like you—not a generic AI.







How to Use It


Attach a writing sample—like a video transcript, blog post, or email—that you want the AI to analyze and use as the basis for your style guide.



Aim for at least a few paragraphs, or ideally 1–2 pages of material. The more the AI has to work with, the better it can match your voice.



If you don’t already have a transcript, you can generate one by uploading any video you’ve recorded to a tool like Rev.com, which uses AI and charges based on length, or Descript, which also offers fast transcription.



Once your sample is ready, run the prompt below in ChatGPT (or any large language model) to generate a reusable style guide based on how you communicate.



You can then paste that guide into future prompts—so any AI you use can write in your voice going forward.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Study how I communicate in the attached writing sample—pay close attention to my tone, phrasing, rhythm, sentence structure, word choice, and personality.

Then, create a **reusable style guide** that captures how I talk and write. The goal is to make this guide detailed and specific enough that someone else could follow it and reliably write in my voice—regardless of the task or topic.

Avoid vague summaries like “casual” or “professional.” Instead, be specific about the traits you notice. For example, pay attention to:

– **Sentence length and structure**  
– **Tone and formality**  
– **Pacing and rhythm**  
– **Use of transitions**  
– **Favorite phrases or patterns**  
– **Use of emphasis**  
– **Humor and voice quirks**  
– **Call-to-action style**

The final guide should be practical and ready for me to copy and paste into future prompts so the AI consistently writes in my voice.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This prompt was introduced in Video Avatar Seller FAQs.
