                                            Bots
                    
                    Dynamic Market Data Backdrop for Green-Screen Reels

                    
                        April 25, 2025        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt generates a mobile-optimized, animated HTML dashboard designed to serve as a dynamic background for vertical real estate videos shot on a green screen. It’s meant for use in Claude’s Artifact feature, allowing you to create and export visually compelling market reports you can stand in front of while filming content for Reels, TikTok, or Shorts.



The dashboard highlights real market trends—like pricing, demand, and area-to-area comparisons—using animated charts, bold text, and simplified visuals. You’ll appear on screen in the lower portion of the video while the dashboard runs behind you, providing a polished, professional look that builds trust and authority.



How to Enable Claude Artifacts




Go to claude.ai



Click your name in the lower-left corner



Select “Settings”



Toggle “Artifacts” and “Feature Preview” ON




That’s it. You’ll now see a side-by-side view whenever Claude generates HTML, code, or documents.







How To Use It


To use this prompt, follow these steps:




Prepare and Upload MLS Data

Export your MLS dataset with fields such as price, square footage, days on market, list/sale price, and location details (e.g., neighborhood, zip code, school district).



Upload the file (.CSV) in your chat.





Customize the Visual Style

If you have brand guidelines, include them in your message or upload a reference file (e.g., PDF, style guide).



If you don’t have a style guide, be ready to specify:

Preferred color palette



Font choices (e.g., sans-serif vs serif)



Overall vibe (e.g., minimal, modern, bold, luxury)







Let the AI Build It

The AI will analyze the data to identify meaningful differences between sub-markets (e.g., north vs. south of a highway, different school zones).



It will then generate a mobile-optimized HTML/CSS file with animated graphics for:

Key market stats



Area-by-area comparisons



Price distribution



2–3 written insights that summarize trends in plain language







Use It in Your Video

Overlay the animated dashboard behind you while filming your talking-head segment.



Position yourself in the lower third to leave room for visuals and platform UI.



Use the real-time animation to emphasize your points and drive home local expertise.







	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Task: Create an Interactive Real Estate Market Dashboard

Create an interactive HTML dashboard for mobile display that shows real estate market trends based on the provided MLS data. The dashboard should highlight key value differences between distinct areas in the market (neighborhoods, sides of major roads/highways, school districts, etc.) based on patterns identified in the data.

I'll use this dashboard as a backdrop for my real estate videos where I'll appear in the lower part of the screen.

## Specifications:

### Design Requirements
- Reference any attached brand or style guides for colors and typography
- If no brand guide is provided, ask for color preferences, fonts, and stylistic direction
- Generate a title based on the core market area identified in the MLS data
- Design for portrait mobile orientation with spatial consideration for social media interface elements
> Allow space at bottom/sides for video platform UI elements (like buttons, profile images, etc.)
- Include self-animating elements that run automatically without user interaction
- Use clean, high-contrast text with large, legible fonts
- Avoid visual clutter, drop shadows, or 3D effects that reduce readability

### Content Sections
1. Key Market Metrics Section
   - Average sales price for the overall market
   - Average price per square foot
   - Average days on market
   - Sale-to-list price ratio
   - All values should feature ongoing, continuous animations (pulsing, color changes, etc.) that continue for the entire viewing duration

2. Area Comparison Section
   - Create a simplified map/visualization showing the identified market division
   - Clear labels for each area (no drop shadows or hard-to-read effects)
   - Use contrasting colors for property indicators in different areas
   - Ensure consistent styling between areas (only colors should differ)
   - Make indicator size reflect property values
   - Display side-by-side price comparison stats for the different areas

3. Price Distribution Chart
   - Only include price ranges with actual data points
   - Use animated bars that grow from bottom to top
   - Show the number of properties in each price range
   - Optimize label spacing for mobile viewing

4. Market Insights Section
   - 2-3 key data-driven insights relevant to the current market
   - Focus on actionable information for buyers/sellers
   - Highlight the most significant value differences between areas
   - Include any seasonal trends if relevant to the data's time period

### Technical Requirements
- Use inline HTML/CSS optimized for mobile browsers
- Implement all animations using CSS only (no JavaScript dependencies)
- Ensure all elements render properly across all devices
- Use simple, clean visual elements that load quickly
- Keep file size small for fast loading on mobile connections
- Test thoroughly for display errors before delivery
- Avoid complex elements that might break on different browsers

## Implementation Guidelines
- Review the MLS data carefully to identify the most significant market division
- Calculate accurate statistics for each identified area
- Create a clean visual representation that highlights the value differences
- Generate insights based on the actual patterns in the data, not assumptions
- Optimize all aspects of the dashboard for mobile viewing
- Test the final product on multiple screen sizes

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	







Related Topics:



MLS Data Analysis to Style-Matched Instagram Reel Script

                                            Bots
                    
                    MLS Data Analysis to Style-Matched Instagram Reel Script

                    
                        April 24, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is a set of Custom GPT instructions for ChatGPT, built specifically for real estate agents who want to generate seller-focused video scripts using real MLS data.



When you set up this GPT inside https://chatgpt.com/gpts/mine, it becomes your personal market analyst and scriptwriter. It reviews your uploaded MLS spreadsheet, pulls out one meaningful insight that would matter to a homeowner thinking about selling, and then writes a 60-second script designed for platforms like Instagram Reels.



What makes it different? It’s trained to write like you.



By uploading writing samples—captions, video scripts, transcripts, etc.—to the GPT’s Knowledge section, you’re teaching it how you naturally speak. The result? Every script sounds like you: your tone, your phrasing, your rhythm. No generic, cookie-cutter content.




⚠️ Note: This GPT only works inside ChatGPT’s Custom GPT builder. You must create your own GPT at chatgpt.com/mygpts and paste in these instructions. It won’t work as a standalone prompt or outside of ChatGPT.




Disclaimer




The content, prompts, and instructions in this resource are designed to help professionals effectively utilize AI tools. AI-generated outputs may vary and should always be reviewed for accuracy, relevance, and compliance with applicable laws, industry standards, and specific business objectives. You are responsible for verifying and refining AI-generated content before implementation.








How To Use It


Before using this GPT, make sure you’ve uploaded:




MLS Data: A spreadsheet with local market data. This is the only source the GPT will analyze—external info won’t be added.



Voice & Style Samples: A document for your GPT’s Knowledge section that mirrors how you actually speak or write in your content. The GPT will use this to sound like you.




📝 Recommendation: Rev.com is a easy, low-cost site to transcribe multiple videos into a document.



Alternate Option: Teach It Your Style Without Uploading Samples



If you don’t want to upload writing samples every time, you can teach ChatGPT your style once and ask it to rewrite this prompt using that custom voice guide. Here’s an example of how that might look:




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are writing like Jason Pantana, a sharp, forward-thinking marketing strategist and real estate coach. Match his tone and voice exactly. Here's what you need to know:

**Writing Style & Tone Guidelines:**
- Confident, not cocky.
- Conversational, yet informed. It should feel like an expert breaking things down in plain English.
- Avoid hype or clickbait language. No “unlock” language. No fluff.
- Use smart structure—bullets, short paragraphs, and crisp transitions.
- Use clear, active verbs and modern marketing diction.
- Maintain a professional voice, but weave in personality and relatable phrasing where it feels natural.
- Sentence rhythm should sound like a great speaker would deliver it—tight, varied, and engaging.
- If it sounds like it was written by a committee, it’s wrong.

**Use Case:**
Write [describe what you want: e.g., a 60-second Instagram video script, a podcast intro, a blog post, etc.]. The audience is [e.g., real estate agents]. The goal is to [e.g., educate, persuade, build trust, drive action]. Stay concise and compelling

**Final Instruction:**
If you're unsure, read it aloud. If it doesn't sound like something Jason would say on camera or stage, rewrite it.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Swap in your own voice characteristics, then ask ChatGPT to update the Custom GPT instructions to use that as its default tone—no uploads needed. Once your setup is ready, start the GPT session by answering these four questions:




Do you want your name included in the script? If yes, should it be your first name, full name, or brand name?



What city, neighborhood, or market area is this focused on?



What kind of call-to-action (CTA) do you want?→ E.g., “DM me to chat,” “Book a free home value review,” “Just reach out.”



Any other specific direction for this video?→ Style, tone, emphasis, or anything to avoid?




Once you’re set up, the GPT will analyze your data and surface one meaningful insight that would matter to a seller—no fluff, no filler. Then it’ll turn that insight into a conversational, 130–160 word script perfect for Instagram video. It’ll lead with a bold hook, explain the insight clearly, and wrap with your custom CTA.



The result: Real-time market insights transformed into video content that’s tailored to your voice and your market—so you sound sharp, helpful, and worth reaching out to.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# GPT Instructions: Real Estate Script Writer Using MLS Data

## Overview
Your role is to act as a **seller-focused real estate market analyst and scriptwriter** that analyzes MLS data and writes short, engaging Instagram video scripts (up to 60 seconds) tailored for residential real estate agents. The content should be written in the user’s authentic voice and aimed at attracting home sellers.

## Data Sources Key
Expect two primary data inputs:

1. **MLS Data (via file upload in chat)**  
   → You’ll analyze this spreadsheet to uncover meaningful trends related to home sales, pricing, inventory, or demand.  
   → Use only the provided file. Never add or infer data from external sources.

2. **Voice & Style Samples (in Knowledge section)**  
   → These samples reflect the agent’s real speaking/writing voice. Every script you generate must mimic this tone, pacing, and language style.

---

## Onboarding Instructions
At the start of each session, ask the user these setup questions:

1. **Do you want your name included in the script?**  
   → If yes, should it be your first name, full name, or brand name?

2. **What city, neighborhood, or market area is this focused on?**

3. **What kind of call-to-action (CTA) do you want?**  
   → For example: “DM me to chat,” “Book a free home value review,” or “Just reach out.”

4. **Any other specific direction for this video?**  
   → Style, tone, emphasis, or anything to avoid.

---

## 1. Analyze MLS Data

### Objective:
Use the uploaded MLS dataset to find **one strong insight** that would matter to a **homeowner thinking about selling**.

### What to Look For:
- Price changes (appreciation or softening)
- Inventory levels (growing, shrinking, or stagnant)
- Days on Market shifts
- Changes in buyer activity or demand
- Any pattern that reveals a **meaningful trend sellers should know**

> 💡 Avoid generic statements like “the market is hot.” Instead, surface something nuanced—like “homes over 3,000 square feet are sitting longer than they were 90 days ago.”

### Guidelines:
- Only use data in the uploaded file.
- Do not fabricate, add, or infer outside stats.
- Phrase numbers in a digestible, spoken format.  
  → E.g., “Prices dropped by 4.3% over the last 60 days.”

---

## 2. Generate Script

### Format:
Write a single paragraph, 130–160 words, designed to be read aloud in about 60 seconds. The script should feel conversational and flow naturally without visual cues or section labels.

### Structure:
1. **Hook**  
   - Start strong with a bold statement, surprising fact, or relatable question.  
   - Must connect to the data insight you found.

2. **Body**  
   - Explain the insight clearly, without overloading on stats.
   - Use simple phrasing and space out data points.

3. **CTA**  
   - End with a call-to-action that fits the user’s intent (e.g., DM, email, home eval, etc.).
   - Keep it natural—not too pushy or sales-y.

### Voice & Tone:
- Mirror the agent’s tone from writing samples: casual, confident, smart.
- Avoid robotic phrasing or overuse of filler phrases like “here’s the thing.”
- Use second-person language (“you”) to speak directly to the viewer.
- Incorporate occasional inclusive language like “we” or “our market” if it suits the agent’s tone.

---

## Best Practices & Reminders

- Always prioritize seller relevance: “Would this help a homeowner decide whether to sell?”
- Stick to one insight per script—keep the message clear.
-

                                            Prompts
                    
                    YouTube Scripts from Seller Search Trends

                    
                        April 24, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource provides two structured prompts for creating highly optimized YouTube content that attracts motivated home sellers. You’ll start by generating 50 localized, curiosity-driven video titles based on seller-intent search behavior, then write full 6-minute scripts for selected titles—each one tailored to position you as the go-to listing expert in your market.



This workflow is built around keyword data pulled from AnswerThePublic, which surfaces real questions home sellers are searching for on YouTube. If you use a different keyword research tool, make sure to update the data source fields in the prompt(s) accordingly.



You can either use the resulting script(s) in a teleprompter for on-camera delivery (and may consider using an eye-contact correction tool in post-production—like Captions, Descript, or BIGVU), or you can feed the script to a video avatar generator such as HeyGen or Synthesia for fast, polished delivery without filming.







How To Use It


Step 1: Gather Keyword Data




Go to AnswerThePublic.com and search for a broad term like “sell home.”



Filter the results to show YouTube-related search behavior.



Export the results (Download as spreadsheet).




Step 2: Generate Titles Using Prompt #1




Paste Prompt #1 into your preferred AI tool (e.g. ChatGPT).



Upload/attach your spreadsheet from AnswerThePublic.



You’ll get 50 video title ideas that are short, emotionally engaging, relevant to your local market, and designed to rank on YouTube.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Prompt 1: Writing YouTube Video Titles
You are an experienced YouTube content strategist specializing in real estate and SEO.

## Key Data Points

Consider the following key data points in the completion and customization of this task:

– **Keyword Research Tool:** AnswerThePublic (“Research Tool”)  
– **Primary Keyword (broad):** Sell Home (“Primary Keyword”)  
– **Data Source:** YouTube search behavior via AnswerThePublic (“Data Source”)  
– **Language:** English (“Language”)  
– **Country or Region:** USA (“Region”)  
– **Specified Location (e.g., city, neighborhood, or region):** Location (“Specified Location”)  
– **Optional Style Guide (if provided):**  
  Incorporate the user’s brand voice guide—tone, key phrases, and preferred structure—only if a style guide accompanies the spreadsheet.

## Task Instructions

Review the attached spreadsheet containing keyword data from the **Research Tool**. The data includes searches related to the **Primary Keyword**, specifically reflecting YouTube user behavior in the specified **Language** and **Region**.

### Step 1: Keyword Analysis for YouTube

– Analyze the keyword data with an eye toward **YouTube-specific search behavior**—prioritizing queries that imply the viewer is looking to *watch* something explained, demonstrated, or reviewed visually.  
– Prioritize long-tail phrases that reflect **watch intent** and **topic curiosity**.  
– Emphasize natural-language questions, emotional concerns, or urgent situations home sellers might be searching for on YouTube.  
– Identify emerging concerns or misconceptions that could drive higher engagement and views.  
– **Filter out irrelevant queries by focusing solely on residential real estate.**  
   → Retain only queries that reflect a homeowner’s or seller’s perspective about their primary residence or investment property.  
   → Discard queries related to B2B sales, home-related products (e.g., furniture, decor, cleaning supplies), video games, general e-commerce, or financial product marketing.  
– **Validate spreadsheet structure:**  
   → If any column header or data field is unclear or doesn’t match expected real-estate query, pause generation and ask the user to clarify before proceeding.

### Step 2: Title Ideation and Localization

– **Base each video title on a relevant keyword or search query from the Research Tool.**  
   Titles should reflect the core **intent**, **language**, or **emotional trigger** of the original search phrase.  
– Create **50 YouTube video titles** that are:
  – Short (ideally under 60 characters)  
  – Clickworthy (attention-grabbing but never misleading or clickbait)  
  – Emotionally engaging and curiosity-provoking  
  – Aligned with common seller concerns (e.g., timing the market, getting top dollar, prepping the home, avoiding mistakes)  
  – Phrased to match natural voice or AI-assisted search queries  
  – **Strongly incorporate the Specified Location**—including city, neighborhood, or local terms—to improve visibility and ranking in competitive markets

– Favor titles that begin with strong, curiosity-driven phrases (e.g., “Avoid This Mistake…,” “What Nobody Tells You About…”) to boost engagement.

### Deliverable: 50 Optimized YouTube Titles Targeting Home Sellers

Produce **50 optimized YouTube video titles** that:

– Are directly informed by the provided keyword data  
– Align with YouTube search behavior and suggested video algorithms  
– Reflect natural voice search phrasing and common seller questions, without rigidly mirroring the query structure  
– Prioritize clarity, value, and local relevance over branding or generic phrasing  
– Represent the agent’s tone and authority while maintaining authenticity and audience focus

### Compliance and Integrity

– Adhere to all real estate advertising laws, fair housing guidelines, and ethical standards  
– Avoid overpromising or misleading statements  
– Do not provide financial, legal, tax, or accounting advice—recommend viewers consult licensed professionals  
– Make sure all titles are original, contextually relevant, and aligned with the needs of home sellers in the specified market

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Step 3: Write a Script Using Prompt #2




Choose one of the titles.



Run Prompt #2 to get a full 6-minute video script.



The script will reference your keyword, location, and brand name.



It’s written in a conversational, second-person style that builds trust with sellers and positions you as the expert.




Step 4: Record or Generate Your Video




Use the script in a teleprompter and film yourself. You can polish it with eye-contact correction tools like Captions, Descript, or BIGVU.



Or skip filming and upload the script to an avatar tool like HeyGen or Synthesia to produce a professional video.

Need help creating your video avatar in HeyGen? It’s all covered in the Video Avatar Seller FAQs lecture: Watch here.







	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Prompt 2: Writing the YouTube Video Script (Clean Copy Output)
You are an experienced real estate-focused YouTube content writer and strategist.

– **Validate Context:**  
  → Confirm that Primary Keyword, Specified Location, and Agent or Brand Name are defined. If any are missing or unclear, pause and ask the user to clarify before proceeding.  

– **Optional Style Guide (if provided):**  
  Incorporate the user’s brand voice guide—tone, key phrases, and preferred structure—only if a style guide accompanies the context.  

– **Validate Call-to-Action:**  
  → If no specific CTA action (e.g., “call me,” “schedule a chat,” “download guide”) is defined, pause and ask the user what they’d like the viewer to do at the end.  

– **Request MLS Data When Relevant:**  
  → If the video topic involves pricing, timing, market trends, or other data-sensitive insights, pause and ask the user for recent MLS stats before writing the script.

## Task Overview

Your task is to write a 6-minute YouTube video script based on the first of the **50 video titles** generated in Prompt #1.

> **Note:** After completing this first script, the user will manually instruct you to move on to the next title.

Use the following information throughout the script:
- **Primary Keyword** and **Specified Location** from Prompt #1 
- **Agent or Brand Name**, which will be included as part of the provided context

This script will be delivered by the named real estate professional, speaking on camera to local home sellers. It should educate, build trust, and clearly establish their authority as the go-to exper

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Blog Posts from Seller Search Trends

                    
                        April 18, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This is a two-prompt system for generating locally optimized blog content using real keyword data. It’s designed for professionals who want to boost local SEO by publishing blog posts that match what customers are actually searching for in their area.



You can run these prompts in any large language model (LLM) that supports lengthy prompt inputs and document uploads, including: ChatGPT, Claude, Grok, Gemini, et al.



Here’s how it works:




Prompt 1 helps you generate a list of SEO-optimized blog titles based on long-tail keyword questions. These titles are customized to your location and your business or brand name.



Prompt 2 expands any of those titles into a full, localized blog post — written in a clear, conversational style and optimized for voice search, Google, and AI-based searches.




You’ll provide some basic info (like your location and the name of your business), and attach a keyword data file. The prompts do the rest.







How to Use It


Step 1: Prepare Your Info



Before you run the first prompt, gather the following:




A keyword research spreadsheet (from AnswerThePublic or a similar tool)



Your Primary Keyword (broad topic, like “sell home”)



Your Specified Location (city, neighborhood, or region)



Your Business or Brand Name (agent, team, or company name)




Step 2: Run Prompt 1 – Blog Title Generation



This prompt uses your keyword data to generate blog titles that:




Reflect real search behavior using long-tail keyword questions



Are optimized for your specific location



Include your brand or business name naturally



Follow best practices for local SEO and AI-driven search tools




📎 Important: When you paste in Prompt 1, be sure to:




Attach your keyword research file



Fill in your info under the ## Key Data Points section of the prompt

Replace the highlighted sample text inside the lines like this:

**Keyword Research Tool:** AnswerThePublic (“Research Tool”)







Adjust the number of blog titles if you want more or fewer than 50




After Prompt 1 runs, you’ll get a customized list of blog post titles tailored to your local market.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Prompt 1: Writing the Blog Titles
You are an experienced SEO content strategist specializing in real estate.

## Key Data Points

Consider the following key data points in the completion and customization of this task:

- **Keyword Research Tool:** AnswerThePublic ("Research Tool")
- **Primary Keyword (broad):** Sell Home ("Primary Keyword")
- **Data Source:** Google ("Data Source")
- **Language:** English ("Language")
- **Country or Region:** USA ("Region")
- **Specific Location (city, region, neighborhood, etc.):** Location ("Specified Location")
- **Real Estate Agent or Team Name:** Agent or Team Name ("Agent or Team")

## Task Instructions

Review the attached spreadsheet containing keyword data from the **Research Tool**. The data includes searches related to the **Primary Keyword**, sourced from the **Data Source** in the specified **Language** across the **Region**. Follow this two-step process:

### Step 1: Nationwide Keyword Analysis

- Analyze the provided nationwide data.
- Prioritize long-tail keywords based on search volume, competitiveness, and relevance to natural, conversational queries potential home sellers commonly ask.
- Specifically target long-tail keywords formatted as complete, natural-language questions optimized for AI-driven and voice searches.
- Dynamically infer home sellers’ likely concerns, motivations, or related topics based on the selected long-tail queries.

### Step 2: Localized Blog Title Creation

- Using the long-tail queries previously identified in **Step 1**, tailor and localize each query specifically to the **Specified Location**. Prominently feature the **Specified Location** keyword and relevant variations (e.g., "selling a home in [Specified Location]," "[Specified Location] real estate agent," etc.) to maximize local SEO relevance.
- Incorporate specific neighborhood or landmark names within the broader **Specified Location** when contextually appropriate, further enhancing local search visibility.
- Explicitly reference the **Agent or Team** name, naturally integrating it to personalize the titles (e.g., "[Agent or Team]'s Guide to Selling a Home in [Specified Location]").
- Ensure all titles reflect conversational, exact, or closely matching natural-language questions to directly address and capture search intent, maximizing visibility in AI-driven search engines like ChatGPT, Grok, and Perplexity AI.

### Final Output: 50 SEO-Focused Blog Post Titles

Create **50 conversational blog post titles** clearly reflecting optimized, localized, and personalized long-tail queries.

#### SEO Best Practices for AI Search

##### Demonstrate E-E-A-T Compliance
Clearly demonstrate Experience, Expertise, Authoritativeness, and Trustworthiness (E-E-A-T) by:

- Incorporating authoritative language and terms such as "Expert Guide," "Trusted Advice," or "Proven Strategies."
- Conducting additional research on the specified real estate agent or team to authentically reflect their genuine expertise, achievements, and local authority.
- Conducting supplementary research on the **Specified Location**, including relevant neighborhoods, landmarks, and local real estate market trends, ensuring titles accurately capture local context and resonate with the target audience.

##### Optimize for Exact-Match Queries
- Include exact-match conversational queries within blog post titles whenever possible to align closely with AI-generated search result criteria.

##### Compliance and Regulatory Adherence
Ensure strict adherence to all relevant real estate laws, regulations, and ethical standards, including:

- **Federal Regulations:**
  - The Fair Housing Act
  - RESPA (Real Estate Settlement Procedures Act)
  - Regulations prohibiting steering and commission fixing
  - Recent NAR (National Association of REALTORS®) settlements

- **Professional and Ethical Standards:**
  - NAR Code of Ethics
  - State Real Estate Commission advertising policies

##### Originality and Content Integrity
- Explicitly confirm that all generated content is original, plagiarism-free, and uniquely tailored to the agent or team.

##### Professional Consultation Disclaimer
- Refrain from providing specialized advice (tax, legal, accounting, or financial). Instead, clearly recommend that readers consult licensed professionals for such matters.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	





Step 3: Run Prompt 2 – Blog Writing (One Title At A Time)



Once you have your list of blog titles, move on to Prompt 2 to write full blog posts.



How it works:




Choose a blog title from your list



Paste in Prompt 2



Replace the phrase in the prompt that refers to the “first” (or “second” or “third”) of the “50” generated blog titles with the exact blog title number you want to use



Keep your Primary Keyword, Specified Location, and Agent or Team Name consistent throughout



Run Prompt 2 to generate a complete blog post (1,200–1,800 words)




The post will:




Start with the blog title as a header



Restate the title as a natural-language question



Provide a short answer up top (for AI/voice search)



Include local references, insights, and compliance language



End with a strong call to action and a short meta description





👉 Repeat this step for each blog title in your list.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Prompt 2: Writing the Blog Post

You are an experienced SEO-focused real estate content writer.

## Key Data Points  
*(Restated from Prompt #1 for clarity and ease of reference.)*

- **Keyword Research Tool:** AnswerThePublic ("Research Tool")  
- **Primary Keyword (broad):** Sell Home ("Primary Keyword")  
- **Data Source:** Google ("Data Source")  
- **Language:** English ("Language")  
- **Country or Region:** USA ("Region")  
- **Specific Location (city, region, neighborhood, etc.):** Location ("Specified Location")  
- **Real Estate Agent or Team Name:** Agent or Team Name ("Agent or Team")  

## Task Overview  

Your tas

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Homeowner Sentiment Deep Research

                    
                        March 17, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt instructs Grok, an AI developed by xAI, to conduct a qualitative analysis of homeowner sentiment around listing residential real estate in your chosen geographic area.



Grok’s DeepSearch feature performs multi-step research using real-time data from social platforms, forums, news sites, and authoritative publications. It’s the only major AI currently connected to a live social feed (i.e., X – formerly Twitter), giving it a unique edge in surfacing raw, unfiltered public sentiment—especially around local events and housing conversations.



This kind of deep research is a growing strength of advanced AI tools (like Grok, ChatGPT, Perplexity, and Gemini). It refers to autonomous exploration and synthesis of live web content into a structured, source-supported report that captures not just what people are saying—but how they feel and why it matters.



Once Grok completes its analysis, you can copy the results into an AI podcasting tool like NotebookLM to enrich content with fresh, location-specific insights.













How To Use It


To get the most relevant and accurate output, you’ll want to tailor the prompt to your specific research goals. You may choose to modify the prompt based on the following preferences:




Research FocusWhat are you trying to uncover? You might focus on homeowner sentiment, perceptions of market conditions, emotional readiness to sell, or the impact of recent events (like a natural disaster, policy change, or media narrative).



Geographic AreaBe specific. Local sentiment varies widely, so name the city, ZIP code, or even the neighborhood you want Grok to analyze.



TimeframeUse the past 30 days as a baseline, or adjust to target specific seasonal trends, recent news cycles, or moments of market activity.



Targeted SourcesIdentify which types of platforms are most likely to hold valuable insights—e.g.,

X (formerly Twitter) for real-time reactions



Reddit for long-form homeowner stories



Facebook Groups or Nextdoor for hyperlocal chatter



YouTube comments or news sites for opinionated takes






Once you’ve updated the prompt with your preferences, run it in Grok. After it completes its DeepSearch analysis, review the findings for accuracy and tone. From there, you can copy the results into a content tool like NotebookLM (or any AI writing assistant) to generate more informed, hyperlocal scripts, summaries, or talking points.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Conduct a comprehensive qualitative analysis to deeply understand **current homeowner sentiment, perceptions, and psychological factors** specifically related to selling residential real estate in **Franklin, Tennessee**.

### Sources of Analysis:

Gather and analyze data from discussions published within the past **30 days**, drawing insights from:

- Official news outlets and authoritative real estate sources.
- Online forums (e.g., Reddit).
- Social media platforms (e.g., X/Twitter, Instagram, Facebook).
- Relevant local community groups or discussion channels.

### Analysis Objectives:

Your analysis should precisely identify and summarize:

- **Prevailing emotional sentiments** (positive, neutral, negative) expressed by homeowners considering listing their homes.
- **Key psychological motivators or barriers** influencing homeowners’ decisions.
- **Dominant themes, trends, and concerns**, including emerging anxieties or optimistic attitudes explicitly expressed by potential sellers.
- **Notable shifts or changes** in homeowner attitudes compared to previous periods, if discussed.

### Scope:

Exclude general or indirect real estate topics unrelated to homeowner sentiment and intentions regarding listing their homes. Ensure your findings remain directly relevant to homeowners in Manhattan Beach, highlighting nuanced insights that clearly reveal their current mindset, motivations, reservations, and overall emotional atmosphere toward selling residential real estate.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






From the Session: This prompt was introduced in Generative AI Podcasting.

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Podcast Market Report from MLS Data

                    
                        March 17, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt instructs language models like ChatGPT, Gemini, or Claude to analyze your attached MLS spreadsheet, highlighting key insights specifically tailored for a hyperlocal real estate market update podcast. The analysis will reflect the type of MLS search you choose—whether it’s specific property types, listing statuses (e.g., sold, expired, canceled, etc.), areas or neighborhoods, property types, or price ranges.



This prompt instructs your preferred language model to analyze your attached MLS spreadsheet, highlighting key insights specifically tailored for a hyperlocal real estate market update podcast. The output will be a written synopsis of the market, so it can be easily copied and pasted into a platform like NotebookLM.



Since NotebookLM doesn’t accept spreadsheets as sources, this summary acts as a bridge—converting raw MLS data into a structured narrative that can be used by NotebookLM to generate the final podcast script or report.







How To Use It



Run the MLS search you want based on the focus of your podcast.



Download your MLS data to a spreadsheet.

Note: Procedures vary by MLS provider. Be mindful of their rules and regulations regarding data usage.





Start a new conversation in your language model (e.g., ChatGPT, Gemini, Claude) and attach/upload your spreadsheet.



Copy and paste the prompt below into your chat. The prompt already instructs the model to provide its answer using Markdown formatting, so the output will be clean, structured, and easy to read—even in platforms that don’t support manual text formatting.

Why Markdown Formatting?You may notice the use of extra characters like hashtags (#), asterisks (*), and dashes (-) in the prompt below. That’s called Markdown, a simple way to format text clearly, especially helpful when the input or messaging fields (like those used with AI chatbots such as ChatGPT) don’t support formatting such as headings, bullets, or numbered lists.





Before running the prompt, modify any portions that don’t match your MLS search, such as area, dates, property types, etc.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## MLS Residential Real Estate Data Analysis Prompt

### Data Map (Complete before use)
– **Location**: [e.g. Franklin, TN]
– **Listing Statuses**: [e.g. Closed (Sold), Expired, Canceled]
– **Date Range**: [e.g. January 1, 2025 – July 13, 2025]

You are tasked with conducting an in-depth analysis of the provided MLS residential real estate data for site-built homes in **{{Location}}**. The dataset exclusively contains listings marked as **{{Listing Statuses}}**, from **{{Date Range}}**. Your analysis will be the foundation for insightful, impactful talking points in a podcast episode addressing current real estate market dynamics.

**Important:** You must not fabricate, amend, or append any data. Rely strictly on the provided MLS data to ensure the accuracy and integrity of your analysis.

Structure your analysis clearly and precisely, addressing the following key areas:

### 1. Pricing Trends
– Identify and describe the current pricing trends within the dataset. Are home prices in {{Location}} trending upward, downward, or stabilizing?
– Provide relevant statistical evidence and highlight any significant trends or changes compared to past periods.

### 2. Sold vs. Expired,  Canceled, or Withdrawn Listings
– Conduct a detailed comparative analysis of homes that successfully sold versus those that expired or were canceled.
– Provide price segmentation to identify price ranges with higher success rates (sold listings) versus those more prone to expiration or cancellation.
– Examine whether certain agents or real estate firms have disproportionately higher expiration or cancellation rates.
– Highlight specific neighborhoods or areas within {{Location}} that consistently experience higher or lower rates of expired or canceled listings.

### 3. Impact of Overpricing
– Assess the effect of initial overpricing on both days on market and final sale prices.
– Clearly quantify the relationship between listing prices set above market value and their impact on eventual sales outcomes.
– Evaluate whether overpricing ultimately benefits or negatively impacts sellers.

### 4. Market Sweet Spots
– Identify and describe market “sweet spots,” including specific home types, sizes, features, or neighborhoods currently outperforming or underperforming.
– Highlight segments demonstrating quicker sales, fewer cancellations or expirations, or achieving above-average sale prices.

Ensure the output of your analysis is factual, actionable, and well-organized, suitable for direct use as discussion points during the podcast. **Format the output in Markdown to ensure clear structure and readability when pasted into platforms that don’t support manual text formatting.**

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.

                                            Guides
                    
                    Glossary of AiM and AI Terms

                    
                        March 7, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This IsEvery tool, session, and resource inside Ai Marketing Academy (AiM) comes with its own vocabulary—and the broader world of artificial intelligence (AI) adds a lot more. This glossary covers the most important terms you’ll run into so the jargon doesn’t slow you down. It’s not meant to be read cover to cover. Bookmark it, come back when something comes up, and keep moving.



Terms Defined:




Generative AI (GenAI): AI that creates new content like text, images, or audio by analyzing patterns in its training data.



Model: The computational structure in AI that generates outputs, such as OpenAI’s DALL·E for images.



Training: The process of teaching AI patterns and relationships using large datasets, like books or images.



Inference: The process where AI uses its training to produce outputs or predictions from given input.



Prompt: A user-provided input or instruction that guides AI in generating a specific response.



Token: A segment of text, such as a word or subword, that AI processes during training or content generation.



Context Window: The range of text or data an AI model considers when generating a response or output. Larger context windows allow AI to reference more information simultaneously.



Grounded: Ensures AI responses are based on factual, accurate, or real-world information rather than solely predictive patterns.



LLM (Large Language Model): A specialized AI trained on extensive text data to generate and interpret language.



Multimodal: AI capable of understanding and generating multiple types of data, such as text, images, and audio.



Fine-Tune: Customizing a pre-trained AI model with specific data to enhance its performance for certain tasks.



Reasoning: AI models or methods designed to mimic logical thought processes, allowing the AI to make decisions based on structured analysis.



Non-Reasoning: AI models that primarily generate responses based on pattern recognition without explicit logical or analytical processes.



Hybrid: AI approaches or models that combine elements of both reasoning and non-reasoning methodologies to optimize performance.



Hallucinations: Instances when AI generates outputs that appear plausible but are factually incorrect or nonsensical.



API (Application Programming Interface): A set of protocols allowing software components or systems to communicate, crucial for integrating AI models into applications.



Deep Research: Multi-step research that autonomously searches the web, analyzes sources, and synthesizes a well-cited report.



Agentic: Describes AI systems capable of acting independently, performing complex tasks, and making decisions with minimal human oversight.

                                            Guides
                    
                    Prompting Best Practices for Reasoning VS. Non-Reasoning AI Models

                    
                        March 6, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


This guide helps you determine when and how to effectively prompt reasoning versus non-reasoning models to achieve better, clearer, and more accurate AI responses and outputs. 



Understanding AI Model Types



Not all AI models think/function the same way. Here’s a quick breakdown of the differences:



Reasoning ModelsThese models use what’s called “chain-of-thought” reasoning. They carefully break down your question step-by-step before giving an answer. Use them when you need clear logic, accurate details, or careful planning.



• Examples: GPT o1, GPT o3, Gemini 2.0 Flash Thinking



Non-Reasoning ModelsThese models respond quickly and intuitively but don’t think through the question first. Use them for casual chats, brainstorming, or simpler tasks.



• Examples: GPT-4o, GPT-4.5



Hybrid ModelsThese models can switch between intuitive and logical reasoning depending on your prompt. If you clearly ask for detailed steps, they’ll respond accordingly.



• Examples: Grok 3 (“Think” mode), Claude 3.5 Sonnet







Step-by-Step Instructions:


Step 1: Identify the AI Model Provider and Type




ChatGPT:

Reasoning Models: GPT o1,GPT o3



Non-Reasoning Models: GPT-4o, GPT-4.5o





Gemini:

Reasoning Models: Gemini 2.0 Flash Thinking



Non-Reasoning Models: Gemini 2.0 Flash





Grok:

Reasoning Models: Grok 3 (“Think” mode)



Non-Reasoning Models: Grok 3





Claude:

Reasoning Models: Claude 3.5 Sonnet (Extended), Claude 3.7 Sonnet (Extended)



Non-Reasoning Models: Claude 3.5 Haiku, Claude 3.5 Sonnet, Claude 3.7 Sonnet







What’s a context window, and why does it matter?A context window is how much text an AI model can consider at once—like its short-term memory. Bigger context windows help reasoning models handle complex tasks and lengthy instructions clearly. But remember, reasoning also depends on the model’s built-in ability to think step-by-step (“chain-of-thought” reasoning). A large context window helps, but it doesn’t guarantee strong reasoning on its own.




Step 2: Prompting Reasoning Models 



Reasoning models naturally approach your request systematically (like analytic thinkers). You don’t need to explicitly instruct them to explain each step because they already do that internally. They perform best when given clear, straightforward requests. Extra context or overly detailed instructions can confuse or distract them from their built-in logical approach.



How to prompt reasoning models clearly:




Be direct and specific—avoid unnecessary background or detail.



Clearly state exactly what information you want, including formatting details, because reasoning models follow explicit instructions closely.




Example Prompt:



List three medium-length hikes near San Francisco. Include:
- Trail name (exactly as listed on AllTrails)
- Start and end points
- Drive and hike durations
- Unique features or important warnings



Step 3: Prompting Non-Reasoning Models 



Non-reasoning models respond intuitively and quickly (like expressive thinkers). Without clear prompting, their responses can lack depth or structure. You must explicitly ask these models to provide reasoning or logic if that’s what you need, because they won’t naturally analyze the question deeply before answering.



How to prompt non-reasoning models clearly:




Explicitly ask the model to explain its logic or clearly show its thought process. For example, say “Explain your reasoning” or “Walk me through your steps.”



Clearly define the details or level of depth you’re looking for, because intuitive models won’t assume you want detailed answers unless specifically instructed.




Example Prompt:



Suggest three medium-length hikes near San Francisco. Briefly explain what's special about each hike.



Step 3: Prompting Hybrid Models



Hybrid models can think intuitively or analytically based on your instructions. They default to quick, intuitive answers, but they can shift into a detailed, reasoning approach when you clearly request it. Explicitly instructing these models to reason step-by-step engages their analytical side, ensuring deeper and more organized responses.



How to prompt hybrid models clearly:




Explicitly request step-by-step explanations or structured reasoning, clearly instructing the model to think analytically rather than intuitively.



Specify clearly if you want detailed logic, because hybrid models will default to quicker, less detailed responses if you don’t ask.




Example Prompt:




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Suggest three medium-length hikes near San Francisco. Explain step-by-step why each is uniquely worth visiting.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	







Related Topics:

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Write Like a Human

                    
                        February 24, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


A writing prompt inspired by Sam Altman, designed to help AI responses sound more like a real person wrote them. It strips out the robotic tone, removes hype, and keeps things direct and conversational—so your content feels natural, clear, and human.







How to use it


Copy and paste the full prompt into any large language model (like ChatGPT, Claude, Gemini, or Grok). You can adjust it to fit your style, but the default version works great for making AI sound less like a robot and more like a smart human who knows how to talk like one.



Use this prompt to help with emails, scripts, web copy—anything you want to sound more human and less “AI.”




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Use the following guidelines to write in a natural, conversational tone:

1. **Use simple, clear language:** Write plainly with short, direct sentences. 
   – Example: “I need help with this issue.”  

2. **Avoid “AI giveaway” phrases:** Skip clichés, robotic wording, or overly polished phrasing. 
   – Avoid: “Let’s dive into this game-changing solution.” 
   – Use instead: “Here’s how it works.”  

3. **Be direct and concise:** Get to the point without filler. 
   – Example: “We should meet tomorrow.”  

4. **Maintain a conversational tone:** Write like you talk. It’s fine to start sentences with “and” or “but.” 
   – Example: “And that’s why it matters.”  

5. **Avoid hype or marketing language:** Keep it real—no over-the-top claims. 
   – Avoid: “This revolutionary product will transform your life.” 
   – Use instead: “This product can help you.”  

6. **Be genuine and honest:** Don’t force a tone. Keep it natural. 
   – Example: “I don’t think that’s the best idea.”  

7. **Simplify grammar if necessary:** Perfect grammar isn’t always needed. Match the context. 
   – Example: “i guess we can try that.”  

8. **Cut the fluff:** Remove unnecessary adjectives, adverbs, or over-explaining. 
   – Example: “We finished the task.”  

9. **Prioritize clarity:** Ensure the message is easy to understand and leaves no room for confusion. 
   – Example: “Please send the file by Monday.”

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.






Related Topics:

                                            Guides
                    
                    10 Formatting Tips for Better Prompting

                    
                        February 24, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


Introduction


The way you format your prompts when communicating with advanced AI language models like ChatGPT, Claude, Grok, or Gemini significantly impacts the quality of responses you receive. Much like effective human communication, well-structured prompts help AI systems better understand your intentions and generate more relevant, useful outputs.



This guide presents ten proven formatting techniques to enhance your AI interactions and get more precise, helpful responses.



1. Use Line Breaks for Clarity



Breaking your requests into separate lines helps the AI process each instruction individually rather than as a dense paragraph.



Instead of writing:



"Please write social media captions for my new luxury property listing, suggest email subject lines I could use when sending it to my client database, and draft a property description for the MLS listing."



Try formatting it as:



"Please help with the following for my new luxury property listing:

Write 3 engaging social media captions I can use with listing photos.

Suggest 5 email subject lines to capture attention in my client newsletter.

Draft a compelling property description for the MLS listing."



When you place each request on its own line, the AI can focus on one task at a time, producing better quality content for each marketing need.



2. Use Bullet Points or Numbered Lists



When your prompt contains a series of items, criteria, or questions, formatting them as a clearly delineated list helps the AI identify and address each point separately.



For unordered collections, use bullet points (- or *):



Please brainstorm content ideas for my real estate newsletter:
- Market update for the spring season
- Home staging tips for sellers
- Current mortgage rate information
- Local neighborhood spotlight



For sequential items, use numbers:



Help me create a follow-up sequence for potential buyers:
1. Write an initial email after the first showing
2. Draft a text message to send 2 days later
3. Create a personalized note about neighborhood amenities
4. Develop a 30-day check-in message



This approach ensures you get complete responses addressing each specific marketing need you’ve outlined.



3. Wrap Example Inputs in Quotes or Code Blocks



When including sample text for the AI to analyze, rewrite, or use as inspiration, set it apart from your instructions using quotation marks or code blocks.



Using quotation marks:



"Rewrite this property headline to be more engaging: 'Beautiful 3BR/2BA home in desirable neighborhood'"



Using code blocks with triple backticks:



When you type three backticks, then add your text, then close with three more backticks, it creates a code block like this:



Here's my current agent bio that needs improvement:

Jane Smith has been a real estate agent for 15 years. She knows the local market well and has helped many clients buy and sell homes. Jane lives in Oakwood with her family and enjoys cooking and hiking.



This visual separation clearly distinguishes between your instructions and the content you want the AI to work with, resulting in more targeted improvements to your marketing copy.



4. Use Markdown for Structure



Most AI platforms support Markdown, a simple formatting system that adds visual hierarchy and emphasis to plain text.



Headers and subheaders (use # symbols):



# Quarterly Market Report Email

## Current Market Trends
Key statistics about home prices in our region...

## Buyer Opportunities
Tips for buyers in the current market...

## Seller Strategies
Best practices for preparing homes for sale...



Text formatting:




Bold text (use **bold text**)



Italic text (use *italic text*)



Special terms (use backticks `term`)




These formatting elements help organize complex prompts when planning comprehensive marketing campaigns or detailed client presentations.



5. Separate Multi-Step Requests



For prompts that contain multiple questions or tasks, use double line breaks to visually separate each component:



I need help creating marketing materials for a new luxury listing. 

Can you draft social media copy that highlights the property's custom kitchen and resort-style pool?

What would be an effective headline for the property brochure that emphasizes its exclusive location?

How should I describe the neighborhood amenities in my email campaign to potential buyers?



This approach makes your request easier to follow and allows the AI to address each marketing element thoroughly.



6. Keep Each Instruction on Its Own Line



Placing individual instructions on separate lines improves clarity and comprehension:



Instead of:



"Write a property description for my new listing highlighting the renovated kitchen, mention the hardwood floors, talk about the large backyard, and emphasize the great school district."



Try:



"Please write a property description for my new listing.
Highlight the recently renovated kitchen with quartz countertops.
Mention the original hardwood floors throughout the main level.
Describe the spacious fenced backyard with mature landscaping.
Emphasize the property's location in the award-winning Lincoln school district."



This vertical organization ensures all key selling points are incorporated into your property descriptions and marketing materials.



7. Use Delimiters for Sections



For longer, complex prompts, use visual delimiters like dashes, equals signs, or symbols to create clearly labeled sections:



=== PROPERTY DETAILS ===
4BR/3BA Colonial in Lakewood Heights
2,400 sq ft on 0.5 acre lot
Built in 2005, renovated in 2022
Asking price: $575,000

--- TARGET AUDIENCE ---
* First-time luxury buyers
* Growing families looking for more space
* Professionals who work from home

+++ MARKETING REQUESTS +++
What headline would capture attention on social media?
How should we highlight the home office space for remote workers?
What unique selling points should be emphasized in the property flyer?



These visual dividers help organize related information and create a clear structure for the AI to follow when creating your marketing strategy.



8. SpecifyDesired Formats or Templates



Clearly indicate the format you want for the AI’s response:



Please create a monthly content calendar for my real estate social media using this template:

WEEK 1:
Monday: [Topic]
Wednesday: [Topic]
Friday: [Topic]

WEEK 2:
Monday: [Topic]
Wednesday: [Topic]
Friday: [Topic]

Focus on spring home selling tips, local market updates, and buyer financing options.



Providing a specific structure ensures your social media or email content will be formatted exactly as you need it for your marketing platforms.



9. Provide Context Before Questions



Share relevant background information before stating your specific requests:



I'm a real estate agent specializing in luxury waterfront properties in the Naples area. My typical clients are retirees or vacation home buyers looking for exclusive amenities and views.

What key selling points should I emphasize in my marketing materials to appeal to this demographic? How can I structure my property descriptions to highlight the lifestyle benefits of these homes?



Giving context first helps the AI understand your target market and provide more relevant, tailored marketing advice for your specific niche.



10. Use Explicit Role Instructions



Define the perspective or expertise you want the AI to adopt:



As an experienced real estate copywriter, please review this draft of my Just Listed postcard and suggest specific improvements:

[Your postcard copy here]



This technique helps frame the AI’s response through the lens of real estate marketing expertise, providing you with professional-quality suggestions and improvements.







Conclusion


These ten formatting techniques will help you craft clearer prompts that elicit more precise, useful responses from AI language models. The extra few moments spent structuring your requests can significantly improve the quality of the AI’s output for your marketing materials, saving you time and enhancing your communications.



Remember that effective prompt engineering is both an art and a science—experiment with these techniques

                                            Bots
                    
                    Personalized Video Script Generator

                    
                        February 13, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This resource provides step-by-step instructions for creating a custom GPT that generates engaging and authentic video scripts for Instagram Reels. This is not a GPT you can use directly—instead, it guides you in setting up your own GPT inside ChatGPT.




For a step-by-step walkthrough on creating a custom GPT, visit:➡️ How to Create a ChatGPT Custom GPT




This GPT will be tailored for real estate agents specializing in residential properties in a specified location. It ensures scripts match the agent’s unique voice, style, and tone, making content feel personal and natural.



Before you start: To ensure this GPT mirrors your unique voice, style, and tone, you’ll need to upload a document containing writing samples to the Knowledge section of your custom GPT. These samples should reflect how you naturally communicate in your social media content.




👉Tip: If you don’t have pre-written samples, you can use a tool like Rev.com for a low-cost, AI-transcription service to convert your spoken content into text.








How to Use It


1. Provide a Clear Topic and Relevant Data



Each script is generated based on a specific topic or focus that you provide. Additionally, include any relevant or necessary data that should be incorporated into the script.



Example topics you can request:




“A market update on home prices in my area”



“A property tour for a new listing”



“Common mistakes homebuyers make”





Important: This GPT does not create topics on its own—it strictly follows your request.




2. Specify Any Key Details




If you have specific numbers, market data, or key details, include them in your request so the script remains accurate and aligned with your needs.



If you want a particular tone (e.g., humorous, direct, educational), let the GPT know!




3. Get a Ready-to-Use Script



Your script will:




Be between 130–160 words to fit a 60-second video.



Start with an engaging hook (question, bold statement, or surprising fact).
Flow naturally, avoiding complex phrasing or robotic wording.



End with a subtle call to action (e.g., “DM me for details!”).



Be formatted ready to paste into a teleprompter—no extra editing needed.




What makes this GPT Unique?



✅ Authenticity: It mirrors your natural voice, tone, and speaking style.✅ Flexibility: Adaptable to different tones and styles upon request. ✅ Accuracy: Instructed not to make up or alter provided data. ✅ Engagement-Driven: Uses proven techniques to keep viewers hooked.



Custom GPT Instructions: The instructions below are written in Markdown, a simple text format that ensures clarity since the Custom GPT setup doesn’t support rich text formatting. You can copy and paste them directly into your Custom GPT’s instructions section.



🔹 Be Specific: The more details you provide, the better the script will match your vision.🔹 Test Different Hooks: Ask for variations to find the most engaging opener.🔹 Keep It Conversational: This GPT excels at informal, engaging scripts—perfect for social media.



This guide helps you set up a powerful tool to make your content creation easier, faster, and more effective. Ready to create your own GPT? 🚀




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

# Objective  
Generate engaging and authentic video scripts for Instagram Reels (up to 60 seconds) tailored for a real estate agent specializing in **residential properties in the location specified by the user**.  

The scripts must **adhere very closely** to the agent’s unique voice, style, tone, and diction, as demonstrated in the sample scripts uploaded in the knowledge section of the GPT.  

During each chat, the user provides the specific **topic or focus** for the video. While the GPT has background knowledge of real estate (e.g., market trends, property features, common buyer/seller concerns), it **must always follow the user’s chosen direction**. The real estate knowledge outlined below is only to **inform context**—the script should not introduce topics beyond what the user requests.  

> **If the user provides specific market data or figures, the GPT must never modify, add to, or fabricate that information.**  

# Instructions  

## Voice, Style, and Tone  
Analyze the sample scripts uploaded in the knowledge section to **match the agent’s unique voice, style, tone, and diction as closely as possible**. All generated scripts must reflect this style consistently, balancing professionalism with approachability.  

Write in a **conversational tone that mirrors the agent’s speaking habits**, using language that is friendly, knowledgeable, and engaging. **Strictly avoid** generic, AI-like phrasing or overly formal language. The tone should feel natural for social media consumption.  

> **Important:** The GPT should default to following the provided writing style and approach. However, if the user explicitly requests a different style (e.g., stronger CTAs, a humorous tone, etc.), adapt accordingly. The user's input always takes priority.  

## Script Length and Pacing  
Each script should be between **130 and 160 words** to suit the average speaking pace for a 60-second video.  

- Ensure the script **flows naturally**, with room for pauses where key points are emphasized.  
- Avoid overly complex phrasing or long sentences, as they could disrupt pacing.  
- **When presenting numbers or data**, space them out for readability.  

**Example of well-paced numbers:**  
> *"Last year, the local real estate market jumped by 5.2% in overall home price appreciation."*  

Avoid overwhelming the listener with too many figures at once—give them time to mentally process before introducing another number.  

## Opening Hook  
Begin each script with an **engaging hook** that directly relates to the topic provided by the user. Effective hooks include:  
- **Intriguing questions** → *“Ever wondered what $700K can get you in Capitol Hill?”*  
- **Bold statements** → *“Most buyers miss out on the best deals because of THIS one mistake.”*  
- **Surprising facts** → *“Home prices just did something unexpected—let’s talk about it.”*  

The hook should immediately grab attention and encourage viewers to continue watching.  

## Content Structure and Subject Matter Expertise  
Structure each script with a **clear beginning (hook), middle (body), and end (conclusion).**  
- The **middle section** should expand on the user’s specific topic in an engaging, informative manner.  
- Draw on real estate knowledge **when relevant**, but ensure the focus remains on the user’s topic. For example:  
  - If the topic is a **property tour**, highlight notable features **without fabricating or speculating**.  
  - If the topic is **market data**, present the numbers in a digestible format **without adding or changing any figures**.  
- **End with a strong payoff**, such as a valuable insight or a subtle call to action.  

## Handling Market Data Responsibly  
- If the user **provides specific market data**, the GPT **must use it exactly as given**—no modifying, extrapolating, or making assumptions.  
- If the user does **not** provide specific data, the script should **not introduce** statistics or figures.  
- When referencing **multiple numbers**, space them out for clarity. Avoid rapid sequences of percentages, dollar amounts, or timeframes.  

## Engagement and Viewer Retention  
- Use **second-person language** (*“you”*) to directly address viewers and foster a personal connection.  
- Occasionally use inclusive pronouns like *“we”* and *“our”* to build community.  
- Keep the audience engaged with **micro-hooks**—subtle hints at upcoming content.  

**Example of a micro-hook:**  
> *“Next, I’ll reveal something that most buyers overlook in this neighborhood—stay tuned!”*  
These techniques help sustain viewer interest and improve retention.  

## Calls to Action (CTAs)  
Each script should conclude with a **subtle, natural CTA** that aligns with the user’s goals. Examples include:  
- *“DM me to learn more about this property.”*  
- *“Thinking of selling your home? Let’s talk.”*  

> **CTAs should not be aggressive or overly sales-driven.** They must feel like a natural extension of the s

                                            Guides
                    
                    How to Create a ChatGPT Custom GPT

                    
                        February 13, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


How to Create a Custom GPT



Log in to ChatGPT

Access the platform via the web (not the app).





Tap Your Profile Icon

Click on your profile image in the top right corner of the screen.





Go to “My GPTs”

From the dropdown menu, click “My GPTs.”





Create a New GPT

Click “Create a GPT.” You’ll be given two options: Create or Configure.



Create: This lets you chat with the GPT like a normal conversation, and it will summarize the key takeaways to form instructions. Note that this method may miss details.



Configure: This is the recommended approach for better control. It allows you to manually set all instructions and behaviors.





Fill in the Fields

Name & Description: Provide a unique name and a concise description of your GPT.



Icon/Favicon: Upload an image or use DALL-E to create one.



Knowledge Upload: You can upload documents, spreadsheets, or other files to provide your GPT with context or information.



Pro Tips: Clearly instruct your GPT on how to use this uploaded knowledge in its responses.

Instructions Section: Use the guidance from your lectures and labs to craft detailed instructions for your GPT’s behavior and how it should handle different types of queries.



Conversation Starters: Set up prompts that users can use to start a conversation. Reference these in your instructions to tailor the GPT’s responses effectively.







Tap “Create” & Save Your GPT

Once you’re finished, tap “Create” in the top right corner. You can then choose whether to save your custom GPT privately or make it publicly available.








From the Session: This guide was introduced in Personalize Your ChatGPT.

                                            Prompts
                    
                    HTML Market Update Email Newsletter

                    
                        February 6, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What this is:


This resource helps you create a professionally designed, insight-rich real estate market update email—automatically. Using Claude’s Artifact feature (or a similar tool), it transforms MLS data you export into a spreadsheet into a polished HTML email that tells the story of your local market.



The prompt doesn’t just format content—it analyzes your MLS data, identifies noteworthy trends, and wraps everything in a layout that’s ready to send to homeowners. It’s perfect for database nurturing, listing lead follow-up, or any moment when a smart market update could spark a conversation.







How To Use It



Review the full prompt below so you understand its key components—personalized greeting, market insight, charts, offline viewing, and PDF support.



Customize the prompt with your local market. Change any references to location (e.g., Franklin, Tennessee) to reflect your target area. Update the date range mentioned in the intro to match your dataset.



Prepare your MLS data in a spreadsheet. You’ll need Closed (sold), Expired, and Withdrawn listings. Label them clearly and define the time period you’re covering in your data. Otherwise, adjust the prompt if you alter your MLS search.



Upload the spreadsheet to Claude when you run the prompt. Attach the spreadsheet directly in Claude and paste in your customized prompt.



Generate the Artifact and review the output. Claude will generate a complete HTML email based on your MLS data. If you want to include your branding (logo, fonts, or colors), just let Claude know in a follow-up prompt and upload a simple brand kit file. You can also ask for layout or content changes, or make manual edits directly in the HTML.



Make any final edits. Ask Claude to make tweaks if you need to adjust layout, style, branding, or tone. You can also edit the HTML manually if needed.



Send it. Copy the final HTML from Claude and paste it into the “Code your own” section of your email service provider (like Mailchimp, Constant Contact, or KVCore). This gives you full control over formatting and ensures the design displays properly in inboxes.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

Assume the role of a masterful graphic artist and expert in interactive infographic design. Your task is to create an HTML email newsletter based exclusively on the data in the attached spreadsheet. Do not alter, fabricate, or infer any information beyond what is provided. The spreadsheet contains a list of homes in Franklin, Tennessee, categorized by Closed (sold), Expired (unsold during the listing period), and Withdrawn (removed from the market by the seller). This email newsletter will serve as a Real Estate Market Update, presenting key trends through expertly designed charts, graphs, and interactive visual elements to inform and engage homeowners. Use the date range in the data to generate a relevant title that accurately reflects the time period covered.

• • •

**REQUIREMENTS:**
*All instructions listed below must be followed:*

• • •

**Personalized Greeting:**  
– Personalize the greeting by addressing the recipient by their first name if available. If no name is present, default to a friendly salutation like “Friend” or “Homeowner.” Format it according to standard email merge tag syntax.

**Compelling Market Insight:**  
– Analyze the data to identify one specific and compelling insight that would resonate with homeowners considering selling their property.  
– Write a three- to four-sentence paragraph summarizing this key market trend, highlighting a data point that would make a homeowner stop and think about selling.  
– Ensure the language is persuasive yet factual, without exaggeration.

**Data Visualization:**  
– Develop interactive charts and graphs that help homeowners visualize key trends and performance metrics year-to-date.  
– Use only the spreadsheet data—do not add or assume any missing information.

**Offline Functionality:**  
– Ensure the entire infographic, including all charts, graphs, and images, is fully viewable and functional in any web browser without an internet connection.

**Expert Design:**  
– Apply advanced graphic design principles to create a visually appealing, easy-to-read, and engaging layout.  
– Add section headers and concise explanatory text where appropriate to guide the reader through the data.

**PDF Compatibility:**  
– Include a “View Full Report & Save as PDF” button that opens the infographic in a web browser, where it is properly formatted for 8.5×11 inch paper (portrait orientation) and includes a built-in “Save to PDF” option for easy downloading.  
– Ensure charts and graphs do not get split across pages—they should be properly formatted to start on a new page if needed.  
– Maintain clean margins and proper spacing to avoid content cutting off at the edges.

**Coding Standards:**  
– Write clean, structured HTML, CSS, and JavaScript that follows best practices for email design.  
– Ensure cross-device and cross-email client compatibility.

**Data Integrity:**  
– Use exclusively the data provided in the spreadsheet.  
– Do not generate, infer, or hallucinate additional information.

By following these instructions, you’ll create a highly effective real estate market update email that engages homeowners, provides valuable data-driven insights, and encourages potential sellers to reach out.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	






DISCLAIMER: This resource provides prompts, instructions, and content to help professionals use AI tools more effectively. Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.
