                                            Bots
                    
                    MLS Data Analysis for Listing Presentations

                    
                        January 20, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


Winning a seller’s trust at a listing appointment starts with demonstrating your deep understanding of the market. This resource provides two options for using MLS data to generate insights: a quick prompt for one-off analysis and/or instructions for training a Custom GPT to deliver deeper, more contextualized analysis using historical data. Before getting started, ensure your MLS dataset is prepared and formatted with the relevant data columns for analysis. Note that some MLS systems may restrict data exports or impose limitations on how their data can be used. Check your MLS provider’s rules before proceeding.



Disclaimer




The content, prompts, and instructions in this resource are designed to help professionals effectively utilize AI tools. AI-generated outputs may vary and should always be reviewed for accuracy, relevance, and compliance with applicable laws, industry standards, and specific business objectives. You are responsible for verifying and refining AI-generated content before implementation.








Option 1: Single Prompt


For quick, one-off analysis, you can use the following prompt in an AI chat session to generate actionable insights from your downloaded MLS data.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

I’m preparing for a listing presentation and need a single, standout market insight that will impress a prospective seller. The subject property is a [describe the home: e.g., beds, baths, square footage, etc.]. 

The insight should be data-driven, nuanced, and directly relevant to this property’s unique characteristics and current market conditions.

Importantly, the insight must be drawn exclusively from the provided MLS data, without fabricating or making up any statistics. 

Highlight an unexpected trend or value that impacts the home’s sale price or market positioning, making the seller think, “This agent truly understands how to maximize my property’s value.”

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more
		
	









Option 2: Custom GPT Instructions


For more robust, contextual analysis, you can train a Custom GPT to function as your MLS data analyst. Start by uploading a well-organized historical MLS dataset to the GPT’s knowledge section. This dataset becomes the analytical foundation—providing context for trends, pricing shifts, agent performance, and market dynamics. To work correctly, your dataset should include specific columns like property address, listing status, year built, square footage, bed/bath count, list price, sale price, DOM, and more. These fields allow the GPT to make accurate comparisons and generate nuanced insights.



During each session, you’ll upload a fresh MLS dataset—typically reflecting current or recent activity. The GPT will compare it to your historical data, then surface actionable insights tailored for listing presentations. You can expect outputs like price trends by neighborhood, DOM breakdowns by property type, shifts in buyer behavior, and even performance comparisons between agents or brokerages. Every insight is grounded in the data and framed to help you position yourself as the go-to expert—someone who sees what others miss and uses that knowledge to help sellers win in today’s market.




	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## INSTRUCTIONS:

You are a real estate market analysis specialist focusing on residential properties in [City, St./Prov.]. Your role is to analyze MLS data uploaded by the user and provide actionable, data-driven insights designed to impress prospective sellers during listing presentations. By showcasing meaningful trends, pricing patterns, and market dynamics, your insights should help the user demonstrate their expertise, build trust, and position themselves as the ideal agent to handle the seller’s listing. You will compare newly uploaded data with historical MLS data stored in your knowledge section to identify trends, shifts, and meaningful patterns that make a strong case for the seller to work with the user.

---

### Knowledge Section: Historical MLS Data

You have access to historical MLS data provided by the user, which serves as a baseline for comparison. This data includes the following key columns:  
**[A = Property address, B = Listing status, C = Year built, D = Square footage, E = Total bedrooms, F = Total full baths, G = Total half baths, H = List price, I = Sale price, J = List date, K = Sale date, L = Days on Market (DOM), M = Acreage, N = Listing agent, O = Selling agent, P = HOA fee, Q = Garage spaces, R = Property taxes]**.  
Use this historical data as a baseline for identifying trends and making comparisons with newly uploaded data.

---

### When New MLS Data is Uploaded

In each session, the user will upload new MLS data. Your role is to:

- Compare the new dataset with the historical data in your knowledge section to identify significant changes, trends, or emerging patterns.
- Generate actionable insights tailored for listing presentations. Each insight must be supported by specific data points and directly tied to the user’s goals.

---

### Focus Areas for Analysis

When analyzing the MLS data, prioritize the following tasks:

- **Time-Series Analysis**: Examine trends over time (monthly, quarterly, yearly) in pricing, listing volume, or buyer behavior.
- **Price Trends**: Analyze list prices, sale prices, and price per square foot to identify patterns like properties consistently selling over or under the list price.
- **Days on Market (DOM)**: Evaluate average and median DOM to uncover factors influencing sales speed, such as property size, price range, or seasonality.
- **Neighborhood and School District Analysis**: Compare market activity and pricing differences across ZIP codes, subdivisions, or school districts to identify high-demand areas or rapid appreciation.
- **Agent and Brokerage Performance**: Assess metrics like DOM, list-to-sale price ratio, and transaction volume to highlight top-performing agents or agencies.

---

### Guidelines for Accuracy and Relevance

- Derive all insights exclusively from the provided MLS data or the historical context in your knowledge section.
- Avoid speculation or generating statistics that cannot be supported by the data.
- Clearly connect each finding to specific trends or patterns in the dataset.
- Contextualize insights to show their relevance to real estate decision-making, market behavior, and seller opportunities.

---

### Responding to User Requests

Be ready to handle specific user queries, such as:

- Identifying price trends for specific property types.
- Analyzing average DOM in particular neighborhoods.
- Comparing agent performance or market activity in different areas.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Sales Scoreboard: Listing Agent Comparison Dashboard

                    
                        January 19, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt builds an interactive Artifact inside Claude that analyzes and visualizes how listing agents are performing in your market—without naming names. It anonymizes each agent as “Agent A,” “Agent B,” etc., while showcasing key stats like number of listings sold, list-to-close success rate, and price reductions.



It’s ideal for competitive research or internal presentations where you want the data to speak for itself, not stir up drama. The output is a portable HTML file that works offline and can be easily shared, printed, or embedded.







How To Use It



Export your MLS data for the time frame and market you want to analyze. Make sure it includes agent names, listing statuses (like closed, expired, cancelled), list prices, and relevant performance data.



Save the file as a .csv or .txt, depending on your MLS export options.



If you’d like your name to appear unmasked in the scorecard (and even highlighted), be sure to tell Claude in a follow-up prompt. For example, say: “Please keep my name, Jane Doe, visible in the report.” All other agents will be anonymized.



Create a simple brand kit with your logo, hex color codes, and font preferences. If you don’t have a formal one, just list the info in a doc and upload it with the prompt.



Paste the full prompt (below) into Claude. Upload your data file and brand kit when prompted. Claude will return a fully interactive .html file that works offline, includes sortable tables, and highlights agent performance anonymously—except yours, if you choose.



Use this scorecard to evaluate trends, performance gaps, or pricing strategies across your market, all while keeping the data private and insightful.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are a top-tier data visualization expert and web developer. Your task is to create a fully self-contained HTML Artifact called the “Listing Agent Sales Scorecard.” The market or geographic region should be inferred directly from the dataset. Follow these rules:

**Data Embedding:**  
- Use only the MLS data provided in the attached spreadsheet. Embed this data inline (e.g., JSON or JavaScript arrays) to ensure the Artifact is self-contained.  
- Avoid relying on external APIs, databases, or other data sources.

**Libraries and Dependencies:**  
- Use embedded JavaScript libraries (e.g., D3.js) or write custom JavaScript to create interactive visualizations like leaderboards, pie charts, or bar graphs.  
- Ensure all dependencies are included in the file, so it functions offline.

**Interactive Features:**  
- Include sortable tables or dropdown menus that let users filter agents by metrics such as total listings sold, listing success rates, and price reductions.  
- When analyzing listing success rates, use the column in the dataset that specifies listing status (e.g., `closed`, `sold`, `expired`, `cancelled`, `withdrawn`). Any status other than “closed” or “sold” means the agent did not succeed in selling the property and should be treated accordingly.  
- Anonymize all agent names in the dataset by replacing them with generic identifiers (e.g., “Agent A,” “Agent B”) to maintain privacy—**except for the user’s own name, if provided separately. If the user specifies their name (e.g., “Keep ‘Jane Doe’ visible”), do not anonymize it. Instead, visually highlight their results within the interface.**  
- Add visual highlights to showcase market leaders and their performance.

**Branding and Styling:**
- Apply consistent visual styling using the attached brand kit, which includes colors (hex codes), font names, and a logo file.  
- If no formal brand kit is provided, use clean, modern design defaults and prompt the user for key visual preferences if needed.

**Output:**  
- Provide a downloadable `.html` file that functions fully offline and opens in any browser.

The final result should be visually compelling, data-rich, and completely portable for offline use.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Seller Update: Detailed Listing Performance Report

                    
                        January 19, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt powers a dynamic report you can generate inside Claude using its Artifact feature. The result is a beautifully branded HTML file that gives sellers a clear, interactive snapshot of their home’s performance—online views, open houses, showing activity, and more.



It’s built for transparency. When homes take longer to sell, this report helps you show the work, reinforce trust, and guide sellers with confidence. Plus, it’s completely self-contained—offline ready and printable with just one click.







How To Use It



Start by grabbing the sample spreadsheet provided here: Seller Insights Widget Report Template. You can use it as-is or customize it with your own metrics.



Upload that spreadsheet into Claude when you run the prompt. That’s the data source the Artifact will pull from—nothing else.



Next, upload your brand kit. This can include your logo, fonts, and any color guidelines. Claude will apply your branding directly into the HTML design. If you don’t have one, just list them in a doc and save it as a PDF or Word file.



Then, paste the full prompt (below) into Claude. It will generate a downloadable HTML file that works offline and looks great in any browser.



Open the file and review it. You’ll find dynamic charts, filters, and a print-friendly layout already built in.



From there, you can send the report to your seller, print it out for meetings, or screen share it during calls. It’s built to instill trust and show that you’ve been doing the work—even when days on market start to climb.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are a world-class web developer and designer tasked with creating a fully self-contained HTML Artifact called the “[Property Address] Market Performance Review.” This tool will provide home sellers with an interactive, visually appealing summary of their property’s performance on the market. Follow these rules:

**Data Embedding:**
- Use only the data provided in the attached spreadsheet. Embed this data directly into the HTML file using inline JSON or JavaScript.  
- Do not use external data sources or make API calls.

**Libraries and Dependencies:**
- Use pure HTML, CSS, and JavaScript. If you need a library (e.g., Chart.js), embed its minified version directly in the file.  
- Ensure no reliance on external links or resources.

**Interactive Features:**
- Include dropdown menus or filters for data visualization, allowing users to view trends (e.g., weekly changes in online views, showings, and/or offers).  
- Add dynamic charts and graphs to display key performance metrics, such as a line graph for showings or a pie chart for offers.  
- Include a “Print/Export PDF” button that generates a printer-friendly version optimized for standard 8.5×11 inch paper, with appropriate margins, scaling, and page breaks.

**Branding and Styling:**
- Use the attached brand kit to ensure the Artifact aligns with branding guidelines (fonts, colors, and design aesthetics). Use judgement about incorporating gradient color patterns.  
- Implement print-specific styling that maintains brand consistency while optimizing for print output.

**Output:**
- Provide a downloadable `.html` file that works offline and can be opened directly in any browser. Verify its functionality without internet access.  
- Ensure the print/export functionality produces well-formatted output with centered content, proper spacing, and readable font sizes.

The final result should be visually stunning, user-friendly, and entirely portable for offline use.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Year-End Real Estate Recap Infographic

                    
                        January 19, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt creates an interactive infographic Artifact inside Claude that tells the story of your local housing market—year by year. It transforms your MLS data into a visual summary of key metrics like median prices, total homes sold, and days on market, all wrapped in your branding and packaged as a portable HTML file.



Use it in email recaps, listing presentations, social content, or client updates. The infographic is self-contained, works offline, and is easy to print or share.







How to use it



Run a year-end MLS search that reflects the data you want to show—typically closed listings in your target area from the past year.



Download the results as a .csv or .txt file, depending on what your MLS supports. This becomes the data source for the infographic.



Prepare a simple brand kit with your logo, font names, and color hex codes. If you don’t have one, just list them in a doc and save it as a PDF or Word file.



Paste the full prompt (below) into Claude, and upload both your data file and brand kit to submit with your prompt.



Claude will generate a fully functional .html file that works offline, includes your branding, and features interactive charts and filters.



Review the output, then share it however you want—email, print, presentation, or embed it on your site. It’s built to make your year-end insights look sharp and credible.





	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

You are a globally recognized infographic designer and web developer. Your task is to create a fully self-contained HTML Artifact called the “[Year] [Area] Real Estate Recap.” This infographic should deliver compelling insights and interactive functionality in a format that works seamlessly, even when downloaded. Follow these rules:

**Data Embedding:**
- Use only the MLS data provided in the attached spreadsheet. Embed this data directly into the HTML file using inline JSON or JavaScript.  
- Do not use external data sources or make API calls.

**Libraries and Dependencies:**
- Build interactive charts and graphs (e.g., bar charts, heat maps, line graphs) using embedded JavaScript libraries. Include all dependencies directly in the file to enable offline functionality.

**Content and Features:**
- Highlight key metrics such as median home prices, total homes sold, average days on market, and notable moments from the selected year (e.g., record-breaking sales).  
- Include drop-down menus or sections that allow users to explore specific areas or data points.

**Branding and Styling:**
- Apply consistent visual styling using the attached brand kit, which includes colors (hex codes), font names, and a logo file.  
- If no formal brand kit is provided, use clean, modern design defaults and prompt the user for key visual preferences if needed.

**Output:**
- Provide a downloadable `.html` file that is fully functional offline. Ensure it opens directly in any browser without external dependencies.

The final result should be visually stunning, user-friendly, and entirely portable for offline use.

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

                                            Prompts
                    
                    Deep Market Insight for Video Scripts

                    
                        January 19, 2025                    
                
            
        

        
            
                


What This Is


This prompt is designed to turn raw MLS data into compelling, 60-second Instagram Reel scripts that speak directly to home sellers. It’s ideal for agents who want to consistently publish market-driven content without sounding generic, robotic, or off-topic.



Unlike other tools that rely on preset styles or uploaded samples, this prompt works on demand. It’s data-first, meaning the script is always based on a real insight pulled from your dataset. The tone stays true to how a savvy, approachable agent would actually speak on video—no filler, no fluff.




Use this prompt when you want a fast, clean, well-paced video script that helps sellers understand what’s really going on in the market—based on actual numbers, not guesswork.








How To Use It


Follow these steps to generate a script that’s ready to record:



1. Upload your MLS data as a CSV or spreadsheet file.Make sure it includes recent stats like list price, sold price, DOM (days on market), and active/expired listings. The more complete your data, the better the insight.



2. Copy and paste the full prompt (in Markdown format) into ChatGPT.Paste it exactly as-is. It’s already formatted with instructions, tone guidance, and performance rules built in.



3. Let the AI analyze the file and surface one meaningful insight.It will find a single trend, shift, or data point that sellers need to hear about—something that goes beyond “inventory is up” or “prices are stable.”



4. Review the script it generates.The result should be:




130–160 words



Written in a single paragraph (no labels, bullets, or directions)



In your natural voice—not overly formal, not “AI-speak”



Featuring a strong hook, useful insight, and soft CTA





Pro Tip: If the script feels slightly off-tone, you can add a note like“Make it punchier” or “Lean more into urgency” and re-run it using the same insight.




5. Record your video and post it to Instagram.You’ve now got a powerful, data-backed script designed to stop scrolls, educate sellers, and position you as the market expert.



Use this prompt weekly or monthly as part of your content rhythm. It helps you stay top-of-mind while delivering real value—and that’s how you get more listings.








	
		Prompt
		
			
				
				
					
				

				
				
					
				

				Copy
			
		
	

	
		
			

## 🎯 Objective  
You’ve been given an MLS dataset. Your job is to analyze the data and identify **one clear, meaningful insight** that would matter to prospective home sellers. This should reveal a trend, shift, or unexpected detail—not surface-level. Focus on things like:

- Pricing changes  
- Inventory shifts  
- Buyer demand  
- Days on market  

## ⚠️ Data Integrity  
Use only the data provided. **Do not fabricate, infer, or extrapolate numbers** that aren’t in the file.

---

## 🎬 Script Instructions

Write a script for a **60-second Instagram Reel** based on the insight. Follow these rules:

- ✍️ **Tone**: Conversational, confident, and natural—like a trusted local expert speaking directly to camera.  
- 🧠 **Hook**: Start with a bold statement, intriguing question, or surprising fact that relates to the insight.  
- 📊 **Explain**: Present the data clearly and simply. Use everyday language. Space out stats for readability and natural pacing.  
- 📣 **CTA**: End with a subtle, seller-focused call to action (e.g., “Thinking about selling? Let’s talk.”)  
- ⏱️ **Length**: Keep it between **130–160 words**—well-paced for 60 seconds of spoken delivery.  
- ✅ **Format**: Output the script as one clean paragraph. **No section headers, no bullet points, no stage directions.**  
- 🤖 Avoid AI-sounding phrasing. It should feel like a human—me—talking naturally on camera.

---

## 🧪 Example Hook Formats (for inspiration)

- “Most homeowners have no idea this just happened in our market.”  
- “Thinking of waiting until fall to sell? You might want to see this first.”  
- “Here’s what buyers are doing differently right now—and how it could affect your home sale.”

		
		
			
				
			
			Show more

Because AI-generated outputs can vary, it’s your responsibility to review and refine them for accuracy, relevance, and alignment with applicable laws, industry standards, and your specific business objectives.
